# BlackOut Trades — Audit Findings (living doc)

Verified issues from the production data-correctness audit. Newest/most-severe first.
Cross-provider ground truth: Polygon + Unusual Whales REST. Started 2026-07-01.

**Merge policy for this doc's PRs:** left OPEN for end-of-day review — do not merge without explicit go-ahead, even when CI is green. **Superseded 2026-07-03 by explicit user standing instruction to run fully autonomously (branch→fix→test→PR→CI→merge→live-verify, repeat) through Monday 2026-07-06 market open — this doc's entries merge immediately alongside their fix PRs for the remainder of that window.**

**Process note, 2026-07-04:** working through the full CEO/CTO audit's remaining ~21 findings back-to-back per explicit "fix everything, don't stop" instruction. Per-fix local verification (tsc/test/build/lint/auth-guards) and a FINDINGS.md entry stay mandatory for every fix; the separate docs-only "deploy confirmed SUCCESS" follow-up PR used earlier tonight is dropped for this batch to avoid serializing ~20 fixes behind ~20 extra PRs — Railway deploy health is spot-checked periodically instead of after every single merge. **Scope note:** the earlier standing "UI is Cursor's job" boundary was specifically about the landing-page BIE banner design work; this "fix everything from the audit" instruction is broader and explicit, so a few of the remaining findings do touch `.tsx` files (`FlowAlertStream.tsx`, `NetPremiumLeaderboard.tsx`, `ZeroDteBoard.tsx`) — each one is a surgical logic-only bug fix (a DTE calculation, a loading-state prop, a freshness signal), never a visual/layout change, to stay out of the way of Cursor's active design work on the same components. **Tooling note:** the GitHub MCP proxy's session quota is separately rate-limited from the underlying GitHub API (confirmed: REST via a direct token has ~14.8k/15k requests remaining while the MCP proxy returned "rate limit exceeded") — from here on, PRs are opened directly ready-for-review (skipping the draft→ready round trip) and comment/review checks use direct REST calls, to conserve that budget for the unavoidable create/merge calls.

## 🧩 ADDED 2026-07-05 — 0DTE Command admin health panel: last-scan-time / candidates-scanned / rejection-rate (task #150, branch `fix/zerodte-command-admin-health-panel`)

**Status:** SHIPPED (enhancement, not a bug fix — closes an observability gap). Internal admin tooling — `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` is an already-existing admin dashboard gated behind Clerk `role:admin`, not a member-facing page, so this is in scope directly (matches task #111's own scoping note verbatim: no new design language invented, this panel reuses that dashboard's existing `GlassPanel`/`MetricChip` conventions exactly). `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty (verified before opening this PR — this task never touches SPX Slayer).

**Motivation:** SPX Slayer got an admin health panel in task #111 (`AdminBieDashboard.tsx`'s "SPX health" `GlassPanel`); 0DTE Command — the SEPARATE multi-ticker scanner branded "0DTE Command" in-app (`/grid`'s default tab, formerly "BlackOut Grid"; see task #127's entry below for the naming confusion this distinction already had to be fixed once) — had no equivalent. An admin glancing at BIE had no way to see "is the 0DTE Command scan pipeline actually running, and how much of the tape is it throwing away" without reading raw Postgres rows.

**Where:**
- `src/lib/admin-zerodte-health.ts` (new) — `fetchZeroDteHealthSnapshot()`, the data source.
- `src/app/api/admin/zerodte/health/route.ts` (new) — `GET`, admin-gated (`requireAdminApi()`, same boilerplate as `/api/admin/spx/health/route.ts`).
- `src/components/admin/AdminBieDashboard.tsx` — new "0DTE Command health" `GlassPanel` + its own independent fetch/state/effect (`zeroDteHealth`/`loadZeroDteHealth`), wired into the existing "Recompute" button alongside the BIE report's and SPX health panel's own `load()`/`loadSpxHealth()`.
- `src/lib/admin-zerodte-health.test.ts` (new) — 12 cases.
- No `db.ts` schema change; no new provider/API dependency; no new instrumentation/counters — every figure is read from tables/functions that already existed before this task (confirmed first, per the task's explicit instruction to check before adding anything new).

**Where each of the 3 required metrics is actually sourced from (read in full before designing, per instruction):**
1. **last-scan-time** — there is **no dedicated `zerodte` entry in `cron-registry.ts`**. Traced the real call graph: `warmZeroDteBoard()` (`src/lib/zerodte/scan.ts`) is the only path that ever calls `persistZeroDteScan()`/`persistZeroDteRejections()`, and it is invoked exclusively from `src/app/api/cron/grid-warm/route.ts`'s `GET`, inside the same `Promise.allSettled` as 8 unrelated market-wide Grid warmers, logged via `logCronRun("grid-warm", ...)`. Per the task's explicit instruction to "mirror exactly" an existing `logCronRun`-based mechanism rather than invent a new one, this panel calls `buildCronHealthSnapshot()` (`admin-cron-health.ts`) — the exact same function `AdminCronDashboard.tsx`, `/api/admin/bie-report`, and the `cron-staleness-watchdog` cron already call — and reads its `grid-warm` job entry verbatim (`status`/`status_label`/`age_min`/`stale_after_min` all come from that function's own market-hours-aware staleness logic; none of it is reimplemented here). **Documented limitation, not silently glossed over:** a "healthy" grid-warm tick proves the CRON ran, not that the 0DTE Command scan specifically found or logged anything that tick — `grid-warm`'s own `logCronRun` payload has no per-warmer breakdown (`{ ok, warmed, failed, total }` only). Adding one would be new instrumentation the task said to avoid unless nothing existing already captures this — and something does (the cron-run history itself), just at grid-warm's granularity, not 0DTE-Command-only granularity.
2. **candidates-scanned** — confirmed via `deriveZeroDteSetups()` (`board.ts`) that every aggregated candidate ticker in a scan cycle ends up in EXACTLY one of two places: `setups[]` (cleared all 4 gates) or, when `opts.rejections` is supplied, a `ZeroDteGateRejection` push (failed a gate) — there is no third, silently-dropped outcome. But `zerodte_scan_rejections` (task #147) is **throttled to one row per (ticker, gate_failed, direction) state-transition**, not one row per scan cycle (`rejections.ts`'s own module doc) — so the persisted table cannot reconstruct "how many candidates were considered in the LAST scan tick," only "how many distinct tickers have transitioned through a rejected state at some point today." This panel therefore reports **today-session-cumulative distinct tickers**, not a last-cycle count: `committed_count` (distinct tickers in `fetchZeroDteSetupLog(today)`) + `rejected_count` (distinct tickers in `fetchZeroDteRejections()` filtered to today's `session_date`, MINUS any ticker also in `committed_count`). The subtraction matters: a ticker that failed a gate earlier today but later cleared every gate and made the board is a genuine success by end of day, not a rejection — without it, that ticker would be double-counted across both tables.
3. **rejection-rate** — `rejected_count / candidates_scanned`, `null` (never a fabricated `0`) when `candidates_scanned` is `0` (nothing scanned yet today — an honest "no data" state, same discipline this doc's other near-miss-log entries (#108, #147, #131) apply to unevaluated-gate fields).

**Sampling caveat, surfaced rather than silently under-reported:** `fetchZeroDteRejections()` (task #147's read path) has no `session_date` filter param — this panel fetches its most-recent 500 rows (`REJECTIONS_SAMPLE_LIMIT`, generous vs. the throttled write volume rejections.ts documents: single digits to low tens of distinct tickers/day) and filters to today in JS, rather than widening `fetchZeroDteScanRejections`'s SQL signature for a read this narrow in scope. `rejections_sample_capped` is `true` only when the full 500-row page came back AND its oldest row is still from today (proving there could be earlier-today rows beyond the page); it's `false` whenever the page's oldest row already rolled off to a prior day (proving every one of today's rows was necessarily captured) or the page came back under the limit at all. Surfaced in the panel exactly like `data-validator.mjs`'s own `INFO`/"skipped" idiom for a check that couldn't fully run.

**Resilience:** every external call inside `fetchZeroDteHealthSnapshot()` is individually try/caught (`buildCronHealthSnapshot()`, `fetchZeroDteSetupLog()`, `fetchZeroDteRejections()` independently) — a failure in any one leg degrades only that leg (`errors: string[]` records what broke) and still returns a 200 with whatever else succeeded, same contract as `admin-spx-health.ts`. The panel's own fetch/state/effect in `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` is fully independent of the main `/api/admin/bie-report` fetch AND the SPX health panel's own fetch — a failure fetching 0DTE Command health can never blank or block either.

**Blast radius:** three new files, plus `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` (new type, new state/effect, one new `GlassPanel`, one edit to the existing "Recompute" `ActionButton`'s `onClick` to also call `loadZeroDteHealth()`). No existing exported function's signature changed (`fetchZeroDteSetupLog`, `fetchZeroDteRejections`, `buildCronHealthSnapshot`, `todayEt` are all called exactly as already exported); no existing route touched; `zerodte_setup_log`/`zerodte_scan_rejections`'s own writers (`persistZeroDteScan`/`persistZeroDteRejections`) are completely untouched — this panel is read-only, additive, and one more reader alongside the existing Largo tools (`get_zerodte_plays`/`get_zerodte_rejections`) that already read the same two tables.

**Fix rationale — what was deliberately left unchanged:** did not add a dedicated `zerodte` key to `cron-registry.ts` — that cron literally does not exist as a separate HTTP route (`warmZeroDteBoard()` is a function call inside `grid-warm`'s handler, not its own endpoint), so registering a phantom cron key with no route to fire it would misrepresent the system, not clarify it. Did not widen `fetchZeroDteScanRejections`'s SQL to accept a `session_date` param — the existing `{ ticker, limit }` signature is reused by the Largo tool (`get_zerodte_rejections`) and this panel with zero changes; a 500-row page filtered in JS is simpler and sufficient for a health-glance panel, and avoids touching a function 2 other call sites already depend on for an admin-only, non-hot-path read. Did not call `scanZeroDteBoard()` live from the admin route to get an exact "this instant" candidate count — the task's own guidance was to derive these numbers from already-persisted data, and a live call would also trigger the same HELIX-tape/Night-Hawk-dossier pipeline the ~2-min cron already runs, on every admin page load, for no benefit over what the persisted tables already answer session-cumulatively.

**Tests added:** `src/lib/admin-zerodte-health.test.ts` (new, 12 cases, `mock.module("./db", …)` / `mock.module("./zerodte/rejections", …)` / `mock.module("./admin-cron-health", …)` / `mock.module("./nighthawk/session", …)` — all RELATIVE paths, per this repo's documented Node 20 `mock.module()`-alias-crash gotcha) — happy path (distinct committed + rejected tickers combine correctly); scan summary sourced verbatim from `buildCronHealthSnapshot`'s `grid-warm` entry; the committed-later-after-being-rejected-earlier dedup case (counts once, as committed); a rejection from a PRIOR `session_date` excluded from today's counts; zero candidates today → `rejection_rate: null`, never a fabricated `0`; cron-health/setup-log/rejections-log failures each independently degrade without throwing and without blanking the other legs; both `rejections_sample_capped` boundary cases (full page with oldest-row-still-today → `true`; full page with oldest-row-rolled-off → `false`) plus the under-limit case (`false`); `db_configured` mirrors `dbConfigured()` verbatim.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite passing on both Node 22.22.2 and Node 20.20.2 (`nvm use 20` + CI's exact glob-expansion invocation `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"`) — see PR for exact before/after counts. `npm run build` clean (`/api/admin/zerodte/health` present in the route manifest). `npm run lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. `node scripts/verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` GREEN (new route added, admin-gated). No browser available in this sandbox (Playwright/Chromium blocked) — the rendered UI was **not** visually verified; correctness was checked at the code/type level only (`tsc` catches JSX/prop-type errors even without rendering, and `next build` statically renders/prerenders during build). `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty.

---

## 🧠 ADDED 2026-07-05 — `gex_regime_events`: durable log of BlackOut Thermal's GEX regime/flip/wall-crossing events, independent of the live gex-alerts push dedup (task #136, branch `fix/gex-regime-event-log`)

**Status:** SHIPPED (enhancement, not a bug fix — closes an observability gap; `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty, verified before opening this PR). Direct GEX/Thermal analogue of task #108's `spx_engine_snapshots` and task #147's `zerodte_scan_rejections` (see those entries elsewhere in this doc for the precedent this follows), applied to `computeGexEvents()`'s intraday regime-transition stream — a different, currently-missing thing from task #135's `gex_positioning` ecosystem-context field (which surfaces the CURRENT dealer-positioning snapshot, not history of what already changed) and from `appendGexEodSnapshot`'s existing `gex-eod:{ticker}` Redis series (which is END-OF-DAY closes only, one entry per trading day, not intraday transitions).

**Where:** `src/lib/db.ts` (`gex_regime_events` table ~line 1163, `insertGexRegimeEvent`/`fetchGexRegimeEventRows` ~line 2066), `src/lib/providers/gex-regime-events.ts` (new file — `persistGexRegimeEvents`/`fetchGexRegimeEvents`/`gexRegimeEventsForLargo`), `src/lib/providers/polygon-options-gex.ts` (`GexEvent` type gains `from_value`/`to_value` ~line 652, `computeGexEvents()` ~line 1736 with its 4 push sites populating them at ~lines 1778/1795/1809/1830/1850, `fetchGexHeatmap()` fires the durable write ~line 2341, `computeGexEvents` now exported for direct testing), `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` (`get_gex_regime_events` ~line 357, `TOOL_GROUPS.stock_analysis`/`spx_desk`), `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts` (`get_gex_regime_events` case ~line 1275), `src/lib/largo/intent-keywords.ts` (`GEX_REGIME_HISTORY_RE`), `src/lib/largo/question-intent.ts` (`needsGexRegimeHistory`).

**Motivation / gap this closes:** `computeGexEvents()` (`src/lib/providers/polygon-options-gex.ts`, ~line 1736 post-fix (~1710 pre-fix, per the task brief) — re-verified current line number, shifted by this and prior unrelated merges) detects 4 kinds of GEX regime transitions (`flip_crossed`/`wall_broken`/`regime_flipped`/`net_gex_sign_flipped`) as a pure diff of the current sample vs. the latest `gex-history:{ticker}` positioning-history ring entry, on EVERY fresh matrix compute (cache miss) inside `fetchGexHeatmap()` (~line 2341 post-fix, ~line 2281 pre-fix). Before this task, that array only ever lived in two EPHEMERAL places: the shared, TTL-capped `gex-heatmap:{ticker}` matrix cache (`heatmap.events`, gone once the cache entry expires/refreshes) and the `gex-history:{ticker}` ring itself (capped at `GEX_HISTORY_MAX` ~24 samples / ~2h, `GEX_HISTORY_TTL_SEC` ~3h). `/api/cron/gex-alerts/route.ts` consumes the SAME `heatmap.events` array to fire live push alerts (confirmed via `grep -n "heatmap?.events" src/app/api/cron/gex-alerts/route.ts`), but on fire it only ever writes a Redis DEDUP key (`gex-alert-sent:{ticker}:{type}:{etDate}[:level]`, `ALERT_DEDUP_TTL_SEC` ~24h) — proof a push WAS sent, never a durable record of the event's own before/after values — and only for its own 3-ticker `REGIME_WATCHLIST` (SPY/SPX/QQQ) plus the subset of event types `isRegimeEvent()` treats as broadcast-worthy (`wall_broken` is regime-worthy ONLY for SPY/SPX, per `WALL_BROKEN_TICKERS`). So "at time T, SPY's gamma flip crossed" or "how many times has NVDA's call wall broken today" was unanswerable after the fact for ANY ticker, and unanswerable at ALL — even for the 3 watchlist names — once the ring/cache/dedup keys rotated.

**Evidence:** `grep -n "gex_regime_events\|gex-regime-events" src/lib/db.ts src/lib` (pre-fix, on `main`) returns zero matches — no durable table or write path existed for this data at all. `git log --oneline main | grep -i thermal-gex-ecosystem-context` (task #135) confirms `gex_positioning`/`getGexPositioning()` only ever surfaces CURRENT state (`src/lib/providers/gex-positioning.ts`'s `gexPositioningFromHeatmap`, a pure snapshot mapper with no history/diff logic) — it was never a substitute for this. Traced `computeGexEvents()`'s exact detection logic line-by-line (post-fix push sites: `flip_crossed` ~1778, `wall_broken`×2 ~1795/~1809, `regime_flipped` ~1830, `net_gex_sign_flipped` ~1850) and confirmed the SAME array flows to both `/api/cron/gex-alerts` (via `heatmap.events`) and, after this fix, the new durable persist call — one derivation, not two.

**What was built:**
- `gex_regime_events` (new table, `src/lib/db.ts`, migrated alongside `zerodte_scan_rejections` — the established "newest additions" spot): `id`, `observed_at` (insert time), `session_date`, `ticker`, `event_type`, `severity`, `message`, `level`, `direction` (these 4 mirror `GexEvent`'s own fields verbatim — never re-derived), `from_value`/`to_value` (the natural before/after numeric pair — see below), `detected_at` (`computeGexEvents()`'s own `at`, the ISO timestamp of the sample where the cross was detected — kept separate from `observed_at` for the same staleness-vs-write-latency reason `spx_engine_snapshots` separates `as_of`/`observed_at`).
- `GexEvent` gains two ADDITIVE optional fields, `from_value`/`to_value` (`polygon-options-gex.ts`) — populated inline at each of the 4 pre-existing `events.push({...})` call sites using values ALREADY in local scope, with zero lines of the actual crossing CONDITION/threshold logic touched (same "insert only, immediately adjacent to existing logic, never restructure" discipline task #147 established for its own gate-rejection captures). What each type's pair means, since each event is a genuinely different kind of crossing: `flip_crossed`/`wall_broken` — SPOT before/after (these events fire on spot moving across a level held FIXED as the prior sample's own reference, so spot is the value that actually changed, not the level); `regime_flipped` — the gamma-flip level at the prior sample vs. the current sample (posture is computed per-end against THAT end's own flip, so unlike `flip_crossed` the flip itself can genuinely differ between endpoints); `net_gex_sign_flipped` — total net dealer GEX dollars before/after. Both null when not computable (never fabricated) — `wall_broken` was the only case needing no new "is this computable" guard, since `priorSpot`/`curSpot` are already unconditionally available inside every branch that can push it.
- `src/lib/providers/gex-regime-events.ts` (new file — deliberately kept lightweight, importing only `@/lib/db` + `./spx-session`, same reasoning `src/lib/zerodte/rejections.ts`'s module doc gives for staying outside a much heavier engine's import graph, here `polygon-options-gex.ts`'s own Polygon/rate-limiter/heatmap-allowlist imports): `persistGexRegimeEvents(ticker, events)` (throttled write path) and `fetchGexRegimeEvents()`/`gexRegimeEventsForLargo()` (read paths).
- Wiring: `fetchGexHeatmap()` now fires `persistGexRegimeEvents(root, events)` fire-and-forget (never awaited, `.catch()`-guarded) immediately after `events = computeGexEvents(...)`, OUTSIDE the pre-existing try/catch that resets `shift`/`vexShift`/`events` to `'collecting'` on failure — a slow/unavailable Postgres can add zero latency to this hot matrix-build path, and a persistence failure can never affect the `events`/`shift` the function returns to its caller.
- New Largo tool `get_gex_regime_events` (`tool-defs.ts`, `run-tool.ts`, `TOOL_GROUPS.stock_analysis` + `TOOL_GROUPS.spx_desk`, alongside `get_gex`/`get_positioning` in both) — explicitly disambiguated in its description from `get_positioning`/`get_gex` (CURRENT snapshot only, no memory of earlier crosses) per the task's requirement. Also added `GEX_REGIME_HISTORY_RE` (`intent-keywords.ts`) + `needsGexRegimeHistory` (`question-intent.ts`) so wording like "when did the flip last cross" or "how many times has the wall moved today" gets a direct hint toward the new tool — same "new regex → new boolean → new toolHints.push" pattern task #110/#127/#147 established, with the same false-positive discipline (require an explicit GEX-domain token, never fire on a bare "how many times"/"when did"/"regime" alone — the last of which is literally `MARKET_REGIME_RE`'s own vocabulary).

**Largo-tool judgment call (per the task's explicit ask to document the reasoning, following task #108's/#147's precedent for this exact decision):** a NEW tool, not an `ecosystem-context` field, and not folded into the existing `get_positioning`/`get_gex` tools. `get_positioning`/`get_gex` (and task #135's `gex_positioning` ecosystem-context field) all answer "what is dealer positioning RIGHT NOW" — a single cache read, no history. "When did the flip last cross" / "how many times has the wall moved today" is a structurally different, genuinely retrospective question those tools cannot answer no matter how they're extended, because the underlying `GexHeatmap`/`GexPositioning` contracts only ever carry the current sample. This is the identical shape of decision task #108 made for `get_spx_engine_snapshots` vs. `get_spx_play`/`get_signal_log` (committed-state tools structurally can't answer "why was the engine scanning/rejecting") — a new tool over an ecosystem-context field, because this is retrospective/debugging data for a caller who already knows which ticker they're asking about, not a "what does the desk currently think" cross-instrument summary every `get_ecosystem_context` call already assembles.

**Throttling judgment call:** `computeGexEvents()` is a raw diff (current sample vs. the latest ring entry) — a real crossing can appear in that diff on EVERY fresh matrix compute until the ring's own ~5-min sample throttle (`appendGexHistory`) finally advances the baseline past it (traced: `appendGexHistory` returns the ring UNCHANGED, without appending the current snapshot, when the last entry is <5 min old — so `computeGexEvents`' "prior" stays fixed for up to 5 min while "current" keeps moving, meaning the SAME crossing can re-diff-true on every intervening fresh compute). This is the exact reason `gex-alerts` needs its own Redis dedup to avoid re-pushing the same cross — `persistGexRegimeEvents` needs the identical protection for durable writes, so it throttles via a `platform_meta` state-transition cursor keyed per `(ticker, event type + direction)` slot (JSON map, same `{date, key}`-per-slot-pruned-to-today shape `zerodte_scan_rejections`' own cursor uses, for the identical "a new day's first occurrence of a previously-seen transition must still log" reason), with the state signature being `(rounded level, direction)` — deliberately excluding `message`/`severity`/`from_value`/`to_value`, which are display/context fields that don't represent a NEW state (same reasoning `signalKey()`/`engineSnapshotStateKey()` give for excluding score/thesis/headline in the SPX precedents). Per-(type+direction) slots (not a single per-ticker cursor) because a single diff can emit MULTIPLE distinct events for the same ticker in one cycle (e.g. a call-wall break and a put-wall break together) — a single scalar cursor per ticker would let one slot's write suppress logging the other. This cursor is DELIBERATELY INDEPENDENT of `gex-alerts`' own Redis dedup key: different storage (Postgres `platform_meta` vs. Redis), different key namespace (`gex_regime_event_cursor` vs. `gex-alert-sent:...`), and different throttle semantics — this persists EVERY distinct transition all session long (a real requirement for "how many times has the wall moved today"), while `gex-alerts`' dedup collapses to once-per-ET-date-per-type for push-noise reasons. Verified via a dedicated test that neither path's storage is ever touched by the other (`gex-regime-events.test.ts`'s "independence" test below).

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/providers/polygon-options-gex.ts` (`GexEvent` +2 optional fields, `computeGexEvents` exported + 4 push sites each gain 2 keys — every existing condition/threshold/branch byte-for-byte unchanged, verified by the full pre-existing test suite passing unmodified plus 5 new dedicated tests; `fetchGexHeatmap` +1 fire-and-forget call, +1 import), `src/lib/db.ts` (+1 table, +2 functions, nothing existing touched), `src/lib/providers/gex-regime-events.ts` (new file), `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` + `run-tool.ts` + `intent-keywords.ts` + `question-intent.ts` (+1 tool end-to-end, +1 intent regex/boolean/hint). `appendGexHistory`/`appendGexEodSnapshot`/`computeGexShift`/`computeVexShift` and every other pre-existing matrix-build function are untouched — this is purely an additional, independent persistence of output that already existed. `/api/cron/gex-alerts/route.ts` is untouched (zero lines) — it keeps reading `heatmap.events` exactly as before; the new durable write is a parallel consumer of the SAME array, not a replacement or a second derivation. Considered and declined widening `gex-eod:{ticker}`'s EOD-snapshot series to also carry intraday events — rejected because that series is deliberately ONE ROW PER TRADING DAY (its own doc comment: "one entry per trading day," idempotent-replace-per-date) and an intraday event stream with potentially several rows per day is a structurally different shape, the same "new table, not a widened existing one" reasoning task #108 gave for `spx_engine_snapshots` vs. `spx_signal_log`.

**Fix rationale:** populated `from_value`/`to_value` inline at each existing `events.push({...})` call rather than restructuring `computeGexEvents()` to compute a generic before/after pair up front — the chosen approach never touches the actual crossing CONDITIONS (each `if` guard is byte-for-byte identical to pre-fix), staying inside the task's hard "do not alter any live GEX computation, alert-firing threshold, or dedup logic" constraint. Fired the durable write from INSIDE `fetchGexHeatmap()` (the single point `computeGexEvents()` is actually called) rather than from `/api/cron/gex-alerts` — the cron route only ever seeds 3 tickers on a ~5-min schedule, while `fetchGexHeatmap()` runs for every ticker Thermal computes a fresh matrix for (heatmap views, the SPX rail, Night Hawk positioning reads, etc.), so wiring at the cron route would have silently limited durable history to the same 3-ticker watchlist the live-alert system already narrows to for broadcast-noise reasons — a narrowing that has nothing to do with what's worth keeping a durable record of. Kept `gex-regime-events.ts` as a new, lightweight file (not added to `polygon-options-gex.ts` directly) specifically so this task's tests — and any future one — never need to mock that file's much heavier Polygon/rate-limiter import graph just to exercise the throttle logic, the same reasoning `zerodte/rejections.ts` already demonstrates works well for its own throttled writes.

**Tests added:** `src/lib/providers/polygon-options-gex.test.ts` (+5 cases, `computeGexEvents` now exported for direct testing, same "export a pure internal helper purely for unit testing" precedent this file already sets with `resolveHeatmapPageGuard`/`gexContractDedupeKey`) — cold history (<2 snapshots) returns `undefined`; a real flip crossing produces `flip_crossed` + `regime_flipped` with correct `level`/`direction`/`from_value`/`to_value` and nothing else fires; spot staying on the same side of a stable flip produces `[]` (no spurious row); a call-wall break produces `wall_broken` with spot before/after, isolated from flip/regime; a net-GEX sign flip produces `net_gex_sign_flipped` with real dollar totals before/after. `src/lib/providers/gex-regime-events.test.ts` (new, 14 cases, `mock.module("../db", …)`/`mock.module("./spx-session", …)` — both RELATIVE paths per this repo's documented Node 20 `mock.module()`-alias-crash finding) — db-not-configured/empty-events short-circuits, first-occurrence insert shape (including `from_value`/`to_value`), the core throttle proof (an unchanged crossing re-detected across the ~5-min ring-throttle window does NOT write a duplicate row even though `message`/`from_value`/`to_value` jitter), sub-point level rounding collapsing to one throttled state, a real reversal (direction flip) writing a new row, a call-wall break + put-wall break in the SAME cycle both writing via independent slots, two different tickers writing independently, a stale cross-session cursor entry not suppressing today's first occurrence, both `fetchGexRegimeEvents` paths, both `gexRegimeEventsForLargo` paths, and a dedicated test proving `persistGexRegimeEvents` never touches a simulated `gex-alerts` Redis dedup keyspace and vice versa (the task's explicit "verify your test asserts they don't interfere with each other" requirement). `src/lib/largo/question-intent.test.ts` (+3 cases) and `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.test.ts` (+3 cases) — the new regex/hint fires only on GEX-domain-qualified retrospective/count wording (with an explicit regression test proving it stays disjoint from `MARKET_REGIME_RE`'s own bare "regime" vocabulary), and the new tool's description disambiguates from `get_positioning`/`get_gex` and is confirmed absent from `SPX_ENGINE_TOOL_NAMES` (generic/ticker-scoped, like `get_gex`, not SPX-Slayer-engine-specific).

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite **1370/1370 passing (22 new)** on BOTH Node 22.22.2 and Node 20.20.2 (`nvm use 20` + CI's exact glob-expansion invocation `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"`) — identical pass count on both, no Node-20-only regressions (this PR's only new cross-module production-code import, `persistGexRegimeEvents` in `polygon-options-gex.ts`, is a static top-of-file `./gex-regime-events` import; every new `mock.module()` call uses a relative specifier). `npm run build` clean. `npm run lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. `node scripts/verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` GREEN (122 routes, no new routes — this task adds no API route). `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty.

## 🧠 ADDED 2026-07-05 — Night Hawk: `nighthawk_rejected`'s `input_snapshot` now carries the confluence-factor breakdown for ALL 5 rejection stages — re-scoped after confirming #129+#141 did NOT already close this gap, and that the task's own suggested fix (a `nighthawk_scoring_history` DB join) would have been a silent no-op (task #142, branch `fix/nighthawk-geometry-rejection-confluence`)

**Status:** SHIPPED (enhancement, not a bug fix — closes an observability gap). `git diff origin/main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty (verified before opening this PR — this task never touches SPX Slayer).

**Re-scoping investigation (per the task's explicit ask to verify whether #129/#141 already closed this before doing anything):** this task's ORIGINAL brief — written before both #129 and #141 merged — was "Night Hawk's `nighthawk_rejected` `decision_trace` never carries the confluence-factor breakdown `scoreCandidate()` computed for the candidate, only target/stop/entry-band pass/fail." Two sibling tasks landed since: **#129** durably archives `scoreCandidate()`'s full scoring breakdown into `nighthawk_scoring_history` (keyed `edition_for`+`ticker`), and **#141** wired 4 more rejection stages (premium-cap, illiquid-strike, ungrounded, sector-concentration) into `alert_audit_log` alongside the pre-existing geometry path, via a new `NighthawkRejectionDetail` union + generic `buildNighthawkStageRejectedAuditRow`/`recordNighthawkStageRejectedAuditTrail`. Read both fully (`src/lib/nighthawk/play-outcomes.ts` post-#141, `src/lib/db.ts`'s `nighthawk_scoring_history`/`fetchNighthawkScoringHistory`) before touching anything, per instruction.

**Finding 1 — the gap is real, confirmed by re-reading `decisionTraceForRejection`/`inputSnapshotForRejection` (play-outcomes.ts) end to end:** neither function references `dossier`, `scored`, `ScoredCandidate`, or `nighthawk_scoring_history` anywhere, for any of the 5 stages (geometry + the 4 from #141). `input_snapshot` for a geometry rejection carries only `entry_range_low/high`, `target`, `stop`, `score` (the model's own self-reported score, not the deterministic breakdown), and the raw Claude strings. So yes — a member/Largo asking "why was ticker X rejected" still cannot see "flow said X but the risk plan was untradeable" from the rejection row alone, exactly as the original brief anticipated. `get_ecosystem_context`'s `recent_audit_entries` (the one Largo surface that lists `nighthawk_rejected` rows) doesn't even forward `input_snapshot`/`decision_trace` at all (see Finding 3) — but the ROOT gap this task is scoped to is the data itself never being computed into the row in the first place, so that's what's fixed here.

**Finding 2 — the task's own suggested fix (querying `nighthawk_scoring_history` from inside the rejection-audit-row builder) does NOT work, and would have been a silently-empty no-op if implemented literally — this is the real reason #129+#141 didn't already cross-link the two tables:** traced the exact pipeline order in `edition-builder.ts`/`claude-edition.ts`. `generateEditionPlays()` (claude-edition.ts) computes `geometryRejected`/`stageRejected` and `edition-builder.ts` calls `recordNighthawkRejectedAuditTrail`/`recordNighthawkStageRejectedAuditTrail` on them at ~line 680-687 — **strictly BEFORE** the edition publishes. `archiveNighthawkStaging()` (task #129's write into `nighthawk_scoring_history`) is only ever called from `archiveAndClearNighthawkStaging()`, which `edition-builder.ts` invokes at its **post-publish** step (~line 901, inside the `try` block immediately after `upsertNighthawkEdition`) or from the various recap-only/force-rebuild-reset branches — every one of which runs AFTER (or, for the force-rebuild reset, on a PRIOR run's leftover data) the point where a rejection this run is recorded. So a query against `nighthawk_scoring_history` scoped to `editionFor` at rejection-build time would find **zero rows for tonight's edition** on the normal, non-resumed path — the literal DB-join the brief suggested would compile, look plausible in review, and silently do nothing in production, the exact class of bug this doc's own `AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md` correction (item 6, "steps 3+4 above were never actually writing rows") warns about: code that looks shipped but isn't exercised by the actual runtime order.

**Evidence:** `grep -n "archiveAndClearNighthawkStaging(editionFor)" src/lib/nighthawk/edition-builder.ts` shows exactly 4 call sites (recap-only clobber-guard skip, recap-only publish, force-rebuild staging reset at the TOP of `buildEveningEdition`, and the main post-publish step) — none of them precede `recordNighthawkRejectedAuditTrail`/`recordNighthawkStageRejectedAuditTrail`'s call site at ~line 680-687 for the SAME run. `grep -n "recordNighthawk.*RejectedAuditTrail(" src/lib/nighthawk/edition-builder.ts` confirms both calls happen immediately after destructuring `generateEditionPlays()`'s return, well before the `upsertNighthawkEdition`/post-publish block. Conversely, `dossierMap[ticker]?.scored` (the exact `ScoredCandidate` a rejection needs) is populated at the TOP of `generateEditionPlays()` (`const dossierMap = Object.fromEntries(params.dossiers.map((d) => [d.ticker, d]))`) and is ALREADY read from, in this same function, for `pinnedScore`/`scoredDirection` in `mapClaudePlayToEdition()` — proving the data is live and available in memory at every one of the 5 rejection push sites, just never threaded into the pushed object.

**Fix — thread the in-memory `ScoredCandidate` through, not a DB join (the correct version of what the brief asked for):** added an optional `scored: ScoredCandidate | null` field to `geometryRejected`/`stageRejected`'s array-item types (`claude-edition.ts`) and to the corresponding builder/recorder parameter types (`play-outcomes.ts`) — populated at all 5 push sites via `dossierMap[ticker]?.scored ?? null` (never fabricated; `null` when a ticker genuinely has no matching dossier this run, e.g. the mechanical-fallback path with no scoring at all). New `confluenceSnapshot()` (play-outcomes.ts) turns a `ScoredCandidate` into a compact, honest object — `total_score`, `direction`, `conviction`, all 5 core sub-scores (`flow_score`/`tech_score`/`pos_score`/`news_score`/`smart_money_score`), the 3 optional modifiers (`fundamental_score`/`catalyst_score`/`short_interest_score`, each defaulting to `null` when `scoreCandidate()` didn't compute them, never `0`) plus `catalyst_flags`/`fundamental_flags`/`earnings_risk`/`regime_multiplier`/`fundamental_block`/`trading_halt` — folded into `input_snapshot.confluence` via the ONE shared `base` object `inputSnapshotForRejection()` already builds for every stage, so all 5 rejection classes (not just geometry) get the enrichment uniformly, for free, from a single line of new code.

**Why extended to all 5 stages, not just geometry (the brief called geometry "the original, still-narrowest rejection class"):** the brief's narrower geometry framing predates #141 — before that task, geometry was the ONLY rejection stage with a durable row to enrich at all. Post-#141, all 5 stages already share one generic builder (`buildNighthawkStageRejectedAuditRow`) and one shared `input_snapshot` `base` object; special-casing the confluence fold to ONLY the geometry branch of a `switch` that already treats all 5 stages identically for `score`/`entry_range`/`target`/`stop` would have been more code (a bespoke branch) than applying it once to `base`, and would leave the exact same gap open for a premium-cap/illiquid-strike/ungrounded/sector-concentration rejection for no principled reason — the missing-confluence-context problem is identical across all 5, not geometry-specific.

**Blast radius:** `claude-edition.ts` — `generateEditionPlays()`'s return-type declaration (2 fields) and all 5 rejection push sites (geometry, premium_cap, illiquid_strike, ungrounded, sector_concentration) gain one additional key each; every existing field/value at every site is byte-for-byte unchanged. `play-outcomes.ts` — `buildNighthawkRejectedAuditRow`, `buildNighthawkStageRejectedAuditRow`, `inputSnapshotForRejection`, `recordNighthawkStageRejectedAuditTrail`, `recordNighthawkRejectedAuditTrail` all gain an OPTIONAL `scored`/`scored?` parameter (never required), so every pre-existing call site and every pre-existing test that omits it continues to compile and pass unchanged — confirmed by running the full pre-existing suite with zero edits to any prior test file. `edition-builder.ts`'s two call sites (`recordNighthawkRejectedAuditTrail(geometryRejected, editionFor)` / `recordNighthawkStageRejectedAuditTrail(stageRejected, editionFor)`) needed ZERO code changes — the new `scored` field flows through structurally since both arrays now carry it from `generateEditionPlays()`. `nighthawk_scoring_history`/`archiveNighthawkStaging`/`fetchNighthawkScoringHistory` (task #129) are completely untouched — per the hard constraint not to duplicate that archive's storage or `scoreCandidate()`'s scoring logic, this fix reads a REFERENCE to already-computed data, writes nothing new to any table, and adds no new DB round trip.

**Fix rationale — what was deliberately left unchanged, and the smaller gap NOT fixed here:** did not touch `get_ecosystem_context`'s `recent_audit_entries` (`src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts`) or `fetchAlertAuditTrail`/`fetchResolvedAlertAuditRows` (`db.ts`) — separately confirmed, while investigating this task, that **`decision_trace`/`input_snapshot` are write-only across the ENTIRE codebase**: `grep -rln "decision_trace\|input_snapshot" src/` finds only the write-side builders (`play-outcomes.ts`, `zerodte/board.ts`, `spx-commentary.ts`, `spx-play-claude.ts`, `flow-persist.ts`) and `db.ts`'s insert functions — zero readers anywhere (`AlertAuditTrailRow`, the type every read path uses, doesn't even declare those two fields; `recent_audit_entries` only surfaces `alert_type`/`fired_at`/`confidence_label`/`trigger_reason`/`outcome`). This is a PRE-EXISTING gap, not introduced or claimed-fixed by #129/#141, and it is NOT Night-Hawk-specific — it affects every `alert_audit_log` row from every product (0DTE, Night Hawk published, Night Hawk rejected, SPX plays). Fixing it properly means deciding how a Largo tool or admin surface should expose a potentially-large JSON blob for an arbitrary historical alert, which is real design work touching every alert type, not a Night-Hawk-scoped one-issue-one-PR fix — flagging it here as a separate, real, follow-up gap rather than folding it into this PR or fabricating an unused enrichment that nothing can ever surface end-to-end today. (Practically: an admin/on-call operator can still see this data via a direct Postgres query against `alert_audit_log`, which is how this repo's audit tooling already inspects the table — so the data is not entirely dark, just not yet wired into any chat-facing tool.) Chose an optional (`?`) field over a required one specifically so this fix touches zero pre-existing test fixtures — every one of #141's own tests for `buildNighthawkRejectedAuditRow`/`buildNighthawkStageRejectedAuditRow` (which predate `scored` and omit it entirely) continue to pass unmodified, proving the addition is additive-only by construction, not just by description.

**Tests added:**
- `src/lib/nighthawk/play-outcomes.test.ts` (+4 cases, no database, fixture-only — same pattern as this file's existing rejection-row tests): a full `ScoredCandidate` fixture folds into `input_snapshot.confluence` exactly (all 8 sub-score/flag fields, `deepEqual`) for a geometry rejection, alongside the pre-existing geometry fields staying untouched; `scored` omitted entirely yields `confluence: null` (never fabricated); a MINIMAL `ScoredCandidate` (only the 5 required fields) proves every optional field defaults honestly (`null`/`[]`/`false`, never a guessed `0`); a premium-cap (non-geometry) stage rejection gets the identical fold, proving the shared `base` object applies uniformly rather than geometry being special-cased.
- `src/lib/nighthawk/play-outcomes-stage-rejected.test.ts` (+3 cases, DB-mocked via `mock.module("../db", ...)` — relative path, matching this file's existing convention and this repo's documented Node 20 `mock.module` alias-crash gotcha): `recordNighthawkStageRejectedAuditTrail` with a `scored` fixture reaches the actual `insertNighthawkRejectedAuditLog` call with `input_snapshot.confluence` populated; omitting `scored` writes `confluence: null` through the full record path; `recordNighthawkRejectedAuditTrail` (the geometry-specific thin wrapper) also threads `scored` through correctly, proving the wrapper's delegation to the generic function carries the new field, not just the pre-existing ones.
- No new/changed test needed for the 5 push sites in `claude-edition.ts` themselves — consistent with task #129's/#141's own documented precedent that `generateEditionPlays()` has no from-scratch integration-test coverage (its ~10-module dependency graph has no existing test-harness precedent in this repo); each push site's one-line `dossierMap[ticker]?.scored ?? null` addition is direct, unbranched data flow already covered structurally by `npx tsc --noEmit` (the return-type change would fail to compile if a push site's shape drifted) and functionally by the builder-level tests above, which exercise the exact same object shape each push site constructs.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite **1352/1352 passing (7 new)** on both Node 22.22.2 and Node 20.20.2 (`nvm use 20` + CI's exact `shopt -s globstar nullglob; files=(src/**/*.test.ts); node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"` invocation) — identical pass count on both (baseline before this branch: 1345/1345, confirmed via `git stash`). This PR's only new production-code import (`type { ScoredCandidate } from "./scorer"` in `play-outcomes.ts`; already imported in `claude-edition.ts`) is a plain top-of-file type-only import, and both edited test files' `mock.module()` calls use the pre-existing relative `"../db"` specifier (no new `mock.module()` calls were added — the new tests reuse the existing mocked module setup in `play-outcomes-stage-rejected.test.ts`). `npm run build` clean. `npm run lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. `node scripts/verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` GREEN (122 routes, no new routes). `git diff origin/main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty.
