## 🟡 ADDED 2026-07-05 — 0DTE Command board had ZERO ground-truth cross-validation in `data-validator.mjs` (task #148, branch `fix/zerodte-board-ground-truth-validator`)

**Status:** SHIPPED (gap closure, not a data-correctness bug in the app itself — the *validator* had a coverage hole, not the product). `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty (verified before opening this PR — this task never touches SPX Slayer, and never touches `src/**` at all).

**Where:** `scripts/audit/data-validator.mjs` only — purely additive: one new `zerodte_board` entry in the `P` payload map, six new helper functions (`nextTradingDayEtYmd`, `polygonSpotNow`, `resolveZeroDteContract`, `polygonHistRange`, `withinHistRange`, plus the pre-existing pattern of inline `rec()` calls), and one new validation block inserted between the existing GEX/greeks section and the flow section. No existing section's logic was touched (diff is 100% additions plus one line inside the `P = {...}` object literal).

**Root cause / motivation:** `scripts/audit/data-validator.mjs` is this repo's cross-provider correctness validator — Polygon+UW ground truth vs. the numbers members actually see — and already covers SPY/SPX/VIX prices, GEX/greeks consistency, and track-record arithmetic. Confirmed before writing anything: `grep -c "zerodte\|grid\|/api/market/zerodte/board" scripts/audit/data-validator.mjs` was **0** — the live 0DTE Command board (`GET /api/market/zerodte/board`, `src/app/api/market/zerodte/board/route.ts`) exposes `entry_premium`, `underlying_price`/`underlying_at_flag`, and `top_strike` for every setup members act on, and none of it was ever cross-checked against independent ground truth the way SPX/SPY/VIX/GEX numbers already are. Tasks #108 (`spx_engine_snapshots`), #127 (tool-routing fixes), and #147 (`zerodte_scan_rejections`) all touched adjacent 0DTE Command observability but none of them added ground-truth validation — this was a genuinely separate, still-open gap.

**What the board actually returns, and what's independently checkable (read in full before designing the fix):**
- `setups[]` (from `scanZeroDteBoard()`, `src/lib/zerodte/board.ts`/`scan.ts`) is the LIVE/ephemeral scan, recomputed on every poll (5s server-cache TTL) — carries `underlying_price`, `top_strike`, `direction`, `expiry` for candidates that may not be persisted yet.
- `ledger[]` (from `zerodte_setup_log` via `persistZeroDteScan()`) is the COMMITTED/persisted record — carries `entry_premium`, `underlying_at_flag`, `top_strike`, `direction`, `first_flagged_at` for tickers actually flagged today.
- **Blast-radius finding, noted rather than silently worked around:** `route.ts`'s ledger mapping (lines ~109-132) does **not** include `expiry` — the DB row (`ZeroDteSetupLogRow.expiry`, `src/lib/db.ts`) has it, but the public JSON omits it. A ground-truth check for a ledger row's option contract therefore cannot trust a caller-supplied expiry; this validator resolves it independently instead (see Fix).

**Fix:**
1. `underlying_price` (live `setups[]`) — fresh Polygon quote for the same ticker "now" (live snapshot during RTH, prev-close off-hours — identical `polygonSpotNow()` logic to the pre-existing SPY/SPX/VIX checks, parameterized by ticker), compared with the **same `priceTol` constant already used for SPY/SPX** (0.3% RTH / 1.5% off-hours) — reused verbatim per the task's own instruction to match, not invent, a tolerance convention. One exception documented in-code: `SPX` needs the indices snapshot endpoint, not the stock snapshot endpoint (mirrors the file's own pre-existing SPX-vs-SPY branching); no other index root is special-cased since none has been observed on this board in practice.
2. `top_strike` (both `setups[]` and `ledger[]`) — Polygon's `/v3/reference/options/contracts` reference endpoint (already proven-good elsewhere in this codebase: `src/lib/providers/polygon-options-gex.ts`'s `fetchPolygonOiByExpiry`), queried by `underlying_ticker` + `contract_type` (from `direction`) + `strike_price` + an `expiration_date` window bounded to `[today, next trading day]`. A match proves the strike is real AND resolves the OCC ticker + true expiration_date in one call — which the ledger's missing `expiry` field (above) made necessary rather than optional. `SPX` gets the same `SPX -> SPXW` root swap `buildOcc()` (`src/lib/ws/options-socket.ts`) already applies, so this isn't a guess — it's the same transform the app itself uses.
3. `entry_premium` / `underlying_at_flag` (`ledger[]` only, historical — these are logged AT `first_flagged_at`, not "now") — Polygon's own 1-minute aggregate bars (`/v2/aggs/ticker/.../range/1/minute/...`) for a ±3-minute window centered on `first_flagged_at`, checking the logged number falls inside `[min(low), max(high)]` of that window (the same "was this price achievable at that instant" test `gradePlanFromBars`, `src/lib/zerodte/plan.ts`, already applies when grading a play's own outcome). `underlying_at_flag` reuses `priceTol` as the range's cushion (consistent with #1); `entry_premium` uses a wider, **sourced-not-invented** tolerance: `src/lib/zerodte/plan.ts`'s own `buildContractPlan()` already treats `spread_pct > 15` as "illiquid," i.e. the app's own liquidity model considers up to 15% spread *normal* for a 0DTE option — reusing that exact number as `ZERODTE_OPTION_PREM_TOL_PCT` means this check only FAILs on a divergence the app's own definition would call abnormal, not on ordinary option bid/ask noise.
4. Empty board (0 `setups` AND 0 `ledger` rows) is reported as `INFO` — a legitimate, common state (pre-market, dead tape, every candidate failed a gate) — never a `FAIL`, matching this same file's pre-existing "if applicable" idiom (the market-holiday skip on the `wall ordering put_wall < call_wall` check, one section above). A degraded board response (`available:false`, route.ts's own catch-branch signal) is `WARN`; a totally failed/null fetch is a soft `INFO` (mirrors how every OTHER section in this file already treats a null payload — silently not running rather than a hard FAIL, since e.g. `P.gex` being null produces no explicit "fetch failed" record either).
5. Every check that cannot be completed (no historical bars for a thin/illiquid contract, unparseable `first_flagged_at`, no resolved contract) is reported as `INFO`/`"skipped — <reason>"`, this file's own established idiom for "not applicable this run" — **never** a new `SKIP` status invented for this file (checked first: the sibling `spx-bie-consistency-validator.mjs` does have its own `SKIP` status, but that is a *different* script with its own vocabulary; this file's existing convention, e.g. line 188's `"skipped — market holiday..."` INFO, was matched instead).
6. Also added `zerodte_board` to the `P` payload map read by the pre-existing generic malformed-number scanner at the bottom of the file — free extra coverage (NaN/Infinity/unrounded-float scanning) for the whole board payload with zero new code in that section.

**Evidence — live-verified from this sandbox where possible, explicit about what wasn't:**
- **Live, end-to-end, against production:** ran the full script for real (`CLERK_SECRET_KEY`/`POLYGON_API_KEY`/`UW_API_KEY` are literal secrets in this sandbox, and — contrary to this doc's own prior "audit at the code + captured-HTTP level" assumption for browser/WS-blocked surfaces — plain HTTPS REST to `blackouttrades.com` through the agent proxy IS reachable). Result: `auth: admin session established` PASS, `0DTE board: setups/ledger to cross-check` INFO ("board empty right now (0 live setups, 0 ledger rows)"), full run exits 0 with `{"PASS":7,"INFO":4}`. This proves the auth → fetch → empty-board-graceful-handling path end to end in production. It could NOT exercise the comparison branches (top_strike existence, historical range checks) because **the board is genuinely empty right now** (2026-07-05 is a Sunday; Polygon itself reports `market=closed`) — there is nothing on the board to cross-check, which is itself the correct, honest outcome for check #4 above, not a limitation of the check logic.
- **Dry-run against real Polygon data with constructed fixtures**, to prove the branches an empty live board couldn't reach: copied the new pure helpers verbatim into a throwaway harness and ran them against real Polygon responses (script + full output kept out of the PR — scratch verification only). `resolveZeroDteContract('SPY', 'long', <real near-the-money strike>, ...)` resolved a real contract (`O:SPY260706C00745000`); the same call with a bogus strike (`987654`) correctly returned `null`; an invalid `direction` short-circuited to `null` without an API call. `polygonHistRange('SPY', <a real, holiday-calendar-checked RTH instant>, 3min)` returned a real `{lo, hi}` bar range; `withinHistRange()` correctly judged the range's own midpoint as inside tolerance and 3x the high as outside. `polygonHistRange(<the resolved OCC>, ..., <wide window>)` returned real option minute-bar data (`{lo: 1.08, hi: 1.93}`) without error. All of this is genuine Polygon ground truth, not fabricated fixtures — only the *board-side* numbers being compared against were constructed, since the live board has nothing to offer today.
- `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. `npm run build` clean. `npm run lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. Full `src/**/*.test.ts` suite unaffected on both Node 22 and Node 20 (this PR touches zero `src/**` files, so this is a regression check, not new coverage — see the note below on why no new `*.test.ts` file was added).

**On tests (per the task's own explicit guidance to check first):** `scripts/audit/data-validator.mjs` is a standalone, manually/cron-invoked HTTP script — it has no companion `*.test.ts` file today, and none of its EXISTING sections (SPX/SPY/VIX price checks, GEX/greeks consistency, track-record arithmetic) are unit-tested either; they're validated by literally running the script, exactly as this task's own live run + dry-run above do. Forcing a `node --test` file onto this one new section, when the other nine sections in the same file have never had one, would be inconsistent with the file's own established convention — so none was added, matching this file's precedent rather than the (differently-scoped) `spx-bie-consistency-validator.mjs`, which also has no dedicated `*.test.ts` file for the same reason.

**Fix rationale — what was deliberately left unchanged:** did not modify `route.ts` to add the missing `expiry` field to the ledger response (the blast-radius finding above) — that would be a product-code change outside this task's explicit scope ("purely additive... a new section for 0DTE Command," never touching the endpoint itself); resolving the expiry independently via Polygon's reference-contracts lookup instead means the validator doesn't even need to trust the app's own (partial) data to do its job, which is arguably the more independent check anyway. Did not attempt a byte-for-byte re-implementation of `deriveZeroDteSetups()`'s full gate pipeline (premium/aggression/dominance/OTM thresholds) to "recompute" a setup from raw UW flow — that would duplicate real product logic inside a validator script (the same class of risk task #124's `spx-bie-consistency-validator.mjs` module doc explicitly reasons about and avoids elsewhere in this repo) and drift the instant the real thresholds change; checking strike/premium against independent Polygon ground truth is a strictly cross-provider check, not a logic-duplication one. Capped checks to 5 live setups + 5 ledger rows per run (`ZERODTE_LIVE_CHECK_CAP`/`ZERODTE_LEDGER_CHECK_CAP`), mirroring the app's own `ENRICH_TOP_N=5` dossier-enrichment cap in `scan.ts` — this is a manual/cron-run script, not a hot path, but there's no reason to fan out Polygon calls across a full 30-row ledger every run.

---

## 🧠 ADDED 2026-07-05 — `zerodte_scan_rejections`: retrospective near-miss/gate-rejection log for 0DTE Command's scanner (task #147, branch `fix/zerodte-scan-rejections-log`)

**Status:** SHIPPED (enhancement, not a bug fix — closes an observability gap; `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty, verified before opening this PR). Direct 0DTE Command analogue of task #108's `spx_engine_snapshots` (see that entry further down this doc for the precedent this follows) — but for the SEPARATE multi-ticker scanner branded "0DTE Command" in-app (`/grid`'s default tab, formerly "BlackOut Grid"), NOT SPX Slayer's own single-instrument engine (see task #127's entry, also below, for the naming-confusion this distinction already had to be fixed once).

**Motivation / gap this closes:** `deriveZeroDteSetups()` (`src/lib/zerodte/board.ts`) computes real gate metrics — gross premium, at-the-ask aggression share, side dominance, OTM/ITM% — for every aggregated candidate ticker the scanner considers, and checks them against 4 exported thresholds (`SETUP_MIN_GROSS`, `SETUP_MIN_AGGR_SHARE`, `SETUP_MIN_DOMINANCE`, `SETUP_MAX_ITM_PCT`). Any candidate that fails even one gate hits a bare `continue` (4 call sites: board.ts's per-ticker loop, pre-fix lines 285/290/294/315) with **nothing persisted** — the aggregated metrics existed only in memory for that one scan tick, then vanished. `persistZeroDteScan()` (`scan.ts`) and `buildZeroDteAuditRow()` (`board.ts`) only ever run on setups that already cleared every gate. So "why didn't ticker X ever hit the Grid board" was completely unanswerable after the fact — identical shape of gap to what task #108 closed for SPX Slayer's own rejected/scanning ticks, just never audited for this separate engine.

**What was built:**
- `ZeroDteGateFailure`/`ZeroDteGateRejection` (new types, `board.ts`) + an optional `opts.rejections` out-array on `deriveZeroDteSetups()`. This is a **surgical, additive-only** change: every existing `continue` statement stays in the exact same place, checking the exact same condition against the exact same threshold constant — the diff only INSERTS an `opts?.rejections?.push({...})` call using whatever data was already in scope immediately before each `continue` fires, then keeps the same `continue`. No gate, threshold, or ordering was touched; `opts.rejections` defaults to `undefined`, so every one of this file's 57 pre-existing tests (and the one production caller before this PR) sees zero behavior or allocation change. A rejection at an EARLIER gate genuinely has `null` for LATER gates' metrics (aggression/dominance/otm_pct) — the real scan never computes them either once it short-circuits, so this never fabricates a value the live code path didn't actually produce (same "never fabricate an unevaluated reading" discipline task #121 verified for the shadow-signal factors).
- `zerodte_scan_rejections` (new table, `src/lib/db.ts`, migrated alongside `spx_engine_snapshots`/`nighthawk_scoring_history`): `id`, `observed_at`, `session_date`, `ticker`, `gate_failed`, `threshold` (the live gate constant cited at rejection time — same discipline `buildZeroDteAuditRow` already uses, so a future threshold tune can't retroactively relabel a historical row), `gross_premium`, `aggression`, `side_dominance`, `otm_pct` (all nullable — see above), `direction`, `prints`, `first_seen`, `last_seen`. A NEW table, not a widened `zerodte_setup_log`, for the same reason task #108 gave for `spx_engine_snapshots` vs. `spx_signal_log`: a rejection has no committed entry/plan/strike the way a real setup does.
- `src/lib/zerodte/rejections.ts` (new file — deliberately kept OUTSIDE `scan.ts`, whose import graph pulls in the full Night Hawk dossier builder + Polygon providers + the options WS socket just to run the scan pipeline; this module only needs `@/lib/db` + the shared ET-date helper, so a test of its throttle logic never needs to mock any of that): `persistZeroDteRejections()` (throttled write path) and `fetchZeroDteRejections()` / `zeroDteRejectionsForLargo()` (read paths).
- Wiring: `scanZeroDteBoard()` now always collects `opts.rejections` into its `ZeroDteScanResult.rejections` field (cheap — a handful of array pushes per candidate). `warmZeroDteBoard()` (the grid-warm cron path) forwards it to `persistZeroDteRejections()`, fire-and-forget, on the exact same call as `persistZeroDteScan()` for committed setups. The member-facing board route (`/api/market/zerodte/board`) calls `scanZeroDteBoard()` too but never reads or persists `rejections` — mirrors the existing asymmetry where that route already never calls `persistZeroDteScan()` either (only the cron does).
- New Largo tool `get_zerodte_rejections` (`tool-defs.ts`, `run-tool.ts`, `TOOL_GROUPS.platform`) — explicitly disambiguated in its description from BOTH `get_zerodte_plays` (same scanner, committed-only — its own description now also points forward to the new tool) and SPX Slayer's `get_spx_engine_snapshots` (a completely different engine, per task #127's precedent for exactly this class of confusion). Also added a new `ZERODTE_REJECTION_RE` intent regex (`intent-keywords.ts`) + `needsZeroDteRejections` (`question-intent.ts`) so wording like "why didn't AAPL make the 0dte board" or "what gate did TSLA fail on the grid" gets a direct hint toward the new tool — same "new regex → new boolean → new toolHints.push" pattern task #110/#127 established, and the same false-positive discipline (REQUIRE co-occurrence with an explicit 0dte/grid token, never a bare "near miss"/"didn't make it"/"rejected" alone) task #127's own merge-time fix had to add for its hunt/scan/find family.

**Throttling judgment call (per the task's explicit ask to document the reasoning, following task #108's/#129's precedent for this exact kind of decision):** `deriveZeroDteSetups()` runs on two paths — the grid-warm cron (`warmZeroDteBoard`, `railway.grid-warm.toml`: every 2 min through the RTH UTC band) and the member-facing board route (`scanZeroDteBoard()` directly, collapsed to one build per 5s across all pollers via `withServerCache`). Critically, **only the cron path ever calls `persistZeroDteScan()`** for committed setups today — the board route is read-only, by design (its own module doc: "the board route calls scanZeroDteBoard() on member polls"). This PR's `persistZeroDteRejections()` call is wired into the SAME cron-only call site, so near-miss writes only ever happen on the ~2-min cadence, never on the 5s member-poll path — no new write pressure was introduced on the hot request path. Even at 2-min cadence, an idle-but-still-rejecting ticker would generate a near-duplicate row every cycle without throttling, so `persistZeroDteRejections()` still throttles via a state-transition cursor — but unlike `spx_engine_snapshots` (one instrument, one `platform_meta` cursor STRING), 0DTE Command tracks many simultaneous candidate tickers per scan, so a single scalar cursor can't represent "have I already logged THIS ticker's current rejection state." The fix keeps ONE `platform_meta` row (`zerodte_scan_rejection_cursor`) whose value is a JSON map `{ [ticker]: { date, key } }` — `key` mirrors `engineSnapshotStateKey`'s exact philosophy (gate_failed + direction only; deliberately excludes the jittery numeric fields), and the map is pruned to TODAY's date on every load so a new session's first rejection for a previously-seen ticker always logs rather than being silently suppressed by a stale cursor entry (verified by a dedicated test — see below).

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/zerodte/board.ts` (+2 types, +1 optional param, 4 new push-then-continue blocks — every existing gate/threshold/continue byte-for-byte unchanged, verified by the full pre-existing 57-test suite passing unmodified), `src/lib/zerodte/scan.ts` (+1 import, `ZeroDteScanResult` gains one field, `scanZeroDteBoard`/`warmZeroDteBoard` each gain a few lines — no existing logic altered), `src/lib/db.ts` (+1 table, +2 functions, nothing existing touched), `src/lib/zerodte/rejections.ts` (new file), `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` + `run-tool.ts` + `intent-keywords.ts` + `question-intent.ts` (+1 tool end-to-end, +1 intent regex/boolean/hint, `get_zerodte_plays`'s own description gains one forward-pointing sentence). `persistZeroDteScan`/`zerodte_setup_log` and `buildZeroDteAuditRow`/`alert_audit_log` — the committed-setup write paths — are untouched; this is a parallel, independent log for the REJECTED half only, never a duplicate of either. `SPX_ENGINE_TOOL_NAMES` (task #112's SPX-tool-calling cohort) deliberately does NOT gain `get_zerodte_rejections` — that cohort is explicitly scoped to SPX Slayer's own engine-state tools (see its own doc comment), and this is 0DTE Command's engine, a different product. Considered and declined adding a `zerodte_recent_rejection` field to `bie/ecosystem-context.ts`'s `EcosystemContext`: task #108 made the identical judgment call for `spx_engine_snapshots` (no ecosystem-context field, Largo-tool-only) for the same class of retrospective/debugging data, and `EcosystemContext`'s existing per-ticker 0DTE field (`zerodte_today`) is about "where does this ticker currently stand," not "why wasn't it flagged" — a genuinely different question this task's own Largo tool already answers end to end.

**Fix rationale:** captured rejection data by inserting a push immediately before each PRE-EXISTING `continue` rather than restructuring the loop to compute all 4 gate metrics unconditionally up front — the latter would have required reordering/duplicating parts of the gate-evaluation sequence (e.g. computing `dominantCall`/`dominance` before the aggression-share gate that currently precedes it), which risks a real behavior change to the live scanning/dedup logic the task explicitly says must stay untouched. The chosen approach is bit-for-bit provably behavior-preserving for `setups` (same conditions, same order, same thresholds) at the cost of the near-miss data being genuinely partial per gate — documented as a deliberate, honest choice, not a shortcoming. Kept `rejections.ts` as a new, lightweight file rather than adding these functions to `scan.ts` directly, specifically so this task's tests (and any future one) never need to mock `scan.ts`'s much heavier provider-import graph (Night Hawk dossier builder, Polygon bars, the options WS socket) just to exercise the throttle logic — the same reasoning `spx-signal-log.ts` already demonstrates works well for SPX's own throttled writes. Chose a per-ticker JSON-map cursor (not N separate `platform_meta` rows, one per ticker) so the throttle state stays a single, bounded row that self-prunes daily, rather than accumulating an ever-growing set of per-ticker keys in `platform_meta` with no natural cleanup path.

**Tests added:** `src/lib/zerodte/board.test.ts` (+7 cases) — one per gate (`min_gross`/`min_aggr_share`/`min_dominance`/`max_itm_pct`) asserting the near-miss row's gate_failed/threshold and that later-gate fields are `null`; a fully-qualifying candidate does NOT also get a near-miss row; a mixed batch only logs the ticker that actually failed; `opts.rejections` omitted is a no-op. `src/lib/zerodte/rejections.test.ts` (new, 12 cases, `mock.module("../db", …)`/`mock.module("../providers/spx-session", …)` — both RELATIVE paths, no `server-only` stub needed since this file's import graph never reaches it) — db-not-configured/empty-input short-circuits, first-rejection insert shape, the core throttle proof (unchanged state on the next cycle does not write a duplicate row even though gross_premium/aggression jitter), a `gate_failed` change firing a new row, a direction flip firing a new row, two different tickers in the same cycle both writing and independently throttling thereafter, a stale cursor entry from a DIFFERENT session date NOT suppressing today's first rejection, `fetchZeroDteRejections`'s ticker-scoping, and `zeroDteRejectionsForLargo`'s both no-ticker and ticker-scoped retrieval paths (satisfying the task's explicit "new Largo tool correctly retrieves near-miss history for a queried ticker" requirement). `src/lib/largo/question-intent.test.ts` (+3 cases) and `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.test.ts` (+3 cases) — the new regex/hint fires only on 0dte/grid-qualified rejection wording (with an explicit false-positive regression test mirroring task #127's own merge-time fix), and the new tool's description mutually disambiguates from both `get_zerodte_plays` and `get_spx_engine_snapshots`.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite **1323/1323 passing (66 new)** on BOTH Node 22.22.2 and Node 20.20.2 (`nvm use 20` + CI's exact glob-expansion invocation `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"`) — identical pass count on both, no Node-20-only regressions (the one new cross-module import this PR adds in production code, `zeroDteRejectionsForLargo` in `run-tool.ts`, is a static top-of-file `@/lib/zerodte/rejections` import, and every `mock.module()` call in the new/edited test files uses a relative specifier, per this doc's own documented Node 20 `mock.module()`-alias-crash finding above). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty.

---

## 🧠 ADDED 2026-07-05 — `flow_anomaly_near_misses`: retrospective near-miss/rejection log for HELIX's market-wide flow-anomaly detector (task #131, branch `fix/helix-flow-anomaly-near-misses`)

**Status:** SHIPPED (enhancement, not a bug fix — closes an observability gap, same class as task #108's `spx_engine_snapshots` and task #147's `zerodte_scan_rejections`, applied to a THIRD, separate engine). `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty (verified before opening this PR — this task never touches SPX Slayer).

**Where:** `src/app/api/cron/market-regime-detector/flow-anomaly-detection.ts` (new file — `detectFlowAnomalies()` extracted from `route.ts`, `FlowAnomaly`/`FlowAnomalyNearMiss` types, `LARGE_PRINT_THRESHOLD`/`SKEW_RATIO_THRESHOLD`/`SKEW_MIN_TOTAL_PREMIUM`/`NEAR_MISS_FACTOR` constants), `src/app/api/cron/market-regime-detector/route.ts` (`GET` — near-miss accumulator wired through `detectFlowAnomalies`, dedup loop's `else` branch now records `DEDUP_SUPPRESSED`, calls `persistFlowAnomalyNearMisses`), `src/lib/db.ts` (`flow_anomaly_near_misses` table ~line 1125, `insertFlowAnomalyNearMiss`/`fetchFlowAnomalyNearMisses` ~line 2058), `src/lib/platform/flow-anomaly-near-misses.ts` (new file — `persistFlowAnomalyNearMisses`/`fetchFlowAnomalyNearMissesFor`/`flowAnomalyNearMissesForLargo`), `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` (`get_flow_anomaly_near_misses` description, `TOOL_GROUPS.platform`, forward-pointer added to `get_market_regime`'s own description), `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts` (`get_flow_anomaly_near_misses` case), `src/lib/largo/intent-keywords.ts` (`FLOW_ANOMALY_NEAR_MISS_RE`), `src/lib/largo/question-intent.ts` (`needsFlowAnomalyNearMisses`).

**Root cause / motivation:** `detectFlowAnomalies()` (pre-fix, inline in `route.ts`, ~lines 63-137) computes real per-ticker metrics for every ticker with HELIX flow in the last 30 minutes — the max single print and the call/put premium split + skew ratio — but only ever pushes an `Anomaly` once a candidate clears one of two hard thresholds: a $2M+ single print (`LARGE_PREMIUM_PRINT`) or a 10:1+ call/put skew on $500k+ total premium (`DIRECTIONAL_FLOW_SKEW`). A candidate that fell short — a $1.8M print, an 8:1 skew — left absolutely no trace once the next 5-min cron tick recomputed `byTicker` from scratch, even though the metric had already been computed a moment earlier. On top of that, `route.ts`'s own 15-minute same-type+ticker dedup check (~lines 195-213) silently skips the `INSERT INTO flow_anomalies` for an anomaly that DID clear its threshold but already has a match logged recently — a SECOND, structurally different way a fully-computed anomaly leaves zero trace. Before this PR, "why didn't HELIX flag ticker X" was unanswerable in both cases, even though the pipeline had already computed the exact number and reason in every case.

**Evidence:** `grep -n "function detectFlowAnomalies" src/app/api/cron/market-regime-detector/route.ts` (pre-fix, on `main`) shows the function unexported and unreachable from any test file — Next.js's route-export validator rejects any named export from a `route.ts` file besides the HTTP method handlers (the same constraint `derive-composite.ts` was already split out to work around in this exact route), so there was structurally no way to unit-test this detection logic at all before this PR; `find src/app/api/cron/market-regime-detector -iname "*test*"` on `main` returns only `derive-composite.test.ts`, confirming zero coverage of the anomaly-detection/near-miss logic itself. `grep -n "flow_anomaly_near_misses" src/lib/db.ts` on `main` is 0. Traced both discard paths line-by-line: the two `if (maxSingle >= 2_000_000 ...)` / `if (total >= 500_000) { if (callRatio >= 10) ... else if (putRatio >= 10) ... }` checks in `detectFlowAnomalies` (nothing written on the untaken branch), and the dedup `SELECT 1 FROM flow_anomalies WHERE ... AND detected_at > NOW() - INTERVAL '15 minutes'` check in `route.ts`'s `GET` (nothing written when a match already exists) — confirmed these are the ONLY two places a computed `Anomaly`/candidate metric is discarded without a durable record.

**What was built:**
1. **Extracted `detectFlowAnomalies()`** into a new sibling file, `flow-anomaly-detection.ts` — forced by the SAME Next.js route-export constraint `derive-composite.ts` already worked around in this route, and a prerequisite for this task's own testing requirement (there was no way to unit-test this logic in its original, unexported, route.ts-embedded form). The extraction is byte-for-byte behavior-preserving for the pre-existing logic; the only additions are the optional `opts.nearMisses` accumulator and an explicit `metric_value` field on `FlowAnomaly` (see point 4 below).
2. **Near-miss band, not "every sub-threshold value":** a near-miss is only captured once a candidate's metric reaches `NEAR_MISS_FACTOR` (50%) of the real threshold — i.e. `LARGE_PRINT_NEAR_MISS_FLOOR` = $1M (half of the $2M print threshold) and `SKEW_RATIO_NEAR_MISS_FLOOR` = 5:1 (half of the 10:1 skew threshold). This is a deliberate judgment call: `flow_alerts` already floors every ingested print at $200k premium (`MIN_PREMIUM` in `flow-persist.ts`), so plenty of ordinary $200k-$900k prints exist in the tape that are not meaningfully "near" a $2M anomaly — recording every one of them as a "near miss" would flood the table with routine, unremarkable prints and defeat the retrospective-answerability purpose of this table (genuine close calls buried in noise). This band ONLY affects what's captured in the new table; the real anomaly thresholds (2M/10:1/500k) are completely untouched.
3. **Short-circuit discipline for the skew check, matching task #147's "never fabricate a later-stage metric that wasn't actually computed" precedent:** the ORIGINAL code gates the skew ratio computation behind `total >= SKEW_MIN_TOTAL_PREMIUM` — `callRatio`/`putRatio` are only ever computed once that gate clears, even though the arithmetic itself would be cheap regardless. A near-miss for `DIRECTIONAL_FLOW_SKEW` is therefore only ever recorded once that SAME gate has cleared — never a synthetic ratio for a ticker the live detector would never have evaluated at all. (Verified this isn't a single flat check per the task's explicit instruction to check before assuming so — there are genuinely two independent checks, `LARGE_PREMIUM_PRINT` and `DIRECTIONAL_FLOW_SKEW`, each with its own gate.)
4. **New `metric_value` field on `FlowAnomaly`** (both the extracted type and the two `anomalies.push()` call sites): a real bug surfaced while wiring the `DEDUP_SUPPRESSED` capture in `route.ts` — the existing `Anomaly.premium` field is a dollar amount for BOTH anomaly types (`maxSingle` for `LARGE_PREMIUM_PRINT`, but the TOTAL call+put premium, not a ratio, for `DIRECTIONAL_FLOW_SKEW`). Citing `a.premium` as the "metric measured against the 10:1 threshold" for a dedup-suppressed skew anomaly would have recorded a dollar figure against a ratio threshold — nonsensical and misleading data. `metric_value` is the actual value each check compares against its own threshold (identical to `premium` for the print case, the real winning ratio for the skew case), added additively so `premium`'s existing meaning/column is untouched everywhere else.
5. **`flow_anomaly_near_misses`** (new table, `db.ts`, migrated in the same `pg_advisory_lock` block immediately after `zerodte_scan_rejections` — the established "newest additions" spot on `main` at the time this branch was cut): `id`, `observed_at`, `anomaly_type`, `ticker`, `reason` (`'BELOW_THRESHOLD'` vs `'DEDUP_SUPPRESSED'` — see below), `metric_value`, `threshold`, `premium`, `direction`, `severity` (nullable — see point 6), `detail`. A NEW table, not a widened `flow_anomalies`, for the same reason task #108 gave for `spx_engine_snapshots` vs `spx_signal_log`: a near-miss has no committed severity/premium-that-actually-fired the way a real anomaly does.
6. **Two DISTINCT reasons, never conflated** (the task's explicit requirement): `'BELOW_THRESHOLD'` — `detectFlowAnomalies` itself never pushed the candidate to `anomalies` because the metric fell short of the hard threshold; `severity` is always `null` here because the live detector never assigns one to a candidate that doesn't fire. `'DEDUP_SUPPRESSED'` — `detectFlowAnomalies` DID push a fully-formed `Anomaly` (real `severity`, exact `premium`/`detail`), but `route.ts`'s own 15-minute dedup window already had a match, so the `INSERT INTO flow_anomalies` never ran; nothing is recomputed or guessed for this case, the already-computed `Anomaly`'s own fields are carried through verbatim. Collapsing these into one reason would make "why didn't X fire" unanswerable in the two most common follow-up shapes members actually ask ("was it just below the bar" vs. "did it already fire recently and get suppressed").
7. **`src/lib/platform/flow-anomaly-near-misses.ts`** (new file, deliberately kept OUTSIDE `flow-anomaly-detection.ts`/`route.ts` — only needs `@/lib/db` + the shared ET-date helper, mirroring `zerodte/rejections.ts`'s same import-light placement so a test of the throttle logic never needs to mock `detectFlowAnomalies`' own `fetchRecentFlows` dependency): `persistFlowAnomalyNearMisses()` (throttled write path), `fetchFlowAnomalyNearMissesFor()` / `flowAnomalyNearMissesForLargo()` (read paths).
8. **New Largo tool `get_flow_anomaly_near_misses`** (`tool-defs.ts`, `run-tool.ts`, `TOOL_GROUPS.platform`) — explicitly disambiguated in its description from BOTH existing anomaly-reading surfaces the task named (`get_ecosystem_context`'s `recent_anomalies` field and `get_market_regime`'s critical-anomaly count, both committed-only reads of `flow_anomalies`) and from `get_zerodte_rejections` (0DTE Command's own separate scanner/threshold set, task #147) — `get_market_regime`'s own description now also points forward to the new tool. Added `FLOW_ANOMALY_NEAR_MISS_RE` (`intent-keywords.ts`) + `needsFlowAnomalyNearMisses` (`question-intent.ts`) so wording like "why didn't HELIX flag AAPL" gets a direct hint toward the new tool.

**Throttling judgment call (per the task's explicit ask to document the reasoning):** `market-regime-detector` runs every 5 minutes during RTH (`railway.market-regime-detector.toml`'s `cronSchedule = "*/5 11-21 * * 1-5"`, confirmed against `cron-registry.ts`'s `schedule_label: "~Every 5 min (market hours)"`) — roughly HALF the cadence of task #147's 2-min grid-warm cron, but still frequent enough that an idle-but-still-near-missing ticker would generate a near-duplicate row every tick across a multi-hour RTH session without a throttle. `persistFlowAnomalyNearMisses()` therefore throttles via a `platform_meta` JSON-cursor map, the same state-transition idiom `persistZeroDteRejections` uses — but with a NEW wrinkle this engine's shape requires: a single ticker can independently near-miss BOTH `LARGE_PREMIUM_PRINT` and `DIRECTIONAL_FLOW_SKEW` in the very same tick (both checks run unconditionally per ticker in the original code — confirmed by a dedicated test), so the cursor is keyed by `${ticker}|${anomaly_type}`, not ticker alone; reusing zerodte's per-ticker-only key would let one anomaly type's state transition silently clobber the other's throttle state for the same ticker. The state-transition key itself (`reason` + `direction`) deliberately excludes `metric_value`/`premium`, which jitter tick-to-tick on an otherwise-unchanged near-miss — same philosophy `engineSnapshotStateKey()`/`rejectionStateKey()` already use.

**Blast radius:** `src/app/api/cron/market-regime-detector/route.ts` (detection logic moved to a new file — zero behavior change for the pre-existing `anomalies`/`market_regime` write paths, verified by the full pre-existing suite passing unmodified; the dedup loop's `else` branch is a pure addition, the existing `if` branch's `INSERT INTO flow_anomalies` is byte-for-byte unchanged), `src/lib/db.ts` (+1 table, +2 functions, nothing existing touched), `src/lib/platform/flow-anomaly-near-misses.ts` (new file), `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` + `run-tool.ts` + `intent-keywords.ts` + `question-intent.ts` (+1 tool end-to-end, +1 intent regex/boolean/hint, `get_market_regime`'s own description gains one forward-pointing sentence). `market_regime`/`flow_anomalies` themselves — and their existing writers/readers (`/api/market/regime`, `/api/market/anomalies`, `/api/platform/intel`) — are completely untouched; this is a parallel, independent log for the DISCARDED half only. Note on schema placement: `market_regime`/`flow_anomalies` themselves actually live in an out-of-band `src/lib/migrations/004_god_tier_features.sql` file (applied manually via `/api/admin/run-migration`, not auto-created by `ensureSchema()`) — `flow_anomaly_near_misses` deliberately does NOT follow that precedent; it's migrated inline in `db.ts`'s `runMigrations()` alongside `spx_engine_snapshots`/`zerodte_scan_rejections` so it self-provisions on first `dbQuery()` like the rest of this observability family, rather than depending on an admin remembering to run a separate out-of-band migration after deploy.

**Fix rationale:** captured near-miss data by inserting an `else if`/`else` branch immediately alongside each PRE-EXISTING threshold check, rather than restructuring the loop to compute and record every candidate unconditionally — the chosen approach cannot alter which anomalies fire, in what order, or under what conditions, since the original `if` branches and their conditions are completely untouched. Chose a 50%-of-threshold near-miss band (not "every sub-threshold value") specifically to keep the new table's signal-to-noise ratio meaningful given `flow_alerts`' own $200k ingestion floor — documented as a deliberate, judgment-based choice per the task's explicit ask, not a shortcoming. Kept `flow-anomaly-near-misses.ts` as a new, lightweight file rather than adding these functions to `flow-anomaly-detection.ts` or `route.ts` directly, for the same "test the throttle without mocking the heavier detection dependency" reasoning `zerodte/rejections.ts` already demonstrates. Chose a per-(ticker, anomaly_type) JSON-map cursor (not a single per-ticker cursor, and not N separate `platform_meta` rows) specifically because this engine's two independent per-ticker checks can BOTH near-miss simultaneously — a per-ticker-only key would have silently dropped coverage of whichever check updated second.

**Tests added:** `src/app/api/cron/market-regime-detector/flow-anomaly-detection.test.ts` (new, 11 cases, `mock.module("../../../../lib/db", …)` — relative path, same depth convention `spx-issues-sync/route.test.ts` already uses) — no-rows/omitted-opts no-ops, a $2.5M print firing a real anomaly with NO near-miss row also written, a $1.8M print in the near-miss band producing exactly one `BELOW_THRESHOLD` near-miss with `severity: null`, a $600k print (below the near-miss floor) producing neither, the analogous three cases for `DIRECTIONAL_FLOW_SKEW` (12:1 fires for real, 8:1 near-misses, a 9:1-ratio-but-sub-$500k-total ticker the live gate never reaches produces nothing), a mixed batch isolating which ticker gets which outcome, and a thrown `fetchRecentFlows` caught internally leaving `nearMisses` untouched. Row values in every test deliberately include a small offsetting opposite-side print — discovered while writing these tests that a ONE-SIDED ticker (all calls or all puts) trivially satisfies the ORIGINAL skew-ratio check too (the losing side's premium is 0, so its ratio resolves to the pre-existing `99` sentinel) — genuine pre-existing behavior this PR does not change, documented in the test file's own header comment so a future reader doesn't mistake the "offsetting row" pattern for arbitrary noise. `src/lib/platform/flow-anomaly-near-misses.test.ts` (new, 14 cases, `mock.module("../db", …)`/`mock.module("../providers/spx-session", …)`, both relative) — db-not-configured/empty-input short-circuits, first-insert shape, the core throttle proof (unchanged state does not duplicate despite `metric_value` jitter), a `reason` change firing a new row, a `direction` flip firing a new row, the SAME ticker near-missing on BOTH anomaly types in one tick both writing and independently throttling thereafter (the new cursor-key wrinkle this table required), two different tickers independently throttled, a stale cross-day cursor entry not suppressing today's first near-miss, and both `fetchFlowAnomalyNearMissesFor`/`flowAnomalyNearMissesForLargo` retrieval paths. `src/lib/largo/question-intent.test.ts` (+3 cases) and `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.test.ts` (+3 cases) — the new regex/hint fires only on anomaly/HELIX-qualified near-miss wording (with an explicit false-positive regression test), and the new tool's description mutually disambiguates from `get_ecosystem_context`, `get_market_regime`, and `get_zerodte_rejections`.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite **1374/1374 passing (29 new — verified against a clean `main` checkout's own 1345/1345 baseline)** on BOTH Node 22.22.2 and Node 20.20.2 (`nvm use 20` + CI's exact glob-expansion invocation `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"`) — identical pass count on both, no Node-20-only regressions (the two new cross-module imports this PR adds in production code — `persistFlowAnomalyNearMisses` in `route.ts`, `flowAnomalyNearMissesForLargo` in `run-tool.ts` — are both static top-of-file `@/lib/platform/flow-anomaly-near-misses` imports, and every `mock.module()` call in the new/edited test files uses a relative specifier, per this doc's own documented Node 20 `mock.module()`-alias-crash finding above). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty.

## 🟢 ADDED 2026-07-05 — Night Hawk: 4 later-funnel rejection stages (premium-cap, illiquid-strike, ungrounded, sector-concentration) were console.warn-only — wired into `alert_audit_log` (task #141, branch `fix/nighthawk-rejection-audit-trail`)

**Status:** SHIPPED (enhancement, not a bug fix — closes an observability gap, same class as task #129's `nighthawk_scoring_history`, just at a later pipeline stage). `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty (verified before opening this PR — this task never touches SPX Slayer).

**Where:** `src/lib/nighthawk/play-outcomes.ts` (new `NighthawkRejectionDetail` union, `buildNighthawkStageRejectedAuditRow`, `recordNighthawkStageRejectedAuditTrail` — plus `buildNighthawkRejectedAuditRow`/`recordNighthawkRejectedAuditTrail` refactored to delegate to them), `src/lib/nighthawk/claude-edition.ts` (`generateEditionPlays` — new `stageRejected` return field, collected at the premium-cap/illiquid-strike/ungrounded/sector-cap call sites ~lines 250-383), `src/lib/nighthawk/edition-builder.ts` (new `recordNighthawkStageRejectedAuditTrail(stageRejected, editionFor)` call alongside the existing geometry one, ~line 682), `src/lib/nighthawk/play-constraints.ts` (`capSectorConcentration`'s `dropped` gained `filled`/`play`; new `SECTOR_CONCENTRATION_MAX_PER_SECTOR` const), `src/lib/nighthawk/grounding.ts` (`groundPlays` gained a `dropped` return field), `src/lib/nighthawk/option-chain-prompt.ts` (`evaluatePlayAgainstChain`'s `StrikeValidation` gained `matchedOi`; new `STRIKE_MIN_OI` const).

**Root cause / motivation — task #129 vs. this task, the pipeline order that matters:** task #129 (`nighthawk_scoring_history`, entry further down this doc) durably archives `scoreCandidate()`'s SCORING breakdown for every candidate the nightly hunt considers, before staging is cleared. That is a strictly EARLIER, different pipeline stage: it answers "why was ticker X scored the way it was." This task is about a candidate that has ALREADY survived scoring, ALREADY survived Claude synthesis, and is being considered for PUBLICATION when one of 4 later gates in `generateEditionPlays()` (claude-edition.ts) drops it — a structurally different rejection point that task #129 does not touch and was never meant to. Read carefully before starting: only ONE rejection stage (`validatePlayGeometry()`, wired by task #29/#207-era work via `recordNighthawkRejectedAuditTrail()` into `alert_audit_log` with `alert_type: 'nighthawk_rejected'`) had a durable record. The other 4 — `filterPlaysWithinPremiumCap()` (claude-edition.ts, now ~line 250), the illiquid-strike `evaluatePlayAgainstChain()` loop (~line 261), `groundPlays()`'s HARD drops (grounding.ts, "ungrounded" — ~line 279), and `capSectorConcentration()`'s `dropped` array (play-constraints.ts, called from claude-edition.ts ~line 300, NOT edition-builder.ts as originally guessed before re-reading the code) — were each `console.warn`-only. So "why was ticker X rejected tonight" had a real, queryable answer for the geometry-fail class and NO answer at all for the other four, even though the pipeline had already computed exactly why in every case.

**Evidence:** `grep -n "console.warn" src/lib/nighthawk/claude-edition.ts` (pre-fix) shows exactly 4 rejection-adjacent warn call sites with no matching `insertNighthawkRejectedAuditLog`/`insertAlertAuditLog` write nearby — "strike validation rejected", "sector-concentration cap dropped", "premium cap rejected", plus `grounding.ts`'s own internal `console.warn(\`[nighthawk/grounding] DROP ...\`)`. `grep -n "nighthawk_rejected" src/lib/db.ts` shows the dedup index (`idx_alert_audit_log_nighthawk_rejected_dedup`) and the one existing write path (`insertNighthawkRejectedAuditLog`) already generic enough to carry ANY rejection stage's payload — it hardcodes `alert_type`/`source_table`, not the trace/reason/snapshot — so the DB layer needed zero schema change, only more callers.

**Task-brief discrepancy, noted for the record:** the assigning brief's title said "3 unlogged rejection stages" but its own body enumerated 4 (premium-cap, illiquid-strike, ungrounded, sector-concentration) alongside the 1 already-logged geometry stage. Re-reading `claude-edition.ts`/`play-constraints.ts`/`grounding.ts` end-to-end (as instructed) confirmed the code has exactly those 4 additional `console.warn`-only rejection points — all 4 are wired in this PR, not 3.

**Fix — design choice (documented per the task's explicit ask for judgment):** one discriminated-union type, `NighthawkRejectionDetail` (`{stage: "geometry"|"premium_cap"|"illiquid_strike"|"ungrounded"|"sector_concentration", ...stage-specific fields}`), and ONE generic pair — `buildNighthawkStageRejectedAuditRow`/`recordNighthawkStageRejectedAuditTrail` — instead of 4 near-duplicate build/record function pairs. Chosen over "4 separate functions" because all 5 stages (including the pre-existing geometry one) share the exact same envelope (`alert_type: 'nighthawk_rejected'`, `source_table: 'claude_edition_synthesis'`, `final_output: null`, the same DB write path with the same dedup index) and differ ONLY in `trigger_reason`/`decision_trace`/`input_snapshot` content — a `switch` over one union keeps that shared envelope in exactly one place instead of copy-pasted 5 times, at the cost of one extra level of indirection (`detail.stage`) callers must supply. The PRE-EXISTING `buildNighthawkRejectedAuditRow`/`recordNighthawkRejectedAuditTrail` (geometry) are kept as thin wrappers with their ORIGINAL exported names/signatures — refactored internally to delegate to the new generic builder, byte-for-byte identical output (proven by the pre-existing tests in `play-outcomes.test.ts` passing unchanged) — so the existing `edition-builder.ts` call site for geometry needed zero changes.

**What each new stage's audit row actually carries (answers "why was ticker X rejected"):**
- **premium_cap** — `entry_premium` (the actual per-share premium that triggered the reject) + `cap_per_share`/`cap_per_contract` (the platform thresholds, `MAX_OPTION_PREMIUM_PER_SHARE`/`MAX_OPTION_COST_PER_CONTRACT` from `constants.ts`) via `decision_trace: [{check: "premium_within_cap", passed: false, value: <premium>, threshold: <cap>}]`.
- **illiquid_strike** — the parsed `strike`/`side`/`expiry` (via `parseOptionsContract`, already used elsewhere in this file) plus the ACTUAL open interest that failed the floor and the floor itself. This required a small additive change to `evaluatePlayAgainstChain()` (option-chain-prompt.ts): it already computed `bestOi` internally to decide `verified`/`contradicted`, but only returned the boolean — added a `matchedOi: number | null` field to `StrikeValidation` (null when the strike+expiry isn't in the chain window at all) so the caller doesn't have to re-derive it. Also named the previously-inline `500` OI floor as `STRIKE_MIN_OI` (same value, now citable in the audit row instead of a bare literal duplicated at the call site).
- **ungrounded** — `groundPlays()` (grounding.ts) already computes a rich per-issue `detail` string for every HARD drop (e.g. `"AVGO target $1800 does not trace to any dossier S/R or chain strike (±2%)"` or `"... strike 1850 present on-chain but OI 120 < 500 (illiquid/off-chain)"`) and folds it into a flattened `summary.notes` text line — but the caller had no STRUCTURED way to get it. Added a `dropped: Array<{ticker, play, issues}>` return field carrying the exact same `GroundingIssue[]` that already produced the note/warn, so the audit row's `decision_trace` cites the real per-check reason(s), never a re-derived approximation.
- **sector_concentration** — `sector` + `already_filled` (the sector's count AT the moment this ticker was dropped — i.e. literally "how many other tickers already filled it") + `max_per_sector` (the threshold, newly named `SECTOR_CONCENTRATION_MAX_PER_SECTOR`, was an inline `2` default before). Required adding `filled`/`play` fields to `capSectorConcentration()`'s existing `dropped` array (it previously returned only `{ticker, sector}` — the caller had no fill-count or play snapshot to build a row from).

**Blast radius — every return-type change is additive, checked against every consumer:**
- `capSectorConcentration()`'s `dropped` array: ONLY consumer repo-wide is `claude-edition.ts`'s call site (grepped) plus `play-geometry.test.ts`'s one exact `assert.deepEqual(dropped, [{ticker, sector}])` — updated to assert the individual new fields instead of a full-object equality (deliberately, since `deepEqual` on an object literal breaks the instant a field is added; this is the one pre-existing test this PR had to touch, and it touches assertions only, not behavior).
- `groundPlays()`'s return shape: grepped every call site — the ONLY one is `claude-edition.ts` (`generateEditionPlays`); `grounding.test.ts` only tests the lower-level `groundPlay` (singular), never asserted on `groundPlays`' return shape, so adding `dropped` needed no test updates there (new tests only).
- `evaluatePlayAgainstChain()`'s `StrikeValidation`: two callers repo-wide — `claude-edition.ts` (this task) and `src/lib/correctness/nighthawk-verifier.ts` (reads only `.contradicted`/`.verified`/property access, never an exact-shape check) — unaffected by the new `matchedOi` field.
- `generateEditionPlays()`'s return type: one caller, `edition-builder.ts`. The new `stageRejected` field is optional (`?:`) exactly like the pre-existing `geometryRejected`, so every early-return path (mechanical-fallback / `!raw` / zero-parsed-plays) that doesn't set it is unaffected — `edition-builder.ts`'s `if (stageRejected?.length)` guard mirrors the pre-existing `if (geometryRejected?.length)` guard byte-for-byte.
- `insertNighthawkRejectedAuditLog()` (`db.ts`) itself: UNCHANGED — it already accepted an arbitrary `trigger_reason`/`decision_trace`/`input_snapshot` payload and hardcodes only `alert_type`/`source_table`, both of which are identical across all 5 rejection stages. Zero DB-layer changes were needed; this is a pure caller-side wiring task, confirming the DB schema/dedup design from task #29/#207-era work was already general enough.

**Fix rationale — what was deliberately left unchanged:** every one of the 4 stages' actual rejection LOGIC/thresholds (premium cap value, OI floor, grounding tolerance bands, max-per-sector count) is byte-for-byte untouched — this is purely additive persistence alongside existing behavior, per the task's hard constraint. The pre-existing `console.warn` calls at all 4 sites are also left in place (not replaced) — Railway log visibility during a live run is still useful independent of the durable record, and removing them was out of scope. Considered but rejected: writing the new audit rows from INSIDE `groundPlays()`/`capSectorConcentration()`/`filterPlaysWithinPremiumCap()` themselves (closer to where the drop happens) — rejected because those are pure, dependency-free functions in `play-constraints.ts`/`grounding.ts` (no `@/lib/db` import, keeps them client-bundle-safe per `play-outcomes.ts`'s own header comment about why `parsePlayLevels` lives in a leaf module) — introducing a DB dependency there would be a much larger, riskier change than returning the structured drop data one level up to `claude-edition.ts`, which already returns `geometryRejected` the same way for the pre-existing stage.

**Tests added (mirrors task #129's own "no from-scratch `generateEditionPlays()` integration-test precedent exists — unit-test the extracted functions directly" fallback, documented in that task's own FINDINGS.md entry):**
- `src/lib/nighthawk/play-outcomes.test.ts` (+4 cases) — fixture-only, no database: `buildNighthawkStageRejectedAuditRow` for all 4 new stages, asserting `trigger_reason`/`decision_trace`/`input_snapshot` cite the real premium+cap / strike+OI+floor / failed-claim detail / sector+fill-count, and `final_output` stays null (a rejected play was never shown to a member).
- `src/lib/nighthawk/play-outcomes-stage-rejected.test.ts` (new, 6 cases) — DB-mocked (`mock.module("../db", ...)`, real module spread + `insertNighthawkRejectedAuditLog` overridden, same idiom as `edition-builder-scoring-history.test.ts`): proves `recordNighthawkStageRejectedAuditTrail` actually reaches the DB write for each of the 4 stages with the right shape, that multiple rejections in one call each write their own row, and that a write failure is swallowed (never thrown — the audit trail must not be able to break edition publishing, same invariant the geometry path already had).
- `src/lib/nighthawk/grounding.test.ts` (+2 cases) — `groundPlays()`'s new `dropped` field: a HARD-dropped play is removed from `plays` AND reported structurally in `dropped` with `severity: "drop"` issues; a flagged/ok mix reports nothing in `dropped`.
- `src/lib/nighthawk/option-chain-prompt.test.ts` (new file, 6 cases) — `evaluatePlayAgainstChain()`'s new `matchedOi` field across contradicted / verified / multi-row-best-OI / chain-absent / unparseable branches, plus `STRIKE_MIN_OI`'s exact-floor boundary (500 fails, 500 itself does not) — this file did not exist before; `option-chain-prompt.ts` had no dedicated test coverage previously (only exercised indirectly via `grounding.test.ts`'s import).
- `src/lib/nighthawk/play-geometry.test.ts` (existing test updated, not added) — `capSectorConcentration`'s sector-cap test now asserts the new `filled`/`play` fields individually instead of one `deepEqual` (see blast radius above).

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite **1312/1312 passing** (26 new) on both Node 22.22.2 (dev default) and Node 20.20.2 (`nvm use 20` + CI's exact `shopt -s globstar nullglob; files=(src/**/*.test.ts); node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"` invocation) — identical pass count on both, no Node-20-vs-22 divergence. This PR's only new production-code static imports (`parseOptionsContract`/`STRIKE_MIN_OI` in claude-edition.ts, `NighthawkRejectionDetail` type-only) are plain top-of-file imports, and the one new `mock.module()` call (`play-outcomes-stage-rejected.test.ts`) uses the relative `"../db"` specifier per this repo's documented Node 20 `mock.module` alias-path gotcha (see the `get_positioning`/`gex_king_strike` entry below for the ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND crash that convention avoids). `npm run build` clean. `npm run lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. `node scripts/verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` GREEN (122 routes, no new routes). `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty.

## 🟢 ADDED 2026-07-05 — BlackOut Thermal's `get_ecosystem_context` had ZERO GEX/dealer-gamma field at all — `getGexPositioning()` was never wired in, even though Thermal computes it for every ticker on every heatmap poll (task #135, BIE/Thermal integration sweep, medium — third instance of the task #123/#128 asymmetry class, applied to Thermal)

**Motivation:** direct continuation of the precedent set by task #123 (SPX Slayer's `spx_full_state`) and task #128 (HELIX's `flow_full_state`, entry immediately below) — each time, `get_ecosystem_context`'s per-instrument reads turned out to be either a shallow hand-rolled summary or missing entirely, while the instrument's OWN dedicated Largo tool (or, here, its own UI) already had the full picture. BlackOut Thermal (the GEX/dealer-gamma heat-map product) had the MOST extreme version of this gap: not a thin summary, but **nothing at all** — grep confirmed zero "gex"/"gamma"/"heatmap" references anywhere in `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts` before this fix. `fetchEcosystemContext()` surfaced today's 0DTE take, the most recent Night Hawk take, the unified audit trail, HELIX flow (both the slim `recent_flow` aggregate and, since task #128, the full `flow_full_state`), pattern-detected anomalies, and (for SPX/SPXW) the entire SPX Slayer play-engine state — but never mentioned dealer gamma/vanna/delta/charm positioning, even though `src/lib/providers/gex-positioning.ts`'s `getGexPositioning(ticker)` already computes exactly that for the same ticker, on every Heat Maps UI poll, every SPX rail render, and every Night Hawk positioning read. So "what does the desk know about NVDA" via BIE/Largo answered SPX play state, HELIX flow, and anomalies, but was silent on whether dealer gamma favored a squeeze or a pin for that exact name.

**Where:**
- `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts` — new `gex_positioning` field on `EcosystemContext` (typed `GexPositioning | null`, re-exporting `GexPositioning` from `gex-positioning.ts` the same way `SpxPlayPayload` is already re-exported), `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELD_DESCRIPTIONS`, `emptyContext()`, `fetchEcosystemContext()`'s `Promise.all` + return object + top-of-function doc comment. No new helper function — see "Fix rationale" below for why.
- `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` — `get_ecosystem_context`'s tool description extended (additive) to document `gex_positioning`, including its relationship to the existing standalone `get_positioning`/`get_gex` tools.
- `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.test.ts` — 4 new tests, `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELDS`'s expected-field list extended.

**Fix:** added a NEW field — `gex_positioning: GexPositioning | null` — populated by calling `getGexPositioning(upper)` **directly inline** in the existing `Promise.all([...])`, no wrapper function. This is a deliberate departure from `fetchFlowFullState()`'s pattern (a named helper wrapping `getFlowTapeSummary()` + `enrichFlowsWithGex()`): `getGexPositioning()` already returns exactly `GexPositioning | null` with the exact honesty convention this field wants (`null` on a cold/no-data matrix, never a fabricated all-zero reading — confirmed by re-reading `gex-positioning.ts` fresh, per this task's explicit instruction not to rely on stale assumptions about its shape, especially since task #126's `gex_king_strike` addition landed on `main` mid-investigation), and needs no additional enrichment/reshaping step. A wrapper here would have been `async function fetchGexPositioningState(ticker: string) { return getGexPositioning(ticker); }` — pure indirection with zero logic — so it was left out, matching this task's explicit "reuse an existing function rather than writing new derivation logic" instruction as literally as possible. Runs for **every** ticker (no `isSpxSlayerTicker`-style gate): GEX positioning is not a single-instrument product the way the SPX play engine is, so there is nothing to gate on.

**Why safe to run unconditionally on every `fetchEcosystemContext()` call (investigated before wiring it in, same diligence task #128 applied to `enrichFlowsWithGex`):** `getGexPositioning()`'s own module doc states its PRIMARY data path is a strict CACHE-READER over the shared `gex-heatmap:{ticker}` matrix (`fetchGexHeatmap`, no forced refresh, never a second live upstream fetch) — the exact same cache key the Heat Maps UI and the SPX rail already read on every poll. The one thing that module doc's top-of-file summary is now slightly STALE about (a real discrepancy, flagged rather than silently trusted): the function body itself unconditionally also calls `validateGexAgainstUW()` to cross-validate call wall/put wall/flip against UW's REST strike ladder — a real second upstream touch the top-of-file "NEVER hits a second upstream" language doesn't quite cover anymore. That call is documented at its own definition as "cached 60s — safe on every call without touching the 2 RPS UW REST budget" and is wrapped in `.catch(() => null)`, so it never throws and never blocks the outer `Promise.all` on a slow/failed UW response. Net effect: one bounded, cached, non-throwing lookup per call — no new failure mode beyond what the shared heatmap cache read already carries, and cheaper than `get_positioning`/`get_gex` pay as standalone Largo tool calls today (both ultimately read the same cache).

**Honesty convention:** `null` when the shared GEX matrix is cold for this ticker (no provider configured, no live spot, or zero strikes) — `getGexPositioning`'s own contract, inherited unchanged rather than re-derived. No new freshness flag needed: unlike HELIX flow (`flow_feed_fresh` disambiguates "quiet" from "pipeline down"), a cold GEX matrix has no separate "genuinely no positioning data" vs. "pipeline down" distinction to make — `null` already means exactly one thing here.

**Blast radius / consumer check:** grepped every reference to `EcosystemContext` and `fetchEcosystemContext` repo-wide before touching anything. The only real runtime consumer is `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts`'s `get_ecosystem_context` case (`return fetchEcosystemContext(ticker);`, no per-field serialization) — needed no code change, the new field surfaces automatically, exactly as task #128's entry already noted for `flow_full_state`. `src/lib/bie/knowledge.ts`'s generated `platform:bie-capabilities` doc reads `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELDS` (names + descriptions only) — grows by one line automatically. `src/lib/bie/precedent-search.ts` still contains zero references to `fetchEcosystemContext`/`EcosystemContext` (re-verified; the task #123 regression test in `precedent-search.test.ts` already guards this generally) — this field's `GexPositioning` object (a bounded, flat shape, no per-strike arrays) has no path into the nightly embedding-ingest cycle. `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-ecosystem.ts`'s `EcosystemShadowInput = Pick<EcosystemContext, "zerodte_today" | "recent_anomalies" | "flow_feed_fresh">` doesn't reference the new field, so it's structurally unaffected. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` is **empty** (verified before opening this PR, per the standing constraint — this task never touches SPX Slayer's own engine).

**Fix rationale — why call `getGexPositioning()` directly instead of via a wrapper, and why not widen `get_positioning`/`get_gex` instead:** a wrapper would add a function whose entire body is `return getGexPositioning(ticker);` — the task's own guidance (mirroring how `fetchFlowFullState` justified its wrapper by the real enrichment logic inside it) was to skip a wrapper when it adds no value, and this is the textbook case: no reshaping, no honesty-convention translation, no secondary call. The alternative of exposing this data by widening `get_positioning` or `get_gex` instead of adding a new `get_ecosystem_context` field was rejected because those are Largo tools with their own established, narrower/differently-shaped contracts (`get_positioning`'s `PositioningSummary` reshapes into a `wall_summary` string and drops DEX/CHARM/`nearest_wall`/`distance_to_flip_pct`; `get_gex` returns the raw per-strike chain) — changing either would be an unrelated, riskier shape change to an existing, already-consumed tool, whereas adding a field to `get_ecosystem_context` is purely additive and matches the exact precedent task #123/#128 already established for this file.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean on Node 22. Full suite **1302/1302 passing** on both Node 22.22.2 and Node 20.20.2 (`nvm use 20`; CI's exact `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"` invocation) — 4 new tests in `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.test.ts`: `gex_positioning` reuses `getGexPositioning()` verbatim with the exact uppercased ticker argument and passes the full canonical object through untouched; `gex_positioning` is `null` (not a fabricated reading) when `getGexPositioning` returns `null` for a cold matrix; `gex_positioning` populates for ticker `SPX` exactly the same as any other ticker, proving it is NOT accidentally gated by `isSpxSlayerTicker` (while confirming `spx_full_state` still gates correctly via the existing `fullStateCalls` counter in the same call, mirroring task #128's equivalent proof for `flow_full_state`); and a plain single-name ticker (`AAPL`) populates identically. Existing `spx_play`/`spx_full_state`/`flow_full_state`/`ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELDS` tests pass unchanged (`ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELDS`'s expected-field list extended with `gex_positioning`, the only edit to a pre-existing assertion). `npm run build` clean. `npm run lint:brand` / `npm run lint:vendor` clean. `node scripts/verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` GREEN (122 routes, unaffected by this change). `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty.

## 🟢 ADDED 2026-07-05 — HELIX's `get_ecosystem_context` only ever got a hand-rolled slim flow aggregate while its own `get_flow_tape`/`/flows` route already computed the full tape + GEX enrichment (task #128, BIE/HELIX integration sweep, medium — same asymmetry class as task #123's SPX fix, applied to HELIX)

**Motivation:** direct continuation of the precedent set immediately above — task #123 gave BIE/Largo the SPX play engine's ENTIRE state (`spx_full_state`) instead of just `spx_play`'s slim mirror, because `get_ecosystem_context`'s per-instrument reads were all shallow hand-rolled summaries while each instrument's OWN dedicated Largo tool already returned everything. HELIX (options flow) had the exact same asymmetry, just never audited yet: `fetchEcosystemContext()`'s `recent_flow` field ran its own bespoke `SELECT ... SUM(total_premium) ... FROM flow_alerts WHERE ticker=$1` (6h call/put/unknown premium totals only — no strikes, no expiries, no individual prints), while Largo's OWN `get_flow_tape` tool (`run-tool.ts`'s `get_flow_tape` case) already calls `getFlowTapeSummary()` (`src/lib/platform/flow-service.ts`) for the exact same ticker and gets the full recent print list (ticker, premium, strike, expiry, direction, score, route, alert time) plus `top_tickers`/`total_premium`. On top of that, the live member-facing `/flows` route (`src/app/api/market/flows/route.ts`) additionally runs every alert through `enrichFlowsWithGex()` (`src/lib/flow-gex-enrichment.ts`) to attach `gex_proximity` (at/near the gamma flip, call wall, or put wall) — a third layer of context `get_ecosystem_context` never surfaced at all. So "what does BIE/Largo know about NVDA's flow right now" returned a thin premium-total aggregate while HELIX's own tape tool and the member dashboard both already had the full picture for that same ticker.

**Where:**
- `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts` — new `EcosystemFlowFullState` type, new `flow_full_state` field on `EcosystemContext`, `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELD_DESCRIPTIONS`, `emptyContext()`, new `fetchFlowFullState()` helper, and `fetchEcosystemContext()`'s `Promise.all` + return object.
- `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` — `get_ecosystem_context`'s tool description extended (additive) to document `flow_full_state`.
- `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.test.ts` — 3 new tests.

**Fix:** added a NEW field — `flow_full_state: EcosystemFlowFullState | null` — alongside the existing `recent_flow`, rather than widening or replacing it. Populated by a new helper, `fetchFlowFullState(ticker)`, which calls `getFlowTapeSummary({ ticker, limit: 50 })` (`src/lib/platform/flow-service.ts`) **verbatim** — the exact same function Largo's `get_flow_tape` tool already calls, already ticker-scoped via that function's own existing `ticker` option (`fetchRecentFlows`'s `WHERE ticker = $1` in `db.ts` — no new SQL, no new query path) — and then runs the returned `recent` rows through `enrichFlowsWithGex()` (`src/lib/flow-gex-enrichment.ts`) **verbatim**, the exact same enrichment the live `/flows` route applies, so each print gets the same `gex_proximity` tag a member would see. Folded into the same `Promise.all([...])` + outer `try/catch` as every other field, and — unlike `spx_full_state`'s SPX/SPXW-only gate — runs unconditionally for every ticker, since HELIX flow isn't a single-instrument engine.

**Why this is safe to run on every `fetchEcosystemContext()` call (investigated before wiring it in unconditionally, per this task's explicit ask):** `enrichFlowsWithGex()` dedupes its GEX lookups by ticker before fetching (`[...new Set(flows.map(f => f.ticker))]`) — since `getFlowTapeSummary()` is already ticker-scoped here, that dedup set has at most 1 entry, so this never spends more than ONE GEX lookup per call. That one lookup (`getGexLevelsForTicker`, `flow-gex-enrichment.ts`) races a 300ms timeout against a 60s in-memory cache and is wrapped in its own try/catch that resolves to `null` on any failure — it never throws, and `enrichFlowWithGex` (the pure per-row mapper, `flow-gex-proximity.ts`) just returns the row unchanged when no GEX levels are available. So this adds no new failure mode to the outer `Promise.all` beyond the plain DB read `getFlowTapeSummary()` already performs, and no meaningful latency beyond what `get_flow_tape` already pays as a standalone tool call today.

**Honesty convention — null, not an all-zero object:** `fetchFlowFullState()` returns `null` when `getFlowTapeSummary()` finds zero prints for the ticker in-window, mirroring `recent_flow`'s own existing `f && f.print_count > 0 ? {...} : null` ternary, rather than returning `{count:0, total_premium:0, top_tickers:[], recent:[]}`. `flow_feed_fresh` (unchanged, still computed the same way) remains the single signal a caller checks to tell "genuinely quiet" apart from "the pipeline is down and we can't see" — `flow_full_state` does not get a second, redundant freshness flag of its own; the tool description was updated to say so explicitly.

**Why ADD a field instead of widening `recent_flow`:** `recent_flow`'s slim call/put/unknown-premium-total shape is read by an existing consumer with a narrow, compile-time-enforced `Pick<EcosystemContext, ...>` (`src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-ecosystem.ts`'s `EcosystemShadowInput`) and asserted on by name in `ecosystem-context.test.ts`'s existing tests — both should see zero shape change. Exactly the same "why ADD" rationale task #123 already wrote up for `spx_play`/`spx_full_state` applies here verbatim; re-reading that entry before starting this one is what made the additive-only design a five-minute decision instead of a fresh one.

**Blast radius / consumer check:** grepped every reference to `recent_flow`, `EcosystemContext`, and `fetchEcosystemContext` repo-wide before touching anything. The only real runtime consumer is `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts`'s `get_ecosystem_context` case (`return fetchEcosystemContext(ticker);`, no per-field serialization) — needed no code change, the new field surfaces automatically. `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-ecosystem.ts`'s `EcosystemShadowInput = Pick<EcosystemContext, "zerodte_today" | "recent_anomalies" | "flow_feed_fresh">` doesn't reference `recent_flow` or the new field at all, so it's structurally unaffected. `src/lib/bie/knowledge.ts`'s generated `platform:bie-capabilities` doc reads `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELDS` (field names + descriptions only, never values) — grows by exactly one line automatically, no edit needed there. `src/lib/bie/precedent-search.ts` still contains zero references to `fetchEcosystemContext`/`EcosystemContext` (re-verified; existing regression test in `precedent-search.test.ts` from the task #123 PR already guards this) — so this field's `recent` array (up to 50 enriched `FlowRow`s) has no path into the nightly embedding-ingest cycle either. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` is **empty** (verified before opening this PR, per the standing constraint — this task never touches SPX Slayer's own engine).

**Fix rationale — why reuse `getFlowTapeSummary()`/`enrichFlowsWithGex()` instead of re-deriving:** identical reasoning to task #123's `getSpxPlayState()` reuse — a second hand-rolled tape query inside `ecosystem-context.ts` would risk exactly the class of duplicated-logic bug this repo has hit before (two independently-drifting derivations of "what is HELIX's flow tape for this ticker" quietly disagreeing). The only alternative considered was widening `recent_flow` in place; rejected because it's a proven, narrowly-typed, already-consumed shape (see "why ADD" above) and because task #123 already established the additive pattern as this repo's convention for exactly this situation — deviating here would just reintroduce the inconsistency task #123 fixed for SPX, one field later.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean on Node 22. Full suite **1279/1279 passing** on both Node 22 and Node 20 (`nvm use 20`; CI's exact `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"` invocation) — 3 new tests in `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.test.ts`: `flow_full_state` reuses `getFlowTapeSummary()` ticker-scoped (asserts the exact `{ticker, limit}` args and that `enrichFlowsWithGex()` runs over the exact rows returned) and passes the GEX-enriched result through untouched; `flow_full_state` is `null` (not an all-zero object) when there are zero prints, and `enrichFlowsWithGex` is proven never called in that case; `flow_full_state` populates for ticker `SPX` same as any other ticker, proving it is NOT accidentally gated by `isSpxSlayerTicker` the way `spx_play`/`spx_full_state` are (while confirming those two SPX-only fields still gate correctly in the same call, via the existing `fullStateCalls` counter). Existing `recent_flow`/`spx_play`/`spx_full_state`/`ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELDS` tests pass unchanged (`ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELDS`'s expected-field list extended with `flow_full_state`, the only edit to a pre-existing assertion). `npm run build` clean; `npm run lint:brand` / `npm run lint:vendor` clean.

---

**Follow-up sweep, 2026-07-04 (post-launch):** all 23 original CEO/CTO audit items closed and merged to `main` (PRs #435/#437/#439/#441/#442); `PG_POOL_MAX=4` also applied directly to the Railway `blackout-web` production service and a redeploy triggered to pick it up (both with explicit user confirmation — see the PG_POOL_MAX entry below for why this couldn't be done from a PR alone). A second, independent audit pass was then run against the resulting `main` specifically hunting for anything the first pass's blast-radius checks missed (same fail-open/duplication/rounding/grounding bug classes, new files). It found 9 more issues, all now closed — this was the 9th and last.
