## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — `get_positioning`'s warm (cache-hit) path hardcoded `gex_king_strike: null` even though the shared matrix already computes it (task #126, found during the Helix/Thermal/Night Hawk/0DTE-Command BIE-integration audit)

**Where:** `src/lib/providers/gex-positioning.ts` (`GexPositioning` type, `gexPositioningFromHeatmap`), `src/lib/nighthawk/positioning.ts` (`fetchPositioningSummary`'s primary branch, ~line 107-118).

**Root cause:** the canonical, shared `GexPositioning` contract (`getGexPositioning()` — the single cache-reader every desk/Largo/Night's Watch surface reads for GEX positioning) never computed a "GEX king" strike (the argmax-|net-gamma| strike — a distinct concept from `call_wall`/`put_wall`, which are the largest-POSITIVE and largest-NEGATIVE strikes separately, so the king can be either sign). `nighthawk/positioning.ts`'s `fetchPositioningSummary()` has two branches: a PRIMARY branch reading the shared `getGexPositioning()` cache (the common, "warm" path — hit on essentially every real call), and a FALLBACK branch (`buildSummary()` calling the older, separate `analyzeStrikeGexRows()`/`fetchPolygonPositioningBundle()` pipeline) that only ever runs when the shared cache is cold. Because the canonical contract had no king-strike field, the PRIMARY branch's return object hardcoded `gex_king_strike: null` with a literal comment `// not available in the light contract` — while the FALLBACK branch (via the older pipeline's own `gex_king_strike`) DID return a real value. So Largo/Night Hawk answered "don't have it" for this field during ordinary (warm-cache) operation, and only got a real answer on the rare cold-cache path — backwards from what a caller would expect, and silently wrong every single warm request.

**This was not merely undiscovered — the correctness-verifier team already found and worked around the same gap** without fixing the root cause: `src/lib/correctness/heatmap-verifier.ts:328`'s own comment reads *"getGexPositioning doesn't surface King directly, but the matrix strike_totals do — derive both."* — i.e. the verifier independently re-derives the king strike from `hm.gex.strike_totals` every time it needs one, rather than reading it off the canonical contract, because the canonical contract didn't have it. Confirmed via grep that the exact same argmax-|net-gamma|-over-`strike_totals` algorithm (`kingFromStrikeTotals`) is **independently duplicated in at least three other files**: `src/lib/correctness/gex-odte-scope.ts:115`, `src/lib/providers/spx-desk.ts:146`, and `src/lib/nights-watch/position-detail.ts:706` — all computing the identical value from the identical underlying matrix because none of them could get it from the one contract meant to be the single source of truth.

**Fix:** added `gex_king_strike: number | null` to the canonical `GexPositioning` type and computed it inside `gexPositioningFromHeatmap()` (the pure mapper every `getGexPositioning()` call ultimately runs) via a local `kingFromStrikeTotals(gex.strike_totals)` — same argmax-|net-gamma| algorithm as the existing duplicates, kept local to `gex-positioning.ts` rather than importing one of the `correctness/`-side copies (that would create a `providers/` → `correctness/` dependency running the wrong direction). Updated `nighthawk/positioning.ts`'s primary branch to read `gex.gex_king_strike` instead of the hardcoded `null`. `npx tsc --noEmit` confirmed this is the ONLY object-literal construction site for `GexPositioning` in the codebase (adding a new required field broke nothing else).

**Blast radius:** every consumer of `fetchPositioningSummary()`'s primary (warm) path now gets a real `gex_king_strike` for the first time — this includes Night Hawk's own positioning read and anything downstream that renders/reasons about it. `heatmap-verifier.ts` and the other 3 duplicate implementations were deliberately left untouched (each still independently re-derives from `strike_totals`, which is correct and equally valid) — consolidating all 4 implementations into one shared helper is flagged as a separate, out-of-scope follow-up (same pattern as this repo's prior `todayEt()`/`fmtPremium` consolidation sweeps), not bundled into this bug fix to keep the PR small and reviewable.

**Fix rationale:** fixed at the canonical-contract layer (`gex-positioning.ts`) rather than patching `nighthawk/positioning.ts` locally, because the missing field was a genuine gap in the shared contract itself (evidenced by the verifier's independent workaround and the 3 duplicate implementations) — patching only the one call site would have left every other current-and-future consumer of `GexPositioning` still missing this field.

**Evidence / tests:** `src/lib/providers/gex-positioning.test.ts` (new, 3 cases) — `gexPositioningFromHeatmap`'s pure mapper: a put-side strike with larger magnitude than the call-side wins the king (proving it's a real argmax-by-absolute-value, not just "reuse call_wall"); an empty `strike_totals` map (not merely all-zero) correctly returns `null`; non-finite keys/values are skipped. `src/lib/nighthawk/positioning.test.ts` (new, 1 case) — end-to-end: `fetchPositioningSummary()` with `getGexPositioning` mocked to a fixture carrying a non-null `gex_king_strike` now returns that value from the primary/warm path (the actual regression this bug caused). Both new test files needed `mock.module("server-only", { namedExports: {} })` — `gex-positioning.ts` (and its `gex-cross-validation.ts`/`gex-intraday-adjust.ts` imports) carry a real `import "server-only"`, this repo's standard cross-test-file gotcha.

**New Node 20 vs 22 finding (adds to this repo's existing dynamic-import gotcha, documented for future test-writers):** `positioning.test.ts` initially registered its mock as `mock.module("@/lib/providers/gex-positioning", {...})` — the SAME `@/`-alias specifier `positioning.ts` itself uses to import it. Under Node 22 this worked. Under Node 20 it crashed outright: `ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND: Cannot find module '.../src/lib/nighthawk/@/lib/providers/gex-positioning'` — tsx's `@/` alias-resolving loader hook does not run inside `mock.module()`'s own specifier resolution on Node 20, so the literal string `@/lib/providers/gex-positioning` gets treated as a relative path segment appended to the test file's own directory, producing a bogus path. This is DIFFERENT from (but in the same family as) the previously-documented Node 20 bug (a dynamic `import("@/...")` from inside an already-mocked module silently missing the mock) — this one is a hard crash at `mock.module()`-registration time, not a silent miss at call time. Fix: always call `mock.module()` with the RELATIVE path from the test file's own location (`"../providers/gex-positioning"` here), never the `@/` alias form — confirmed working on both Node versions. This matches every pre-existing `mock.module()` call elsewhere in this repo's test suite, which already use relative specifiers exclusively; this is now the second, independent confirmation of why that convention matters, not just style.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite 1280/1280 passing (4 new) on both Node 22.22.2 and Node 20.20.2 (`nvm use 20` + CI's exact `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"` invocation). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty (this fix never touches SPX Slayer's own play-engine code).

---

## 🧠 ADDED 2026-07-05 — `nighthawk_scoring_history`: durable copy of Night Hawk's per-candidate scoring dossiers, archived before staging is cleared (task #129, branch `fix/nighthawk-scoring-history-persist`)

**Status:** SHIPPED (enhancement, not a bug fix — closes an observability gap; `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty, verified before opening this PR). Direct Night Hawk analogue of task #108's `spx_engine_snapshots` (see that entry further down this doc for the precedent this follows).

**Where:** `src/lib/db.ts` (`nighthawk_scoring_history` table ~line 1062, `archiveNighthawkStaging`/`fetchNighthawkScoringHistory` ~line 4636), `src/lib/nighthawk/edition-builder.ts` (`archiveAndClearNighthawkStaging` ~line 174, its 4 call sites at ~282/305/344/889), `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts` (`get_nighthawk_dossier` case ~line 1357), `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` (`get_nighthawk_dossier` description ~line 370).

**Motivation / gap this closes:** `scoreCandidate()` (`src/lib/nighthawk/scorer.ts` lines ~740-912) computes a FULL per-candidate scoring breakdown for every ticker Night Hawk's nightly hunt considers — flow/tech/positioning/news/smart-money/fundamental/short-interest/catalyst sub-scores, `fundamental_block`, `trading_halt`. `edition-builder.ts`'s `buildEveningEdition` stages this via `saveDossierStaging()` (`db.ts` ~line 4513) into `nighthawk_dossiers_staging` DURING the hunt run, and the existing Largo tool `get_nighthawk_dossier` reads that table to answer "why was ticker X scored/excluded tonight." But `nighthawk_dossiers_staging` is a SCRATCH table: `clearNighthawkStaging(editionFor)` (`db.ts` ~line 4619) `DELETE`s every row for that edition the moment the edition publishes successfully — confirmed 4 real call sites in `edition-builder.ts` (pre-fix): the publish-guard "existing edition already has plays" clobber-avoidance branch inside `publishRecapOnlyEdition`, the recap-only-edition publish branch (same function), a force-rebuild's staging reset at the top of `buildEveningEdition`, and the main successful-publish path's post-publish step. So the dossier data was only queryable WHILE the run was still in flight; by the next morning, when a member actually asks Largo "why didn't Night Hawk pick TICKER last night," the staging rows were already gone and `get_nighthawk_dossier` returned an empty/null result with no way to answer the question.

**Evidence:** `grep -n "clearNighthawkStaging(editionFor)" src/lib/nighthawk/edition-builder.ts` (pre-fix, on `main`) returns exactly the 4 call sites above; `saveDossierStaging`'s own `nighthawk_dossiers_staging` schema (`db.ts`) has no `archived`/history sibling table anywhere in the pre-fix migration block — `grep -c "nighthawk_scoring_history" src/lib/db.ts` on `main` is 0. Traced every one of the 4 call sites' surrounding control flow in `edition-builder.ts` to confirm each one runs strictly AFTER the edition is either published (real plays or recap-only) or the job is judged safe to reset — i.e. exactly the point at which the staged dossier data becomes unrecoverable.

**Fix:** additive, three-part:
1. **New durable table** `nighthawk_scoring_history` (`db.ts`, migrated in the same `pg_advisory_lock` block, appended after `spx_engine_snapshots` — the established "newest additions" spot): `id`, `edition_for`, `ticker`, `dossier_json`, `scored_json`, `staged_at` (the staging row's own `created_at`, i.e. when `scoreCandidate` actually ran), `archived_at` (when the archive write happened — same staleness-vs-write-latency separation `spx_engine_snapshots` uses for `as_of`/`observed_at`), `UNIQUE(edition_for, ticker)`.
2. **`archiveNighthawkStaging(editionFor)`** (`db.ts`) — a single `INSERT INTO nighthawk_scoring_history ... SELECT ... FROM nighthawk_dossiers_staging WHERE edition_for = $1 ON CONFLICT (edition_for, ticker) DO UPDATE ...`. One round trip (not a fetch-then-loop-insert from the app layer), so the copy can't race a concurrent staging write. The upsert (not append-only) matters because a checkpoint-resumed build can archive the same `edition_for`'s partial staging more than once as more tickers get staged across resumes — the later, fuller archive for a given ticker supersedes the earlier one instead of stacking duplicates. No throttling needed (unlike `spx_engine_snapshots`, which guards a tight per-minute poll loop) — the nightly hunt runs once per night and this is one bulk archive of already-computed rows, not a per-tick write, per the task's explicit scope.
3. **`archiveAndClearNighthawkStaging(editionFor)`** (`edition-builder.ts`, exported for testability) — a thin wrapper that calls `archiveNighthawkStaging` then `clearNighthawkStaging`, swallowing (logging, not throwing) an archive failure so a transient DB error can never block the clear — a stuck staging table would break the NEXT run's checkpoint-resume gating (`fetchStagedDossierTickers` filtering `remaining` in `stage_dossiers`), which is worse than losing one night's post-hoc queryability. **All 4 of the pre-fix `clearNighthawkStaging(editionFor)` call sites now call this wrapper instead** — same exact point in the pipeline, so WHEN staging is cleared relative to publish is byte-for-byte unchanged; only a durable copy is interposed immediately before the delete.
4. **`get_nighthawk_dossier` now falls back to the archive transparently.** `fetchNighthawkScoringHistory(editionFor, ticker?)` (`db.ts`) is the read path (same row shape as `fetchStagedDossiers`, so the two are drop-in interchangeable in the tool's response). `run-tool.ts`'s `get_nighthawk_dossier` case tries live staging first (`fetchStagedDossiers`/`fetchStagedDossierTickers`) and only consults the archive when staging comes back empty for that `edition_for` — response now carries `archived: boolean` so Largo (and its output) can distinguish "the hunt is still running tonight" from "this is last night's archived data."

**Design decision — extend `get_nighthawk_dossier` rather than add a new Largo tool (documented per the task's explicit ask for judgment + rationale):** task #108 added a brand-new tool (`get_spx_engine_snapshots`) because it was answering a genuinely NEW question `get_signal_log` structurally could never answer (committed-only vs. every tick). This case is different: `get_nighthawk_dossier` already asks the exact right question ("why was ticker X scored") — it just goes stale once staging is cleared. Adding a second tool (`get_nighthawk_scoring_history` or similar) would force Largo (or its routing hints) to guess up front whether tonight's edition has published yet, which it usually has no clean signal for — and a member's phrasing ("why didn't Night Hawk pick AAPL last night") never distinguishes "ask live staging" from "ask the archive." Making the existing tool fall back transparently means Largo's tool-calling behavior and `tool-defs.ts` routing hints need zero changes, and the member-facing answer is correct regardless of when the question is asked. The `archived` flag on the response preserves the one piece of information a caller might still want (staged-tonight vs. archived-from-last-night) without requiring two tools.

**Blast radius:** `db.ts` (+1 table, +2 functions — `saveDossierStaging`/`clearNighthawkStaging`/`fetchStagedDossiers`/`fetchStagedDossierTickers` byte-for-byte untouched), `edition-builder.ts` (+1 wrapper function, 4 call-site swaps from `clearNighthawkStaging` to `archiveAndClearNighthawkStaging` — no other line of the funnel/publish/recap logic touched), `run-tool.ts` (+1 import, `get_nighthawk_dossier` case body extended with a fallback branch — every other `case` untouched), `tool-defs.ts` (one description string extended to document the fallback — no schema/parameter change). `scoreCandidate()` itself (`scorer.ts`) is completely untouched — this is a pure persistence addition, per the task's hard constraint. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` is empty.

**Fix rationale — why this design, what was deliberately left unchanged:** chose a single `INSERT...SELECT` over fetching staged rows into JS and re-inserting, for the same reason `archiveNighthawkStaging`'s docstring gives — one round trip, no read-then-write race window. Chose to wrap `clearNighthawkStaging` (swap the call site) rather than inlining an `archiveNighthawkStaging` call next to each of the 4 sites independently, because a future 5th call site (or a refactor of one of the existing 4) could otherwise silently forget the archive step — routing everything through one wrapper makes "staging is never cleared without archiving first" a structural invariant instead of a convention four different code paths have to each remember. Deliberately did NOT change when/how often `clearNighthawkStaging` fires, per the task's explicit constraint, and left `saveDossierStaging`'s write path, the staging table's own schema, and every scoring/gate branch inside `scoreCandidate()` completely alone — this is additive persistence downstream of an already-computed result, nothing upstream needed to change.

**Tests added:**
- `src/lib/nighthawk/edition-builder-scoring-history.test.ts` (new, 4 cases) — mocks `../db`'s `archiveNighthawkStaging`/`clearNighthawkStaging` (spread from the real module, same idiom `run-tool.test.ts` uses, since `edition-builder.ts` statically imports several other `db.ts` names that would otherwise throw `does not provide an export named ...` once `mock.module`'s exports fully replace the real module) with a call-order log, then drives `archiveAndClearNighthawkStaging` directly (the one function every real pipeline call site now goes through): archive always precedes clear; the same `edition_for` is threaded to both calls; an archive failure is swallowed and the clear still runs (never blocks publish/resume); a 0-row archive (empty staging) still clears cleanly. `evaluateSpxPlay`-style from-scratch integration testing of the full `buildEveningEdition` pipeline was not attempted — same reasoning task #108 documented for `spx-signal-log-engine-snapshot.test.ts`: `edition-builder.ts`'s dependency graph (dossier fetch, Claude synthesis, critic, market-wide context, index dossiers, play backfill — ~10 modules) has no existing from-scratch test precedent in this repo, so directly unit-testing the extracted write-then-clear function is the established fallback.
- `src/lib/largo/run-tool.test.ts` (extended, +6 cases in a new `describe` block) — hoisted the file's single `before`/`mock.module("../db", …)` call and `runLargoTool` binding out of the pre-existing `describe` to file (root-suite) scope, because Node's ESM loader caches `./run-tool` on first dynamic import: a second `mock.module("../db", …)` call in a second `describe`'s own `before` would never reach the already-resolved module graph from the first import. New cases cover `get_nighthawk_dossier` both with and without a `ticker` filter: returns the live-staged dossier with `archived:false` when staging still has it; falls back to `nighthawk_scoring_history` with `archived:true` once staging is empty for that edition; returns `null`/`archived:false` when neither source has the ticker; and the equivalent three cases for the no-ticker "list tickers" path.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite (`node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test`) — **1286/1286 passing (10 new)** on both Node 22.22.2 (dev default) and Node 20.20.2 (`nvm use 20` + CI's exact glob-expansion invocation) — identical pass count on both, no Node-20-vs-22 divergence (the one new production-code static import this PR adds, `archiveNighthawkStaging` in `edition-builder.ts` and `fetchNighthawkScoringHistory` in `run-tool.ts`, are both plain top-of-file imports, and every `mock.module()` call this PR's tests add uses a relative `"../db"` specifier, per this repo's documented Node 20 `mock.module` alias-path gotcha). `npm run build` clean. `npm run lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. `node scripts/verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` GREEN (no new routes). `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty.

## 🟡 FIXED 2026-07-05 — 0DTE Command vs. SPX Slayer: both "0DTE"-branded engines shared the same bare routing token, risking Largo answering one engine's question with the other's data (task #127, medium — production mis-routing risk, not yet observed as a live incident)

**Where:** `src/lib/largo/intent-keywords.ts` (`SPX_DESK_RE`, `SPX_DESK_TOOLS_RE`, `PLAY_STATE_RE`, `SPX_ENGINE_STATE_RE` — the last one added by task #110 just one entry below this — plus the new `ZERODTE_COMMAND_RE`), `src/lib/largo/question-intent.ts` (`analyzeLargoQuestion`, `LargoQuestionIntent` — new `needsZeroDteCommand`), `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` (`get_zerodte_plays` ~line 218, `getToolsForIntent` ~line 632).

**Root cause:** this platform has two completely independent 0DTE engines that are BOTH branded "0DTE" in the product: **SPX Slayer** (`/dashboard`) is a single-instrument SPX/SPXW-only play engine (`get_spx_play`, `get_spx_structure`, etc.); **"0DTE Command"** (in-app tab label; historically "BlackOut Grid," `/grid`'s default tab) is a completely separate always-on scanner that hunts the BROADER MARKET across many tickers — index products (SPY/QQQ/NDX) and single names alike — for brand-new setups (`src/lib/zerodte/scan.ts`'s `zeroDtePlaysForLargo()`/`scanZeroDteBoard()`), surfaced to Largo via `get_zerodte_plays`. Every one of `SPX_DESK_RE`/`SPX_DESK_TOOLS_RE`/`PLAY_STATE_RE`/`SPX_ENGINE_STATE_RE` included the bare token `0dte` with no other SPX-specific qualifier required, so ANY question containing "0dte" hinted Largo toward SPX Slayer's tools — even a question actually about the separate scanner. `getToolsForIntent` (the function that gates which tool DEFINITIONS Claude even sees this turn) independently fires its own bare `0dte`/`zero dte`/`zerodte` match that adds `get_zerodte_plays` to the allowlist AND the entire `TOOL_GROUPS.spx_desk` bundle (which itself contains `get_spx_play`) — so a generic "what's the 0dte play looking like" question handed Claude BOTH engines' tools with zero signal to prefer one over the other. Compounding this, `get_zerodte_plays`'s description was a thin one-liner ("0DTE Command board — today's live 0DTE plays from the always-on scanner...") with no disambiguating clause at all, unlike `get_spx_play`'s description (rewritten in task #110 below) which explicitly says "for market-wide conditions... use get_market_regime instead" — `get_zerodte_plays` had no equivalent sentence pointing back at `get_spx_play`. Net effect: Largo had every structural ingredient to answer a 0DTE-Command-scoped question by citing SPX Slayer's numbers (or vice versa) and the member would have no way to tell which engine's data they were actually reading.

**Evidence:** confirmed the literal pre-fix `get_zerodte_plays` description string (tool-defs.ts, pre-fix): `"0DTE Command board — today's live 0DTE plays from the always-on scanner: lifecycle status (OPEN/HOLD/TRIM/CLOSED), entry premium and -50%/+100% plan, live P/L, graded results, plus fresh finds with BlackOut Intelligence action lines. Same data as /grid."` — zero mention that this is a different engine from SPX Slayer. Confirmed `getToolsForIntent`'s zero-dte branch (`/\b(0\s*dte|zero\s*dte|zerodte|command board|today'?s plays|the plays|scanner plays)\b/i`) already adds `get_zerodte_plays` AND `...TOOL_GROUPS.spx_desk` (which includes `get_spx_play`, `get_spx_structure`, `get_open_plays`, etc.) on the same bare match — verified by reading `tool-defs.ts` lines 627-677 and `TOOL_GROUPS.spx_desk`'s member list (lines 438-460). Confirmed `src/components/Nav.tsx` line 23 brands the `/grid` route `"0DTE Command"` with tagline `"Always-on 0DTE play hunter"`, and `/grid`'s own `page.tsx`/`GridPageTabs.tsx` describe it as "the always-on 0DTE hunter — scans the tape all session for new single-name plays" — confirming the two products' near-identical self-description is the actual source of the ambiguity, not a naming accident.

**Fix:** additive only, no tool-selection gate rewritten and no existing regex's bare `0dte` token removed (removing it would regress genuine SPX Slayer 0DTE questions — SPX Slayer legitimately IS a 0DTE product too, so a bare "0dte" mention staying an SPX Slayer signal is correct, not the bug). Three changes, following the exact pattern task #110 established one entry below for `SPX_ENGINE_STATE_RE`/`MARKET_REGIME_RE`: (1) added `ZERODTE_COMMAND_RE` to `intent-keywords.ts` — wording that specifically NAMES the scanner ("0dte command," "command board," "grid scanner," "grid board," "blackout grid," "across tickers," "multi-ticker," "fresh find(s)") or pairs scan/hunt/find-family words with 0dte, deliberately MORE SPECIFIC than the bare token the other four regexes and `getToolsForIntent` already match on; (2) wired `needsZeroDteCommand` into `LargoQuestionIntent`/`analyzeLargoQuestion` with a `toolHints.push("get_zerodte_plays")` call, giving a genuinely scanner-scoped question a stronger, additive hint without touching the pre-existing (still intentionally ambiguous on a bare "0dte") hint set; (3) rewrote `get_zerodte_plays`'s description to the same depth as `get_spx_play`'s — documents the real return shape (`plays` from the ledger with lifecycle status/entry/mark/pnl/peak_score/action/intel/graded-outcome, `fresh_finds` — the top-5 NOT-yet-ledgered setups, `excluded_covered_elsewhere` — tickers withheld because Night Hawk already covers them, and `rules` — the 0DTE discipline the board manages every play to) and adds an explicit two-way disambiguating clause: "IMPORTANT — do not conflate this with SPX Slayer... For SPX/SPXW's own single-instrument play-engine state, use get_spx_play... instead."

**Judgment call (per this task's explicit ask to document the reasoning):** deliberately did NOT strip `0dte` from `SPX_DESK_RE`/`SPX_DESK_TOOLS_RE`/`PLAY_STATE_RE`/`SPX_ENGINE_STATE_RE`, and did NOT touch `getToolsForIntent`'s existing zero-dte branch (which already puts `get_zerodte_plays` on the allowlist for a bare token — confirmed still true, no code change needed there). A bare "what's the 0dte play" genuinely has zero information pinning it to either engine — both products are legitimately "the 0dte play" from a member's point of view — so this fix does not claim to fully resolve that zero-signal case; the new regression test documents this explicitly as the pre-existing, intentionally-unresolved ambiguity. What the fix DOES resolve is the specific-wording cases: a question naming the scanner ("grid scanner," "0dte command") now gets an unambiguous extra hint toward `get_zerodte_plays`, and a question naming SPX Slayer explicitly continues to hint `get_spx_play`/`get_spx_structure` exactly as before, unaffected by the new regex.

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/largo/intent-keywords.ts`, `src/lib/largo/question-intent.ts`, `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts`, plus their two test files — no other file touched. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` is empty (confirmed before opening this PR); no scoring/gating logic in either engine touched. `getToolsForIntent`'s tool-ALLOWLIST behavior is unchanged (both tools remain reachable on a bare "0dte" exactly as before) — only the soft guidance-text hint layer and the `get_zerodte_plays` tool description changed.

**Fix rationale:** extended the existing hint system (new regex → new boolean → new `toolHints.push`) rather than adding a hard tool-selection gate or restructuring `getToolsForIntent`, matching this repo's established "Largo's tool selection is deliberately soft everywhere" precedent (task #110's own fix rationale, reused here for consistency). Chose NOT to require `get_zerodte_plays` to be REMOVED from the allowlist when SPX-specific wording is present (or vice versa) — over-narrowing the allowlist risks Largo being unable to call a tool it legitimately needs for a follow-up in the same turn (e.g. "how's SPX Slayer's play doing, and did the grid scanner find anything else today" needs both) — the fix is about which tool Claude is nudged to PREFER and CITE, not about hard-blocking either from being callable.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean on both Node 22 and Node 20. Full suite: 1280/1280 passing on Node 20 (`nvm use 20`; CI's exact `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"` invocation) — 4 new tests in `src/lib/largo/question-intent.test.ts` and 1 new test in `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.test.ts`. On Node 22, the same 30 pre-existing failures present on a clean `main` checkout (confirmed via `git stash` before/after) reproduce identically with this branch's changes applied — unrelated to this fix, matching this doc's standing note that Node 22 has a documented divergence from CI's actual Node 20 gate. `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty.

**Merge-time fix (caught during review, before merging):** the first cut of `ZERODTE_COMMAND_RE`'s scan/hunt/find alternation — `\b(scan|scans|scanning|scanner|hunt|hunts|hunting|hunter)\b` — had NO required co-occurrence with `0dte`/`zero-dte`, so it bare-matched "hunt"/"scanner" in totally unrelated questions, e.g. "what is Night Hawk hunting tonight" or "did the market scanner pick up anything on NVDA" both incorrectly set `needsZeroDteCommand: true` and nudged `get_zerodte_plays` into the hint set for a question with nothing to do with the 0DTE Command scanner. This reintroduced, in miniature, the exact class of bug this task exists to fix (an irrelevant tool nudged into the guidance for a different product's question) — verified via a standalone Node repro before touching the code. Fixed by requiring every scan/hunt/find variant to co-occur with `0dte`/`zero-dte` in the same question (matching the `find`-family alternation's already-correct pattern from the original diff), added a dedicated regression test (`"bare 'hunt'/'scanner' wording with NO 0dte context does not falsely fire needsZeroDteCommand"`), and re-verified: all 4 originally-intended cases (scanner-scoped hints fire, SPX-Slayer-scoped and bare-"0dte" cases stay unaffected) plus the 3 new false-positive repros all pass. Re-ran the full suite after the fix — unchanged pass count (1280/1280 on Node 20; same pre-existing unrelated Node 22 failures).

## 🧩 ADDED 2026-07-04 — SPX health panel in AdminBieDashboard (task #111): live phase/action/gates + desk/flow-feed freshness + recent signal log, read-only

**Status:** SHIPPED (`fix/admin-spx-health-panel`). Internal admin tooling — `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` is an already-existing admin dashboard gated behind Clerk `role:admin`, not a member-facing page, so this is in scope directly (the standing "member-facing/landing-page visual design is Cursor's job" boundary does not apply here — no new design language was invented; the panel matches this dashboard's existing `GlassPanel`/`MetricChip`/`DataTable` conventions exactly).

**Motivation:** `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` (the BIE control-room tab) had no view into the SPX 0DTE Command play engine's own live state — an admin glancing at BIE health had no way to see "is the engine currently blocked, and by what" without leaving the tab for the separate, much heavier `/api/admin/spx/dashboard` (analytics/lotto/power-hour/issues/terminal feed — built for deep SPX debugging, not a compact status glance). Task #108 (gate-rejection snapshots / `spx_engine_snapshots`) has **not** landed yet as of this PR (`git log main --oneline | grep -i "gate-rejected\|snapshot"` returns no such table/function) — this panel is built against what exists today (the live read-only evaluation snapshot + the committed signal log) and is designed to be extended once #108 lands, not blocked on it.

**Where:**
- `src/lib/admin-spx-health.ts` (new) — `fetchSpxHealthSnapshot()`, the data source.
- `src/app/api/admin/spx/health/route.ts` (new) — `GET`, admin-gated (`requireAdminApi()`, same boilerplate as `/api/admin/bie-report/route.ts`).
- `src/components/admin/AdminBieDashboard.tsx` — new "SPX health" `GlassPanel` + its own independent fetch/state/effect (`spxHealth`/`loadSpxHealth`), wired into the existing "Recompute" button alongside the BIE report's own `load()`.
- `src/lib/admin-spx-health.test.ts` (new) — 7 cases.
- No `db.ts` schema change; no new provider/API dependency.

**Design decision — why a new dedicated route, not `/api/admin/bie-report`:** that report is BIE-specific (interactions, calibration, discovery, embeddings/DB-pool/Redis probes) — SPX play-engine state doesn't belong in it, and folding it in would mean every BIE-report consumer pays for an extra desk+play evaluation on every load. Also deliberately **not** reusing the existing `/api/admin/spx/dashboard` route: that endpoint's `play` field is only populated when called with `?live=1` (otherwise `null`), and even then it pulls in a full `SpxAdminDashboardPayload` (analytics, lotto, power-hour, terminal feed, open incidents, 200-row outcome history) — the wrong shape and cost for a compact BIE-tab status glance. `admin-spx-health.ts` instead calls the same two functions the **member-facing** `/api/market/spx/play` route and the existing admin dashboard's own `live=1` dry-run path already call: `loadMergedSpxDesk()` (the one shared desk cache lane) + `readSpxPlaySnapshot()`.

**Read-only proof (critical constraint: this panel must never write to, mutate, or trigger any play-engine action):** `readSpxPlaySnapshot()` → `evaluateSpxPlay(desk, technicals, { mutate:false })`. Traced every `if (mutate)` branch in `spx-play-engine.ts` (lines ~184, 261, 302, 347, 408, 448, 589, 652, 734, 790, 856, 868, 907, 962, 978, 983) — every position open/close/trim write (`openPlay`/`closeOpenPlay`/`recordBuy`/`updateOpenPlay`), the `notifyPlayDiscord` alert, and every watch-record write is gated behind `mutate === true` and is therefore unreachable from `mutate:false`. The only unconditional side effect of calling `evaluateSpxPlay` at all is the pre-existing "shadow mode" observational factor logging (`spx-signal-log.ts`'s `logSpx*ShadowFactors` family) — that already fires on **every** member SPX Slayer poll today via the same `/api/market/spx/play` route; this panel adds one more read of an already-continuously-run path, not a new class of write. `fetchRecentSpxSignals()` is a plain `SELECT`. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` is **empty** (verified before opening this PR, per the standing constraint).

**What the panel shows:** current `phase`/`action`, `grade`/`score`, gate pass/fail **with the actual block reasons** (`gates.blocks`, not just a boolean — e.g. "Buy cooldown"), desk-feed freshness (`age_sec` vs. `playGexStaleMaxSec()` — reusing the **exact same threshold the live engine itself uses** to decide desk staleness, `spx-play-engine.ts` line ~181/`spx-play-gates.ts`, rather than inventing an independent number that could disagree with the engine's own judgment), the cluster-wide UW flow-feed heartbeat (`isFlowFrameFreshAnywhere()` — same helper the shadow-factor logging and `admin-spx-issues.ts` already use to answer "is flow live"), and the last 8 committed signal-log rows (`fetchRecentSpxSignals()`).

**Resilience:** every external call inside `fetchSpxHealthSnapshot()` is individually try/caught (desk+play together, since a play snapshot without its desk is meaningless; flow-feed probe and signal-log fetch independently) — a failure in any one leg degrades only that leg (`errors: string[]` records what broke) and still returns a 200 with whatever else succeeded. The panel's own fetch/state/effect in `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` is fully independent of the main `/api/admin/bie-report` fetch — a failure fetching SPX health can never blank or block the rest of the dashboard, matching the existing "Audit trail" panel's own "never breaking the rest of this panel on partial data" comment (line ~509 in the pre-PR file) applied at the whole-panel level instead of within one payload.

**Blast radius:** three new files, plus `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` (new types, new state/effect, one new `GlassPanel`, one edit to the existing "Recompute" `ActionButton`'s `onClick` to also call `loadSpxHealth()`). No existing exported function's signature changed; no existing route touched.

**Fix rationale:** chose the member-route's exact read-only pair (`loadMergedSpxDesk` + `readSpxPlaySnapshot`) over reinventing a lighter-weight confluence-only check, because gate block reasons and grade/score only exist as a product of running the full evaluation — there is no persisted "current gate state" table yet (that's what #108 will add). Chose `isFlowFrameFreshAnywhere()` over the heavier `buildMarketHealthSnapshot()` (which additionally pings Postgres, reads pool stats, and reads cross-instance telemetry) because this dashboard's hero chips already surface DB-pool/Redis health from the BIE report — pulling in the full market-health snapshot here would be a mostly-redundant, more expensive second read for the same signal.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean on both Node 22 and Node 20. Full suite (`node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test`) — **1251/1251 passing** (7 new) on both Node 20.20.2 (CI's exact invocation) and Node 22.22.2. `npm run build` clean (`/api/admin/spx/health` present in the route manifest). `npm run lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. No browser available in this sandbox (Playwright/Chromium blocked) — the rendered UI was **not** visually verified; correctness was checked at the code/type level only (`tsc` catches JSX/prop-type errors even without rendering, and `next build` statically renders/prerenders during build).

## BIE self-eval: SPX-tool-calling Largo turns get their own calibration cohort — task #112 (branch `fix/bie-spx-tool-cohort-calibration`)

**Status:** SHIPPED. Direct follow-up to task #103 (merged to `main`), which added `bie_interactions.tools_used`/`intent_bucket` as groundwork but wired nothing into `bie/calibration.ts` — the self-eval loop this task closes.

**Root cause / motivation (gap, not a bug):** before this PR, `bie/calibration.ts` had two passes — `computeCalibration` (0DTE Command's `zerodte_setup_log`) and `computeSpxCalibration` (SPX Slayer's own closed-play P&L, `spx_play_outcomes`). Neither could answer "how good are Largo's ANSWERS specifically when SPX Slayer's own engine-state tools were involved" — that cohort didn't exist as a queryable slice of `bie_interactions` until task #103 gave rows a `tools_used`/`intent_bucket`, and nothing read them for calibration purposes. Grounding-verifier claim correctness (`claims_verified`/`claims_total`) says nothing about answer quality on its own — every numeric claim in an answer can be individually grounded/true while the answer still dispatches the wrong tool, misreads the SPX Slayer phase, or serves stale-but-technically-accurate state. Per the task brief, this closes that continuous-tracking gap for this specific cohort.

**Cohort-membership decision (documented per the task's explicit ask for judgment + rationale):**
- `SPX_ENGINE_TOOL_NAMES` (`src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts`) is a **narrower** list than `TOOL_GROUPS.spx_desk` — kept to the tools whose `run-tool.ts` implementation reads SPX Slayer's own live-engine state (`marketPlatform.spx.*`, or pure compute over the already-cached live desk / the engine's own lotto/power-hour evaluator output): `get_spx_structure`, `get_spx_play`, `get_open_plays`, `get_signal_log`, `get_lotto_state`, `get_lotto_live`, `get_setup_stats`, `get_trade_history`, `get_spx_confluence`, `get_power_hour`. Excluded, and verified via their `run-tool.ts` case bodies: `get_flow_tape`/`get_greek_flow`/`get_gex`/`get_group_greek_flow` — all take a generic `ticker`/`group` input and hit the same UW/Polygon providers used for ANY ticker (`get_greek_flow`/`get_gex` are literally shared with `TOOL_GROUPS.stock_analysis`), so a turn calling only those says nothing about SPX-Slayer-engine-state answer quality specifically. Also excluded `get_ecosystem_context` (`BIE_TOOL_NAMES`): it's cross-product/any-ticker, and `bie_interactions.tools_used` only records tool NAMES, never call inputs — there's no way to tell from a row alone whether a given call was scoped to SPX, so including it risks false-positive cohort membership. `tool-defs.test.ts` pins this as a verified subset of `spx_desk` plus an explicit exclusion check, so the cohort can't silently drift if `spx_desk`'s bundle composition changes for unrelated routing reasons.
- **Cohort test is a UNION, not a pure `tools_used` check** — this is the non-obvious part. `logBie()`'s router-answered branch (`largo-terminal.ts`, task #103) always records `tools_used: ["blackout_intelligence"]`, never the real tool name, even though the router's `spx_structure` intent (`composers.ts::composeSpxStructure`) internally calls `runLargoTool("get_spx_structure", {})` — the identical engine read a Claude-tool-calling turn would make. A pure `tools_used`-intersection test would therefore silently exclude EVERY deterministically-routed SPX-engine turn from the cohort by construction, which would make the router-vs-Claude-fallback ratio the task explicitly asks to track (`router_match_rate_pct`) read a permanent, meaningless 0% — not because BIE's router coverage is actually bad, but purely as an artifact of how `tools_used` is populated on that path. Fix: cohort membership = `tools_used ∩ SPX_ENGINE_TOOL_NAMES ≠ ∅` **OR** `intent_bucket === "spx_structure"`. Deliberately excludes the router's `zerodte_plays`/`ticker_play_state` intents (0DTE Command — a different product, already covered by `computeCalibration`) and `market_context` (broader SPX+SPY+QQQ+VIX context, not SPX Slayer's own engine state specifically).

**What was built (`src/lib/bie/calibration.ts`, following the file's own established "add a slice, don't rewrite the core" pattern — `computeSpxCalibration` was the precedent for how `computeCalibration` grew a second slice):**
- `computeSpxToolCallCalibration(rows, window)` — pure, exported, directly unit-tested (no DB mocking needed, same as its two siblings): reports `n` (cohort sample count), `claude_fallback_n`/`router_matched_n`/`router_match_rate_pct`, `grounding_pass_rate_pct` (aggregate `sum(claims_verified)/sum(claims_total)` over cohort rows that actually carried claims — weighted by claim count, not an unweighted per-row average), `avg_latency_ms`, and evidence-gated `recommendations` (same `MIN_EVIDENCE = 10` bar the other two passes already use).
- `formatSpxToolCallCalibration(r)` — human-readable summary, same convention as `formatSpxCalibration`.
- `CalibrationReport.spx_tool_calls: SpxToolCallCalibrationReport | null` — additive field, same attach-after-compute pattern as `spx_slayer`. `formatCalibration` now appends a third `---`-separated section when present; a report without it (e.g. any pre-existing caller) renders identically to before (regression-tested).
- `computeSpxToolCallCalibrationFromDb` (non-exported async orchestrator, mirrors `computeSpxSlayerCalibration`'s existing fail-open contract) + `fetchSpxToolCallingBieInteractions` (new, `src/lib/db.ts`) — wired into `runBieCalibration(days = 14)` alongside the existing two passes, same rolling window. Unlike the two existing fetchers (`fetchZeroDteSetupLogRange`/`fetchClosedPlayOutcomes`, both fetch-then-filter-in-JS on small, admission-gated tables), the cohort filter runs at the SQL layer (`tools_used ?| $2::text[] OR intent_bucket = 'spx_structure'`, Postgres `jsonb ?|` array-overlap operator) because `bie_interactions` is one row per Largo QUESTION — much higher volume — so pulling the whole 14-day window client-side to mostly discard it in JS would be wasteful.
- **Wiring, zero new surface needed:** `GET /api/admin/bie-report` already returns `{ data: calibration, text: formatCalibration(calibration) }`, and `AdminBieDashboard.tsx`'s "Gate calibration · 14 sessions" panel already renders `data?.calibration?.text` as raw `<pre>` text — so the new section appears automatically once `runBieCalibration` populates `spx_tool_calls`; no route or dashboard component change needed.

**Evidence (test run, this PR):**
- 9 new pure-math tests in `bie.test.ts` covering: cohort inclusion (`tools_used` intersection) / exclusion (generic-only tools); router-matched `spx_structure` rows joining the cohort despite the `["blackout_intelligence"]` sentinel (and a `zerodte_plays` router match correctly NOT joining); aggregate math over a mixed cohort (`sum(verified)/sum(total)` = 12/15 = 80%, weighted; avg latency = (4000+6000+40)/3 → 3347ms, rounded); claims_total=0 rows counted in `n` but excluded from the grounding ratio; evidence-gating (`n<10` → zero recommendations); recommendations firing once `n≥10` with low grounding/router-match rates; empty-cohort → `null` rates (not 0/NaN); 3-way combined-report text and the "no third section when unattached" regression.
- 4 new tests in `tool-defs.test.ts`: every `SPX_ENGINE_TOOL_NAMES` entry is a real `LARGO_TOOL_DEFS` tool, is a subset of `TOOL_GROUPS.spx_desk`, excludes the 4 generic tools by name, and has no duplicates.
- Node 22 (dev default): full suite unchanged pass/fail delta from `main` — confirmed by running the identical full suite with this PR's changes `git stash`'d out: **28 failures both with and without this PR's changes** (same files: `whop-revocation`, `ecosystem-context`, several `spx-signal-log-*` shadow tests, etc. — all pre-existing on `main`, unrelated to this change). With this PR's changes: 58/58 new-file-scoped tests pass (`bie.test.ts` + `tool-defs.test.ts`).
- Node 20 (CI's exact invocation — `nvm use 20`; `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"`): **1257/1257 passing, 0 failures** — the pre-existing 28 Node-22-only failures do not reproduce under Node 20 at all (unrelated to this PR either way).
- `npx tsc --noEmit`: clean. `npm run build`: clean. `npm run lint:brand` / `npm run lint:vendor`: clean.
- `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts`: empty — confirmed this PR never touches the live play-engine (per-task hard constraint).

**Fix rationale — why this design, what was deliberately left unchanged:** followed the file's existing precedent exactly (a third pure-function-plus-format-plus-orchestrator slice, not a rewrite of `computeCalibration`/`computeSpxCalibration`) so the three passes stay independently testable and independently failure-isolated (a bug in the new SPX-tool-calling fetch can never take down the 0DTE or SPX-outcomes sections — same `try {} catch { return null }` contract as `computeSpxSlayerCalibration`). Chose SQL-layer cohort filtering over the existing fetch-then-JS-filter pattern specifically because of `bie_interactions`' higher per-row volume (one row per question, not per graded setup/closed play) — a deliberate, documented departure from the two existing fetchers' pattern, not an oversight. Kept `SPX_ENGINE_TOOL_NAMES` as an explicit literal list rather than deriving it from `TOOL_GROUPS.spx_desk` (e.g. filtering out a "generic" tag) so the cohort can't silently widen/narrow if `spx_desk`'s bundle composition changes for unrelated system-prompt-routing reasons — `tool-defs.test.ts` pins the intended subset relationship instead. Left `MIN_EVIDENCE`, the grounding-ratio weighting convention, and the recommendation-threshold philosophy (< 70% grounding, < 30% router-match) matching the file's existing conventions rather than inventing new ones.

**Merge-time addendum (sibling-PR integration, applied while merging `main` into this branch):** task #108 (`spx_engine_snapshots` / `get_spx_engine_snapshots`, previous entry below) landed in parallel on a separate branch and was merged to `main` first, so this PR's `SPX_ENGINE_TOOL_NAMES` list was written before that tool existed and didn't include it. `get_spx_engine_snapshots` reads the identical class of engine-state data `get_signal_log` does (the throttled, gate-rejection-inclusive snapshot stream rather than the committed-only one) and is already a member of `TOOL_GROUPS.spx_desk`, so excluding it from the cohort would have been the same blind spot this PR's own `get_signal_log` inclusion was meant to close. Added it to `SPX_ENGINE_TOOL_NAMES` at merge time (one-line addition, all four existing `tool-defs.test.ts` invariants — real tool / subset-of-spx_desk / excludes-generics / no-dupes — still pass unmodified) rather than leaving the gap for a future PR to notice, since the two PRs' branches never saw each other's diff.

---

## 🧠 ADDED 2026-07-04 — `spx_engine_snapshots`: retrospective log of EVERY SPX play-engine tick, not just committed signals (task #108, branch `fix/spx-engine-snapshot-log`)

**Status:** SHIPPED (enhancement, not a bug fix — closes an observability gap, `computeSpxConfluence()`/`src/lib/spx-signals.ts` never touched, `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty, verified before opening this PR).

**Motivation / gap this closes:** `evaluateSpxPlay()` (`src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts`) only ever persists a signal via `maybeLogSpxPlay()` (`src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts`) when the engine actually COMMITS a BUY/SELL/TRIM — grep `maybeLogSpxPlay(` in that file: 6 call sites, all inside `evaluateOpenPlay`'s exit branches or `evaluateFlatPlay`'s BUY-commit path. Every OTHER tick — plain SCANNING with no setup, a gate-blocked entry (`entryGatesRaw.passed === false`), a Claude veto, a WATCHING/near-miss setup — hits a `return` with none of the `maybeLogSpxPlay` guards satisfied, so nothing is ever written for it. `evaluateSpxPlay` runs on every `mutate:true` poll (effectively every RTH minute — `spx-evaluator.ts`'s `runSpxEvaluator`), and the confluence score/gates/thesis that decided each of those non-committing ticks existed only in memory for the lifetime of that one request — the next tick overwrote it, with nothing durable left behind. "Why did SPX Slayer sit out that setup at 10:15" or "why was the last signal vetoed" was unanswerable after the fact from anywhere in the app; the only near-neighbor, `spx_signal_observations` (`src/lib/spx-signal-db.ts`'s `insertObservation`, written by the separate `spx-signal-observe` cron), deliberately ships `gates_blocked_json: []` with a comment reading "gate blocks are in spx-evaluate cron_job_runs" — i.e. that cron never calls the real gate layer (`evaluatePlayGates`) at all, it only calls the raw, gate-free `computeSpxConfluence()`, so it was never a substitute for this.

**What was built:**
- `spx_engine_snapshots` (new table, `src/lib/db.ts`, migrated under the existing `pg_advisory_lock(42)` migration path alongside `spx_confluence_shadow_observations`): `id`, `observed_at` (insert time), `session_date`, `phase`, `action`, `direction`, `score`, `gates_passed`, `gates_blocks` (JSONB array), `thesis`, `as_of` (the engine's own as-of timestamp, kept separate from `observed_at` so staleness and write-latency are distinguishable). A NEW table rather than widening `spx_signal_log`'s schema — a rejection/scan has no committed direction/entry/premium the way a real signal does, so forcing it into that row shape would mean a wall of nullable signal-only columns.
- `maybeLogSpxEngineSnapshot()` (`src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts`) — the write path, throttled via the SAME `platform_meta` getMeta/setMeta cursor idiom `maybeLogSpxPlay` already uses for its own `signal_key` above it in the same file, just keyed on a `{phase, action, direction, gates.blocks}` JSON tuple (`engineSnapshotStateKey`) instead of `maybeLogSpxPlay`'s action/direction signal key. Deliberately excludes score/thesis/headline from the throttle key — those jitter tick-to-tick on an otherwise-unchanged rejection/scan state (same reasoning `signalKey()`'s own doc comment gives for `maybeLogSpxPlay`), and including them would defeat the throttle by making almost every tick look "new." Writing unconditionally here (no throttle) would flood Postgres with a near-duplicate row every single poll tick while the engine idles unchanged — the explicit risk called out in the task.
- `fetchRecentSpxSnapshots(limit)` (`src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts`) + `fetchRecentSpxEngineSnapshots(limit)` (`src/lib/db.ts`) — the read path, `ORDER BY observed_at DESC`.
- Wiring into `evaluateSpxPlay`: the original function body was renamed to `evaluateSpxPlayCore` (private, unchanged internals — zero lines of gate/score/branch logic touched) and `evaluateSpxPlay` is now a thin exported wrapper that calls it, then fires `maybeLogSpxEngineSnapshot` (via the file's existing `firePlayTelemetry` fire-and-forget helper, same as every shadow factor) with the resulting payload's `phase`/`action`/`direction`/`score`/`thesis`/`headline`/`gates`/`as_of`, but ONLY when `options.mutate === true`. This single choke point observes EVERY exit path through `evaluateSpxPlayCore` (closed-session SCANNING, gate-blocked/Claude-vetoed SCANNING, WATCHING near-miss, committed OPEN/SELL) without needing a `maybeLogSpxEngineSnapshot` call inserted at each of that function's several `return` statements individually.
- New Largo tool `get_spx_engine_snapshots` (`src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts`, `run-tool.ts`, `TOOL_GROUPS.spx_desk`, `platform/spx-service.ts`'s `getSpxEngineSnapshots`) — explicitly disambiguated in its description from `get_signal_log` (committed-only) per the task's requirement: answers "why was the last signal rejected" / "what was the engine doing at time Y," which `get_signal_log`'s `spx_signal_log` table structurally cannot answer.

**Evidence this doesn't touch the real engine:** `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` is empty. `evaluateSpxPlayCore`'s body is a byte-for-byte move of the old `evaluateSpxPlay` body (only the function name + a doc comment changed); the new wrapper only ever reads fields off the already-computed return payload, never mutates it or feeds anything back into scoring/gating. `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite (`node --test`) 1253/1253 passing on BOTH Node 22 and Node 20 (`nvm use 20` + CI's exact glob-expansion invocation, per this repo's documented Node-20-vs-22 dynamic-`import()`-under-mocks divergence — the one new cross-module import this PR adds in production code, `maybeLogSpxEngineSnapshot` in `spx-play-engine.ts`, is a static top-of-file import for exactly this reason); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/db.ts` (+1 table, +2 functions, nothing existing touched), `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts` (+1 write function, +1 read function, +2 types, imports extended — every existing `maybeLogSpxPlay`/`logSpx*ShadowFactors` function byte-for-byte untouched), `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` (function renamed + thin wrapper added, one new static import — every line of actual gate/score/branch logic inside the renamed function untouched), `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` + `run-tool.ts` + `src/lib/platform/spx-service.ts` (+1 tool end to end). `get_signal_log` and its backing `fetchRecentSpxSignalLogs`/`spx_signal_log` were explicitly left alone per the task — this is a parallel, independent log, not a change to that path. Also left alone: `src/lib/spx-signal-db.ts`/`spx_signal_observations` and the `spx-signal-observe` cron — a legitimate sibling system with a different purpose (per-minute raw-confluence snapshots for signal-weight backtesting, gate-agnostic by design), not something this PR needed to fix or fold into.

**Fix rationale:** chose to wrap the whole `evaluateSpxPlay` function (rather than adding a `maybeLogSpxEngineSnapshot` call inline at each of the ~4 return points inside it) specifically so this PR's diff to the actual engine logic is zero lines — the wrapper is a pure, additive, one-choke-point observer, which is also easier for a future reader to verify never influences a live decision. Chose to key the throttle on `{phase, action, direction, gates.blocks}` (including `direction`, which the task's own wording didn't explicitly list alongside phase/action/gates.blocks) rather than the narrower 3-field set, because a direction flip with no other visible change (e.g. a bullish WATCHING setup turning bearish) is exactly the kind of transition "why was the engine watching/scanning at time Y" needs to see, and leaving it out of the key would silently collapse two materially different states into one logged row. Chose a brand-new table over widening `spx_signal_log` per the task's explicit direction, and because the two rows shapes are genuinely different (a rejection has no entry/stop/target/premium).

**Tests added:** `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log-engine-snapshot.test.ts` (9 cases, same `mock.module("../db", …)` / lazy-import idiom as every `spx-signal-log-*.test.ts` sibling) — db-not-configured short-circuit, first-tick insert shape (session_date/phase/action/direction/score/gates_passed/gates_blocks/thesis/as_of all asserted), the core throttle proof (an unchanged state on the next tick does NOT write a duplicate row even when score/thesis/headline jitter), a `gates.blocks` change firing a new row, a bare direction flip firing a new row, the throttle re-engaging immediately after a transition (no third row on a third identical tick), the thesis-falls-back-to-headline case, and both `fetchRecentSpxSnapshots` paths (db-not-configured empty array; delegates and returns newest-first). Given `evaluateSpxPlay`/`evaluateSpxPlayCore` has no existing test file in this repo (its dependency graph — ~20 modules including `spx-play-store`, `spx-play-claude`, `spx-play-mtf`, `db.ts` — has no precedent for a from-scratch integration test), this test suite directly exercises the new write function per the task's own documented fallback ("or directly unit-tests your new write function"), which is also how every sibling shadow-factor's own logging function is tested in this codebase (see `spx-signal-log-precedents.test.ts` et al.) — the wrapper wiring itself (renaming + a 15-line pass-through) was verified by code review plus the full existing suite staying green, since it introduces no new branching for a test to exercise.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite 1253/1253 passing (9 new) on Node 22 AND Node 20 (`nvm use 20` + CI's exact glob-expansion `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"` invocation). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` empty.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — Largo could reach for the wrong SPX tool: `get_spx_play`'s description gave Claude almost nothing to disambiguate against `get_market_regime` (task #110, Largo intent-routing sweep, medium)

**Where:** `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts` (`get_spx_play` ~line 194, `get_market_regime` ~line 397-400), `src/lib/largo/intent-keywords.ts` (`PLAY_STATE_RE` ~line 13-14), `src/lib/largo/question-intent.ts` (`analyzeLargoQuestion`, `LargoQuestionIntent`).

**Root cause:** Largo (`src/lib/largo-terminal.ts` → `anthropicToolLoop`) has no hard tool-selection gate — Claude picks a tool purely from its `description` string in `LARGO_TOOL_DEFS`. `get_spx_play`'s description was a single terse line, `"SPX play engine state."`, with zero detail on what fields it actually returns or when to prefer it. `get_market_regime`'s description, by contrast, was rich and explicitly invited "what's the market regime / what's the backdrop / is this a good environment for X" phrasing — language that overlaps in surface meaning with an engine-state question like "what phase/setup/bias is SPX Slayer in." With one tool under-described and the other tool's own wording pulling toward it, a bare engine-state question could plausibly get routed to the market-wide tool instead of the play-specific one. Compounding this, the hint layer (`analyzeLargoQuestion`) only nudged toward `get_spx_play` via `PLAY_STATE_RE`, which requires an explicit action/state word (buy/sell/hold/trim/play/setup/signal) alongside an SPX-like token — a bare phrasing like "what phase is the engine in right now" or "why did the play get rejected" matches neither that regex nor anything for `get_market_regime` (no dedicated regex existed for it at all), so the turn got zero routing guidance either way and fell entirely on the two tool descriptions to disambiguate — which, as above, they couldn't.

**Evidence:** confirmed the literal pre-fix strings — `get_spx_play`: `"SPX play engine state."` (tool-defs.ts line 194); `get_market_regime`: a 4-sentence description explicitly citing "is this a good environment for X" (tool-defs.ts lines 397-400). Confirmed `PLAY_STATE_RE` (`/\b(spx|s&p|0dte|sniper|lotto)\b.*\b(buy|sell|hold|trim|play|setup|signal)\b|\b(play state|open play|desk play)\b/i`) does not match either "what phase is SPX Slayer in right now" (no action/state word present) or "why did the play get rejected" (no SPX-like token present) — the new regression test `src/lib/largo/question-intent.test.ts` asserts `needsPlayState === false` for both. No dedicated regex existed for `get_market_regime` at all prior to this fix.

**Fix:** three additive changes, no gate/score logic touched: (1) rewrote `get_spx_play`'s description to the same depth as `get_ecosystem_context`'s (the existing quality bar for a rich Largo tool description) — now documents every real field `SpxPlayPayload` (`src/lib/spx-play-payload.ts`) returns (phase, action, direction, grade, score, confidence, factors, levels, gates.passed/blocks/warnings/entry_mode/play_idea, the AI arbiter's verdict, open_play, confirmations, technicals, mtf, option_ticket, watch, telemetry, lotto_play, power_play, session_phase, signal_committed — including the "a BUY action alone does NOT mean a position is live, wait for signal_committed" nuance) and states explicitly when to use it vs. `get_market_regime` (SPX Slayer's OWN play-engine state vs. market-wide backdrop that isn't specific to any one instrument) vs. `get_ecosystem_context` (which already embeds this exact object as `spx_full_state` for SPX/SPXW — mirroring how `get_ecosystem_context`'s own description already documents that same overlap from its side). (2) added a symmetric, two-way disambiguating clause to `get_market_regime`'s description: "NOT SPX Slayer's own play-engine state... for that, use get_spx_play (or get_ecosystem_context's spx_full_state field)." (3) added `SPX_ENGINE_STATE_RE`/`MARKET_REGIME_RE` to `intent-keywords.ts` and `needsSpxEngineState`/`needsMarketRegime` to `LargoQuestionIntent`/`analyzeLargoQuestion`, following the exact existing `NIGHTHAWK_RE`/`needsNightHawk` pattern (new regex → new boolean → new `toolHints.push`, no restructuring) — an engine-state-flavored question (phase/setup/bias/confluence/gate(s)/veto/reject(ed/ion) wording next to an spx/s&p/0dte/sniper/slayer token, or "play ... reject/veto" standing alone) now hints `get_spx_play` directly; a market-wide-flavored question (regime/backdrop/environment/playbook wording) now hints `get_market_regime` directly.

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts`, `src/lib/largo/intent-keywords.ts`, `src/lib/largo/question-intent.ts` only — `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` is empty (confirmed before opening this PR); no scoring/gating math touched anywhere. `get_confluence_outcomes`'s description (which also references `get_spx_play` for a single play's own grade) was left as-is — it already correctly deferred to `get_spx_play` and needed no change.

**Fix rationale:** extended the existing hint system (a new RegExp pair + two new booleans + two `toolHints.push` calls) rather than restructuring `analyzeLargoQuestion` or adding a hard tool-selection gate — per this task's explicit scope, this is a description/hint-quality fix, not a new routing mechanism, and Largo's tool selection is deliberately soft everywhere else too. Chose to let "play ... reject/veto" match on its own inside `SPX_ENGINE_STATE_RE`, without also requiring an SPX-like token, because the play engine is the only thing on the desk with gate-block reasoning to explain — "why did the play get rejected" is unambiguous even without an explicit spx/sniper/0dte token, and requiring one would have reproduced the exact gap this fix closes for that phrasing.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean on both Node 22 and Node 20. Full suite: 1247/1247 passing on Node 22 and again on Node 20 (`nvm use 20`; CI's exact `node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"` invocation) — 3 new tests in `src/lib/largo/question-intent.test.ts` (new file; `analyzeLargoQuestion` had zero prior test coverage). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.
