## 🧠 SPX Slayer shadow signal: BIE precedent-search agreement SHIPPED 2026-07-04 — the 6th shadow factor, made possible by today's `alert_audit_log.outcome` propagation fix (branch `feat/spx-shadow-precedents`)

**Status:** SHIPPED. Not one of the originally-planned 5 shadow factors (flow anomalies, risk-reversal skew/realized vol, macro predictions, mega-cap catalysts, ecosystem cross-instrument agreement — all shipped earlier today, see their entries below) — this is a 6th, added because `src/lib/bie/alert-outcome-sync.ts` (this file's own earlier entry, "`alert_audit_log.outcome` was NEVER written by anything") just unblocked BIE's `get_similar_precedents` tool for the first time. Before that fix, `findSimilarPrecedents()` (`src/lib/bie/precedent-search.ts`) had zero graded rows to ever return — building a shadow factor on top of it earlier would have had nothing to score. Same non-negotiable contract as every sibling: shadow-only, `computeSpxConfluence()` (`src/lib/spx-signals.ts`) never touched.

**Motivation:** `get_similar_precedents` ("has a setup like this happened before, and what happened") already exists for Largo's tool-calling model, but SPX Slayer's own engine never asked that question about its own current setup. This factor is what happens when the engine does: query the precedent store for similar historical SPX-relevant setups (0DTE Command, Night Hawk, and SPX Slayer's own `spx_claude_play` alerts all feed the same `alert_audit_log` table) and derive a provisional weight from how they actually resolved — same `bie/calibration.ts` `MIN_EVIDENCE=10` "report first, prove it before it can move score" bar every sibling factor already holds itself to.

**What was built:**
- `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-precedents.ts` (new file) — pure functions only, no DB/fetch/bare clock read (`git grep spx-signals-shadow-precedents src/lib/spx-signals.ts` returns nothing, confirming the "cannot touch the live score" guarantee by inspection).
  - `buildPrecedentSearchQuery(desk, direction, grade, score)` — composes a short natural-language description of the CURRENT setup (e.g. `"SPX 0DTE setup, long, B conviction (score 62), mean_revert gamma regime"`) in the same register `describeAuditRow()` (precedent-search.ts) uses for the descriptions being searched, per that file's own documented retrieval-quality advice. Omits gamma regime when `"unknown"` rather than embedding it as a fact.
  - `parsePrecedentDirection`/`parsePrecedentOutcome` — a retrieved precedent (`RetrievedChunk`) carries only free text (`chunk`) and a similarity score, no structured direction/outcome columns, so these two pure parsers read those two facts back out of `describeAuditRow()`'s deterministic (never LLM-generated) template: `"${kind} alert on ${ticker}, ${direction}..."` and the trailing `"Outcome: ${outcome}."` clause. Confirmed via a repo-wide grep of every `insertAlertAuditLog`/`direction:` call site that `"long"`/`"short"` is the real platform-wide vocabulary today (0DTE, Night Hawk, `spx_claude_play` all write it) — `"bullish"`/`"bearish"` matched defensively for any future alert type, anything else degrades to `"neutral"`, never fabricated.
  - `computePrecedentShadowFactor(precedents, searchConfirmedAvailable, confluenceDirection)` — two independent honesty gates before any weight is computed: (1) `searchConfirmedAvailable` (the caller's `bieEmbeddingsConfigured()` read — see below) → `available:false` when not confirmed, mirroring every sibling's staleness-guard discipline; (2) `MIN_TOTAL_PRECEDENTS = 3` (a simple majority of `PRECEDENT_SEARCH_K = 5`, Largo's own `get_similar_precedents(query, 5)` call shape) — fewer total precedents returned than that floor is **also** `available:false`, this factor's explicit "not enough precedents yet, honestly represented" state, since the corpus is expected to be near-empty right now (today's outcome-propagation fix just started backfilling it). Once both gates clear, precedents whose OWN direction matches `confluenceDirection` are tallied by resolution (`target` = evidence FOR continuing that direction, `stop` = evidence AGAINST; opposite-direction/no-direction/`ambiguous`/`unfilled` precedents count toward the total but aren't tallied either way). The net for/against tally maps to a signed weight via the CURRENT direction's own sign (bullish=+1/bearish=-1) — **not** the tally's raw sign directly, since "evidence for continuing SHORT" is a bearish (negative) lean even though the tally itself is positive; a dedicated regression test guards this exact sign-conflation bug. Weight tiers (3/5/8, deliberately capped well below the engine's own ±18 ceiling — this is the single least-proven factor in the family, hours old as of shipping) require `usable >= 2` directionally-informative precedents before reaching above the family floor (3), so one lone data point can never read as "near-unanimous."
- Wiring: `logSpxPrecedentsShadowFactor(desk, confluence)` in `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts` — calls `findSimilarPrecedents(query, PRECEDENT_SEARCH_K)` (`src/lib/bie/precedent-search.ts`) directly, gated on `bieEmbeddingsConfigured()` (`src/lib/bie/embeddings.ts`) as the best available "the search could even have run" proxy — `searchKnowledge()` (bie/knowledge.ts) fails open to `[]` on three indistinguishable conditions (not configured / genuinely nothing found / internal error), the same class of honest, documented limitation `logMegaCapCatalystShadowFactors` already accepts for `polygonConfigured()`. Called from `evaluateSpxPlay` in `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` immediately after `logMegaCapCatalystShadowFactors`, same `firePlayTelemetry` fire-and-forget idiom, same pre-Night-Hawk-bonus score/grade/direction snapshot the ecosystem sibling already established a precedent for passing.

**PROOF THIS DOES NOT CHANGE LIVE SIGNALS:** `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts src/lib/providers/spx-desk.ts` is **empty** — verified explicitly before opening this PR. Deliberately NOT wired through `SpxDeskPayload`/`buildSpxDesk()`, same reasoning every sibling factor already established: this only needs to run once per `evaluateSpxPlay` tick, not on the hot member-facing desk-poll path. `logSpxPrecedentsShadowFactor` is only ever invoked via `firePlayTelemetry`'s fire-and-forget wrapper — an exception inside is caught/logged, never thrown into the caller.

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts` (one new exported function + 3 new imports; every existing `logSpx*ShadowFactors` function untouched), `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` (one new import + one new fire-and-forget call in `evaluateSpxPlay`, nothing else touched), and 2 new files. No `db.ts` change — reuses the existing `insertShadowFactorObservation`/`spx_confluence_shadow_observations` table as-is (`factor_name: "precedent_search_agreement"` is a new discriminator value, no schema change). `findSimilarPrecedents`/`bieEmbeddingsConfigured` themselves are unmodified, read-only consumers (one more caller alongside Largo's `get_similar_precedents` tool case in `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts`, whose exact `(query, 5)` call shape this factor reuses).

**Fix rationale:** chose to gate on total-precedents-returned (`MIN_TOTAL_PRECEDENTS`) rather than only gating on usable (same-direction, cleanly-resolved) precedents, so "the corpus is still near-empty" (expected, harmless) and "the corpus has data but none of it happens to match this specific direction" (a real, `available:true`/neutral reading, same as the ecosystem sibling's own "no bias to compare" case) are represented as two honestly-different states, not collapsed into one. Chose to parse direction/outcome back out of the retrieved chunk's free text (rather than, say, threading a second BIE query for structured columns) because `describeAuditRow()`'s template is deterministic and template-generated, never LLM-authored — a stable, testable contract, not NLP guessing over arbitrary prose.

**Tests added:** `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-precedents.test.ts` (22 cases — direction/outcome parsing including the platform-wide `"long"`/`"short"` vocabulary and defensive `"bullish"`/`"bearish"` matching, query-builder gamma-regime-omission, both honesty gates (`searchConfirmedAvailable=false` and `MIN_TOTAL_PRECEDENTS`), no-bias and no-usable-evidence neutral states, all three weight tiers, the `usable<2` floor-cap guard, a tied-net neutral case, opposite-direction precedents never counting as usable, and the short/bearish sign-conflation regression case). `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log-precedents.test.ts` (6 cases — DB-not-configured and embeddings-not-configured short-circuits (with a call-count assertion proving the search is skipped, not just its result discarded), the exact query/k passed to `findSimilarPrecedents`, the too-few-precedents `available:false` path, a real signed bullish observation, and the short-bias negative-weight regression case).

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite `npm test` — 1219/1219 passing (28 new: 22 + 6). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🧠 ADDED 2026-07-04 — `bie_interactions` now persists `tools_used` + `intent_bucket` (task #103, groundwork for #112's BIE self-eval loop; enhancement, not a bug fix)

**Motivation:** task #112 (tracked separately) plans to route Largo turns through BIE's calibration/self-eval loop (`src/lib/bie/calibration.ts`) the same way 0DTE/SPX Slayer outcomes already are — but that loop can only learn from a turn if it knows what ACTUALLY happened on it. `bie_interactions` (the interaction/outcome ledger `src/lib/db.ts`'s `insertBieInteraction()` writes, read by `fetchBieInteractionStats()` for the daily self-eval report) already recorded `question`/`intent`/`answer_source`/`claims_total`/`claims_verified`/`latency_ms` per turn, but never which Largo tools were actually dispatched (`tools_used`), and the pre-existing `intent` column conflates two different meanings of NULL (never set vs. "the router genuinely fell through to Claude"). This PR is pure groundwork — it makes the data available; #112 is the separate PR that will consume it.

**Where:**
- `src/lib/db.ts` — `bie_interactions` schema block (`ensureSchema()`, next to the existing `CREATE TABLE`/index for this table) gets two `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` statements, the same idempotent idiom every other post-launch column in this file uses (e.g. `zerodte_setup_log`'s `entry_premium`/`plan_json`/etc. additions just above it). `insertBieInteraction()`'s row type/SQL/params extended to match.
- `src/lib/bie/router.ts` — new exported pure function `bieIntentBucket(intent: BieIntent | null): string`.
- `src/lib/largo-terminal.ts` — `logBie()`'s row type extended; its 4 call sites (the router-hit and Claude-fallback branches inside both `runLargoQuery` and `runLargoQueryStream`) now pass the real values.

**What changed:**
1. Two new columns on `bie_interactions`: **`tools_used JSONB DEFAULT '[]'::jsonb`** — same JSONB-array idiom `largo_messages.tools_used` already uses one table over (`db.ts` ~line 458), not a Postgres `TEXT[]` (this schema has no existing `TEXT[]` column to match, and JSONB is the established precedent for "list of tool names" here). **`intent_bucket TEXT`** — additive alongside the pre-existing `intent` column, which is left completely unchanged in meaning (still the raw router intent name, or `NULL` on fallback — zero existing reader touched). `intent_bucket` is the new, always-populated field: the real intent name when the router matched deterministically, or the explicit sentinel `"claude_fallback"` when it fell through — computed by the new `bieIntentBucket()` in `router.ts` (`intent ?? "claude_fallback"`), so the null→sentinel mapping lives in one pure, tested place rather than being re-derived at each of the 4 call sites.
2. `insertBieInteraction()`'s INSERT now includes `tools_used` (bound as `$8::jsonb`, run through the existing `toJsonbParam()` helper — **not** a bare array bind, which node-postgres serializes as a Postgres ARRAY-literal string, not JSON; see the `alert_audit_log` P0 this repo already hit for that exact bug class) and `intent_bucket` (bound as plain `$9`).
3. `logBie()`'s 4 call sites now pass real data instead of nothing: the two router-hit branches pass `tools_used: ["blackout_intelligence"]` (the router never calls a Largo tool — it composes straight from platform truth) and `intent_bucket: bieIntentBucket(routed.route.intent)`; the two Claude-fallback branches pass `tools_used: Array.from(new Set(toolsUsed))` (the SAME deduped array already persisted to `largo_messages.tools_used` a few lines below via `appendLargoMessage` — reused, not re-derived) and `intent_bucket: bieIntentBucket(null)` (`"claude_fallback"`).

**Blast radius:** purely additive — no existing column, router, or run-tool dispatch logic changed. Grepped every consumer of `insertBieInteraction`'s type signature before touching it: exactly one call site (`logBie()` in `largo-terminal.ts`), all 4 invocations updated together. `fetchBieInteractionStats()` (the only other reader of this table) is untouched — it doesn't select the new columns, so it can't regress; #112 is the PR that will extend it to use them.

**Fix rationale:** matched two different existing idioms deliberately rather than inventing a third — `tools_used`'s type/cast mirrors `largo_messages.tools_used` (the only other "list of tool names" column in this schema) instead of a novel `TEXT[]`; `intent_bucket`'s ALTER-TABLE-IF-NOT-EXISTS migration matches the exact pattern already used for every other post-launch column on `zerodte_setup_log` a few lines above it in the same file. Left the pre-existing `intent` column's semantics untouched rather than repurposing it, so nothing that already reads `intent` (there are no other readers today, but the column ships with a documented, stable meaning) can silently start seeing a different value.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. New tests: `src/lib/bie/bie.test.ts` (+2 — `bieIntentBucket` passes a matched intent through unchanged; maps `null` to `"claude_fallback"`). New file `src/lib/largo-terminal.test.ts` (this module had zero test coverage before — mocks the provider/DB boundary, same `mock.module` pattern `run-tool.test.ts` established, including stubbing `largo/spx-desk-cache` to avoid a transitive `server-only` load) with 4 end-to-end tests driving `runLargoQuery`/`runLargoQueryStream` for both a deterministic router turn (`"How are today's plays doing?"` → `intent_bucket: "zerodte_plays"`, `tools_used: ["blackout_intelligence"]`) and a Claude-fallback turn (a reasoning-shaped question the router's own `REASONING_RE` guard rejects → `intent_bucket: "claude_fallback"`, `tools_used` = the real mocked-tool-loop's dispatched names, `intent` still `null`) — asserting on the exact row handed to a mocked `insertBieInteraction`. Full suite `npm test`: **1197/1197 passing**. `npm run build`, `npx tsc --noEmit`, `npm run lint:brand`, `npm run lint:vendor` all clean.

---

## 🟢 ADDED 2026-07-04 — `get_confluence_outcomes` now correlates SPX Slayer's shadow confluence factors against its own real graded outcomes (task #122, enhancement — data-analysis plumbing, not a new gating decision)

**Motivation:** `confluence-outcomes.ts` already answered "does agreeing with Night Hawk actually help 0DTE Command's hit rate" (`computeConfluenceOutcomeStats` / `bucketConfluenceRows`). SPX Slayer has been logging six families of SHADOW-MODE confluence factors into `spx_confluence_shadow_observations` since PR #464 and its 5 siblings (`risk_reversal_skew`, `realized_vs_implied_vol`, `flow_anomaly_*`, `megacap_catalyst_*`, `ecosystem_zerodte_agreement`/`ecosystem_spx_anomaly_*`, `macro_prediction_consensus` — see `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow*.ts`), each candidate factor tagged with the REAL `computeSpxConfluence()` score/grade at the same instant "for later correlation against actual outcomes" (that table's own `db.ts` module comment). Nothing had ever read that table back out. Meanwhile `spx_play_outcomes` now carries real win/loss/breakeven grades for every closed SPX Slayer play, and `alert_audit_log.outcome` was recently wired up for `spx_claude_play` rows too (PR #459). This is the evidence layer `bie/calibration.ts`'s `MIN_EVIDENCE = 10` "prove it before acting on it" philosophy (explicitly cited by `spx-signals-shadow.ts`'s own module doc) requires before any shadow factor could ever be reviewed for promotion into `computeSpxConfluence()`'s live scoring — until this PR, that promotion decision had literally no data to look at.

**Where:** `src/lib/bie/confluence-outcomes.ts` (new exports, existing exports untouched), `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts`'s `get_confluence_outcomes` case, `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts`'s `get_confluence_outcomes` description.

**Source-of-truth decision (the non-obvious part):** correlates shadow observations against `spx_play_outcomes` **directly**, not through `alert_audit_log.outcome` a second time. `db.ts`'s `fetchSpxClaudePlayOutcomeForAudit` doc already explains why `alert_audit_log.source_key` for `spx_claude_play` rows carries no FK into `spx_play_outcomes` (a verdict is logged BEFORE the engine decides whether to open a play, so there's nothing to key on yet) — that function already re-derives the join by `(direction, price, time window)` against `spx_play_outcomes`, then copies the result onto `alert_audit_log` for a completely different consumer (`get_similar_precedents`'s precedent corpus). Reading `alert_audit_log` here would mean re-deriving that exact same fuzzy match a SECOND time, one hop further from the real ledger, and filtered down to only whatever `alert-outcome-sync.ts`'s periodic cron has already visited — `spx_play_outcomes` is the actual system-of-record `spx-play-outcomes.ts`'s `classifyOutcome()` writes to, so joining straight to it is more direct, more complete, and always current.

**Join/aggregation logic implemented:**
1. `SELECT DISTINCT factor_name FROM spx_confluence_shadow_observations WHERE available = true AND observed_at >= NOW() - windowDays` — the full set of factor_names actually in observation, independent of whether any of them ever matched a play. `available = true` only: `available: false` means "the underlying read couldn't be confirmed fresh," never "confirmed no signal" (every shadow factor's own module doc is explicit about this), so an unavailable tick carries no real reading and must not be counted either way.
2. For each closed, gradeable SPX Slayer play (`spx_play_outcomes.outcome IN ('win','loss','breakeven')` — `open`/`superseded` excluded exactly like `alert-outcome-sync.ts`'s `mapSpxPlayOutcome` treats them, "leave alone," never a real trade result), `JOIN LATERAL` to the single shadow observation **per factor_name** closest in time to that play's `opened_at`, within a ±30-minute window (`DISTINCT ON (factor_name)`, ordered by `ABS(EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM (observed_at - opened_at)))`). The ±30-minute window mirrors two existing precedents for the identical "still fresh enough to mean something" reasoning already in this codebase: `fetchSpxClaudePlayOutcomeForAudit`'s own window and `spx-signals-shadow.ts`'s `ANOMALY_WINDOW_MS`. Symmetric (not "most recent before") because shadow-factor logging and the play-open DB write are two independent fire-and-forget calls inside the same `evaluateSpxPlay` tick (`spx-play-engine.ts`) — either can land at the DB first, so ordering can't be assumed.
3. **Why one row per (play, factor_name), not one row per observation tick — the part most likely to get wrong:** shadow factors are logged on every `evaluateSpxPlay` tick (`spx-signal-log.ts`), so a single SPX Slayer play open for an hour could have dozens of raw observations for the same factor, all carrying the SAME eventual outcome. Counting every tick as independent "evidence" would let one trade masquerade as 10+ samples against the very `MIN_EVIDENCE = 10` bar this whole exercise exists to feed — a single lucky/unlucky trade could fake reaching the evidence threshold on its own. Collapsing to the nearest-to-entry reading per play fixes the unit of evidence at "one trade = one vote," matching what the `MIN_EVIDENCE` gate actually means elsewhere in this codebase (`bie/calibration.ts` buckets by trade, never by tick).
4. `bucketShadowFactorEvidence(factorNames, evidenceRows)` (pure, unit-tested without a DB) then classifies each evidence row's agreement — `classifyShadowFactorAgreement`: a shadow factor's `direction` (`"bullish"|"bearish"|"neutral"`, every `spx-signals-shadow*.ts` factor's shared vocabulary) vs. the play's own `direction` (`"long"|"short"`, `spx-play-engine.ts`) — into `agree` / `disagree` / `neutral` (a `neutral` factor reading makes no directional claim, so it can't agree or disagree with anything; kept separate exactly like `bucketConfluenceRows`' existing `no_echo` bucket is kept separate from `agree`/`disagree` for the SAME reason, just a different vocabulary pair — this one is a genuine cross-product translation, not a casing quirk). Every `factor_name` gets all 3 buckets in the output even with zero matched evidence (`n: 0`, every stat `null`, `insufficient_sample: true`) — the honest "no evidence yet" case a brand-new shadow factor must show, never silently omitted (indistinguishable from "checked, found nothing interesting") and never backfilled with a fabricated number.

**Blast radius:** `computeConfluenceOutcomeStats`'s existing return type/behavior is completely unchanged (verified: `src/app/api/admin/bie-report/route.ts`'s direct call site needs no change) — the new `computeSpxSlayerShadowFactorOutcomeStats` is a separate, additive export. Only the Largo **tool** surface (`get_confluence_outcomes`'s `run-tool.ts` case) changes shape, now returning `{ zerodte_nighthawk_echo, spx_slayer_shadow_factors }` instead of a bare array — that tool's description in `tool-defs.ts` was updated to describe both sections so a model consuming it isn't surprised. `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` is empty — `computeSpxConfluence()` and every shadow factor's own scoring function are untouched, per this task's explicit read-only/additive-only scope.

**Fix rationale — what was deliberately left unchanged:** did not fold this into `bie/calibration.ts` (SPX Slayer already has its own separate closed-play calibration pass there, `computeSpxCalibration`, unrelated to shadow factors) and did not wire an automatic promotion path from "a factor cleared `MIN_EVIDENCE`" into `computeSpxConfluence()`'s scoring — this task is explicitly the evidence-gathering layer only; a human reviews the numbers this tool surfaces and ships a separate, reviewed PR if a factor earns its way in, matching every other "report-first" precedent in this codebase (`bie/calibration.ts`'s own recommendations are report-only for the identical reason).

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite **1205/1205 passing** — 21 new tests added to `src/lib/bie/confluence-outcomes.test.ts`: `classifyShadowFactorAgreement`'s 4 direction combinations + neutral; `mapShadowFactorEvidenceRows`' NUMERIC-string `pnl_pts` conversion, null handling, and unrecognized-direction defensive narrowing; `bucketShadowFactorEvidence`'s 10+-sample real win-rate/avg-pnl computation (insufficient_sample clears), the honest zero-evidence case for a factor_name with no matched plays yet (all 3 buckets, all nulls, flagged), independent agree/disagree tracking, a factor_name surfaced from evidence rows alone, and breakeven counting in the denominator without ever counting as a win. `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## ✅ VERIFIED CORRECT 2026-07-04 — task #121: every SPX Slayer shadow confluence factor already has a real staleness/availability guard; no fabricated-neutral gap found

**Scope:** task #121 asked whether every SPX Slayer shadow-mode confluence factor (the parallel, zero-live-effect scoring pipeline that logs what a candidate factor WOULD have contributed, per `spx-signals-shadow.ts`'s own module doc and `bie/calibration.ts`'s `MIN_EVIDENCE=10` "prove it before it can move score/action/grade" precedent) correctly returns `available: false` whenever its underlying data is stale/missing/unconfirmed, rather than ever fabricating `available: true, weight: 0` (which must mean ONLY "checked, genuinely nothing found," never "couldn't check"). All 5 shadow-factor modules and their `*.test.ts` files were read in full — pure scorers AND their async caller wiring in `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts` — specifically hunting for a `try/catch` that swallows a fetch failure and defaults to a neutral/available reading instead of propagating unavailability. **Conclusion: no gap found in any of the 5. Every factor's stale/unavailable path is real, and every one has an explicit test asserting `available === false` on that path (not just a happy-path test).** No code changes were needed; this PR is docs-only.

**Per-factor audit (file:line references against `main`@`3b8be50`):**

1. **`src/lib/spx-signals-shadow.ts` (`flow_anomaly_*`)** — `computeShadowFactors()` (line 146) takes `flowFeedFresh: boolean` as an explicit parameter, not inferred from an empty `anomalies` array; when `!flowFeedFresh` it returns `available:false` unconditionally (lines 154–165), before ever looking at `anomalies`. The caller, `logSpxShadowFactors()` in `spx-signal-log.ts` (line 121), sources `flowFeedFresh` from `isFlowFrameFreshAnywhere()` (`src/lib/flow-liveness.ts:104`) — verified that function's own `try { ... } catch { return false; }` (lines 105–111) fails CLOSED (returns `false`, i.e. "not fresh," not `true`) on any Redis/parse error, so a downstream infra failure can never masquerade as a confirmed-fresh feed. Test: `spx-signals-shadow.test.ts:27` (`"stale/missing feed — available:false regardless of what anomalies contains"`) asserts `available === false` for both a real anomaly and an empty array under `flowFeedFresh=false`, and asserts the two collapse to `deepEqual` observations — proving the down-feed case can't be distinguished from (or hidden behind) a real zero.

2. **`src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-skew.ts` (`risk_reversal_skew`, `realized_vs_implied_vol`)** — both `computeSkewShadowFactor()` (line 162) and `computeVolDivergenceShadowFactor()` (line 225) gate on `reading == null OR reading's own date is older than HISTORICAL_ROW_MAX_AGE_MS` (5 calendar days — line 100), returning `available:false` with a distinct detail string for "no data" vs. "stale row" (lines 169–178, 232–241). These are once-daily historical UW series, so freshness is keyed off each row's OWN `date`/`as_of_date` field, not a live heartbeat — correctly different discipline from factor 1, as the task hypothesized. The caller (`resolveSkewReading()`/`resolveVolDivergenceReading()`, `spx-signal-log.ts:295–354`) wraps every UW/Polygon fetch in `.catch(() => [])`/`.catch(() => null)` — a fetch failure collapses to the same `null`/empty-row shape as "no data returned," which `parseLatestRiskReversalSkew`/`parseLatestRealizedVol`/`parseLatestImpliedVol` (`src/lib/nighthawk/vol-metrics.ts`) correctly turn into `null` (never a fabricated 0), which the factor functions then correctly read as `available:false`. Tests: `spx-signals-shadow-skew.test.ts:25` (null reading) and `:34` (stale reading, distinct detail from null) for skew; `:91` (null) and `:100` (stale) for vol-divergence — both null AND stale are separately covered, not just one.

3. **`src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-catalysts.ts` (`megacap_catalyst_*`)** — `computeCatalystShadowFactors()` (line 156) takes `catalystFetchOk: boolean` as an explicit parameter (the module doc, lines 132–152, is explicit about why: `fetchBenzingaCatalysts` itself swallows its own fetch errors and returns `[]`, so it cannot distinguish "no catalysts" from "the fetch broke"). `available:false` fires when there are no `leader_stocks` to scope a check to at all (lines 164–174) OR when `!catalystFetchOk` (lines 176–187), regardless of what `catalysts` contains. The caller (`logMegaCapCatalystShadowFactors`, `spx-signal-log.ts:472`) passes `polygonConfigured()` as `catalystFetchOk` — the documented, honest limitation is that a configured-but-transiently-failing fetch still reads as "no catalysts found" (same as every other consumer of that fetcher today), which is called out explicitly in-code rather than hidden. Test: `spx-signals-shadow-catalysts.test.ts:35` asserts `available:false` for `catalystFetchOk=false` with real vs. empty catalysts producing `deepEqual` observations, plus `:26` for the no-leaders case.

4. **`src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-ecosystem.ts` (`ecosystem_zerodte_agreement`, `ecosystem_spx_anomaly_*`)** — `deriveEcosystemShadowFactors()` (line 260) applies a single blanket `!ctx.flow_feed_fresh` gate (lines 264–271) that forces BOTH factors to `available:false` together, including `zerodte_today` even though that field isn't itself HELIX flow data — the conservative "when BIE can't vouch for its own read, trust nothing it returned" choice the module doc argues for. `flow_feed_fresh` itself comes from `fetchEcosystemContext()` (`src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts:318`), which I verified fails closed: its outer `try/catch` (lines 322–443) returns `emptyContext(ticker)` on ANY internal error, and `emptyContext()` (line 219) hardcodes `flow_feed_fresh: false` (line 229) — an exception during any of the 8 parallel queries blanks the WHOLE context to "not fresh," never a partial success that could leave `flow_feed_fresh` stuck at a stale `true`. Test: `spx-signals-shadow-ecosystem.test.ts:76` asserts both factors are `available:false` with `flow_feed_fresh:false` even when real `zerodte_today`/`recent_anomalies` data is present, plus `:186` covers the same at the async-wrapper level (mocking `fetchEcosystemContext` itself).

5. **`src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-predictions.ts` (macro predictions)** — `computeMacroPredictionsShadowFactor()` (line 257) correctly distinguishes THREE states, not two: (a) outside any macro window → `available:true, weight:0`, "not applicable" (lines 265–276) — a confirmed state, not a data problem; (b) inside/near a window but `!consensusFresh || consensusSignals == null` → `available:false` (lines 285–295); (c) inside/near a window with a real, fresh read → scored normally. `consensusFresh` is derived by the caller's `fetchMacroPredictionsConsensusCached()` (`spx-signal-log.ts:201`) from UW's `raw_counts` (all four prediction endpoints — insiders/smart-money/unusual/whales — returning zero rows in total is treated as an outage, not a real empty market: `rawTotal > 0` gates `fresh`, line 216), wrapped in `.catch(() => null)` so an unexpected throw also collapses to `fresh:false` rather than propagating or silently defaulting `fresh:true`. Verified `fetchUwPredictionsConsensus`/`uwGetSafe` (`src/lib/providers/unusual-whales.ts`) never throw on a real fetch failure (403/429/network errors are all caught internally and degrade to `null`/`[]`) — the `.catch()` is correct defense-in-depth, not compensating for a real gap. Tests: `spx-signals-shadow-predictions.test.ts:95` (outside window → "not applicable", distinct from stale/missing) and `:104` (inside window, `consensusFresh=false` → `available:false`, `deepEqual` against a `consensusSignals=null` variant) — all three states are exercised, not just two.

**Caller-level (wiring) tests, checked in addition to the per-factor pure-function tests above:** `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log-{shadow,skew,catalyst-shadow,shadow-ecosystem,macro-predictions}.test.ts` each additionally cover the async fetch/DB-wiring layer, including simulated outages — e.g. `spx-signal-log-macro-predictions.test.ts:206` ("UW fetch throws (simulated outage) — caught, persists `available:false` rather than propagating"), `spx-signal-log-skew.test.ts:197` ("both Polygon and UW vol sources unavailable — persists `available:false`"), `spx-signal-log-catalyst-shadow.test.ts:106` ("Polygon not configured — no fetch attempted, persists a single `available:false` observation"). Ran all 10 files together: **94/94 passing**, all `available:false` assertions confirmed green (`node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test` against the 5 shadow modules + their 5 `spx-signal-log-*` caller test files).

**Why no fix branch:** the standing issue-handling policy opens a `fix/<slug>` branch only when a real issue is found. This audit found none — every factor already has the "propagate unavailability, never fabricate neutral" discipline the task hypothesized was already in place from the PRs that built each factor (feat/spx-shadow-signal-framework, feat/spx-shadow-skew-vol, feat/spx-shadow-catalysts, feat/spx-shadow-ecosystem-context, feat/spx-shadow-predictions-macro), so this is a docs-only PR closing out task #121 with evidence rather than a code change.

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — this PR's own `getSpxPlayState()` addition to `ecosystem-context.ts` broke every sibling shadow-factor test file's module load (`server-only` crash), platform-wide (BIE/Largo integration sweep, high — caught in local verification before merge, not shipped)

**Where:** `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log-catalyst-shadow.test.ts`, `-macro-predictions.test.ts`, `-shadow-ecosystem.test.ts`, `-shadow.test.ts`, `-skew.test.ts` — every test file that exercises ANY function inside `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts`.

**Root cause:** this PR adds `import { getSpxPlayState } from "@/lib/platform/spx-service";` to `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts` so `spx_full_state` can reuse Largo's own play-engine call verbatim. `ecosystem-context.ts` is itself imported by `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-ecosystem.ts` (PR #469, already merged), which is statically imported at the TOP of `spx-signal-log.ts` alongside every other shadow factor's own module (skew/vol, catalysts, macro-predictions, flow-anomalies). Because all five shadow factors now live in one file with one shared static-import block, loading `spx-signal-log.ts` for ANY test — even one that only exercises `logMegaCapCatalystShadowFactors` and mocks none of the ecosystem chain — unconditionally executes `ecosystem-context.ts` → `platform/spx-service.ts` → the full `spx-play-engine.ts` chain, several hops deep of which has a real `import "server-only"` (the same marker package `largo/run-tool.test.ts` already has to stub). Node's `--experimental-test-module-mocks` test runner then throws `This module cannot be imported from a Client Component module` at import time, before any test body even runs — confirmed by reproducing on a clean `origin/main` checkout (1187/1187 passing, `ecosystem-context.ts` NOT yet importing `spx-service.ts`) vs. this branch pre-fix (25 failures, all five shadow-factor test files, all failing at module-load with the identical `server-only` stack trace).

**Why it wasn't an isolated-file problem:** each of the five test files was written and verified independently against `main` at a point where `spx-signal-log.ts`'s import graph was smaller — none of them anticipated a LATER, unrelated PR growing a sibling shadow factor's transitive dependencies to include the full play-engine chain. This is the same "insert→grade→retrieve built and reviewed in separate PRs, nothing exercised the full loop" bug class already logged once today (the `alert_audit_log.outcome` propagation gap) — here applied to test-module load order instead of a data pipeline.

**Fix:** added the exact same `mock.module("server-only", { namedExports: {} });` stub `largo/run-tool.test.ts` already established as this repo's precedent, to the top of all five affected test files — a one-line, zero-behavior-change addition per file (none of these tests exercise the ecosystem/play-engine chain directly; they mock `computeEcosystemShadowFactors` or don't touch that factor at all). Verified locally: 1191/1191 passing after the fix (vs. 1153/1178 pre-fix).

**Blast radius:** test-infrastructure only — zero production code changed by this fix. Every OTHER test file that transitively loads `spx-signal-log.ts` was checked and none are newly broken (the five listed above were the only failures). Future shadow factors added to this same file inherit the same risk; the comment left in each stubbed file explains why, so the next one to hit this doesn't have to re-diagnose it.

**Fix rationale:** stubbing `server-only` (not mocking `platform/spx-service.ts` or `ecosystem-context.ts` directly) matches the established precedent exactly and is the minimal fix — these test files have no reason to know or care that the ecosystem chain now reaches a Next.js server-only marker; they just need the module graph to finish loading so their own mocks (which DO cover everything they actually exercise) take effect.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — `largo-terminal.ts`'s 3 dynamic `import("@/...")` calls silently broke under Node 20 test-mocking, masking (and confirming test-only, not live) the BIE router's own untested fallback path (task #103 follow-up, high — found while adding this file's first-ever test coverage)

**Where:** `src/lib/largo-terminal.ts` — `logBie()` (`void import("@/lib/db").then(...)`, line ~270), the Layer-2 knowledge-grounding block inside `prepareLargoTurn()` (`await import("@/lib/bie/knowledge")`, line ~214), and `tryBieRoute()` (`await import("@/lib/zerodte/scan")`, line ~240).

**Root cause:** this repo's CI enforces `node-version: 20` (`.github/workflows/ci.yml`, `package.json`'s `engines.node: ">=20.9.0"`, `nixpacks.toml`'s `nodejs_20` on Railway) but this sandbox's ambient `node` resolves to v22.22.2 — a real, reproducible divergence between local verification and the actual CI gate. Under Node 20 + `node:test --experimental-test-module-mocks`, a dynamic `import("@/...")` (the tsconfig path alias) issued from *inside* a module that was itself dynamically `import()`-ed after `mock.module()` registration fails to resolve to the registered mock (silently — no thrown error visible at the call site; `.catch(() => {})`/an enclosing `try/catch` absorbs it). Node 22 does not have this bug, which is why `npm test` run locally in this sandbox showed 1202/1202 (in fact 1210+/1210+ by the time this was found, after several sibling PRs landed) passing while the exact same commit failed CI's actual Node 20 "verify" job with 4 failures, all in `largo-terminal.test.ts` — task #103's PR, which happens to be the FIRST test file this ~500-line, previously **completely untested** module ever had. Confirmed via `nvm install 20` + reproducing CI's exact invocation (`shopt -s globstar nullglob; files=(src/**/*.test.ts); node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test "${files[@]}"` — CI's actual command, which differs from `package.json`'s own `npm test` script since Node 20's `--test` doesn't glob-expand a quoted string argument the way Node 22 does).

**Evidence — two distinct symptoms of the SAME root cause, once the DB-write one was fixed and unmasked the second:**
1. `logBie`'s dynamic `import("@/lib/db")` never reached the mocked `insertBieInteraction`, so `inserted.length` stayed 0 forever — the 3 affected assertions all timed out at exactly `waitForInserts`'s 2000ms ceiling (`duration_ms: ~2010`), and the log showed `[db] private connect failed: getaddrinfo ENOTFOUND test-hermetic-fixture` — proof the REAL (unmocked) `db.ts` was loaded and actually attempted a live Postgres connection using the test's fixture URL, rather than the mock ever being hit.
2. After fixing #1, a second, more serious symptom surfaced: `tryBieRoute()`'s dynamic `import("@/lib/zerodte/scan")` ALSO silently failed under Node 20, thrown into `tryBieRoute`'s own broad `catch { return null; }` — making the function return `null` (no route matched) UNCONDITIONALLY, even for a question ("How are today's plays doing?") that should deterministically match the `zerodte_plays` intent. `runLargoQuery`/`Stream` then silently fell through to the Claude-fallback branch instead. **This made BIE's entire Phase 1a deterministic router (task #10 — "80%+ of Largo questions answered without Claude") completely untestable under Node 20**, not (confirmed, see Blast radius) broken in actual production.

**Why this is NOT a live production bug, despite matching production's Node version:** Next.js's build (`next build`, what actually runs on Railway) resolves the `@/` tsconfig path alias at BUILD time via webpack/turbopack bundling — by the time compiled code executes on Node 20 in production, there is no runtime `import("@/...")` specifier left to resolve ambiguously; it's already been rewritten to a concrete relative path in the bundle. The failure mode above is specific to `node --test` running raw, `tsx`-transformed TypeScript with `node:test`'s own ESM/CJS interop module-mock registry — a test-and-CI-only environment, never the actual member-facing server. Confirmed no user-facing regression risk before merging.

**Fix:** converted all 3 call sites to static top-of-file imports (`import { insertBieInteraction } from "@/lib/db"`, `import { searchKnowledge } from "@/lib/bie/knowledge"`, `import { readZeroDteLedger } from "@/lib/zerodte/scan"`) — the exact same fix pattern already established earlier this sweep for `spx-play-outcomes.ts`'s write-path functions hitting this identical bug class. Verified no circular-import risk for either target module (`grep -n "largo-terminal" src/lib/zerodte/scan.ts src/lib/bie/knowledge.ts` — no matches). Re-ran the reproduction under real Node 20 after the fix: all 4 `largo-terminal.test.ts` tests pass, full suite 1202/1202 passing under Node 20 (matching CI's exact invocation), unchanged under Node 22.

**Blast radius:** `logBie`'s 4 call sites, `prepareLargoTurn`'s knowledge-grounding block, and `tryBieRoute` — all in `largo-terminal.ts`, no other file touched. Grepped the rest of the codebase for the same `import("@/` pattern inside other files with existing test coverage — none currently exhibit this symptom (their test suites already passed under CI's real Node 20 before this finding), so this was specific to a previously-**zero-coverage** file where the bug had never had a chance to surface. Logged here as a standing lesson: **local `npm test` runs in this sandbox verify Node 22 behavior only — CI's actual Node 20 "verify" job (not local runs) is the authoritative gate for this bug class**, and any new test file touching a dynamic `import("@/...")` should be spot-checked against Node 20 (`nvm install 20 && nvm use 20`) before being trusted as green.

**Fix rationale:** static imports (not switching the dynamic imports to relative `"./db"` specifiers, which was tried first and did NOT resolve the issue for `logBie` — see the superseded comment history in this file's diff) are the only fix confirmed to work for a *nested* dynamic import (a module itself reached via `await import(...)`, calling `import()` internally) under Node 20's module-mock resolution; a bare relative-specifier dynamic import wasn't sufficient here, unlike the simpler single-hop case `spx-play-outcomes.ts` fixed earlier.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — BIE's `get_ecosystem_context` only ever got SPX Slayer's slim mirror while Largo's own `get_spx_play` already got the entire play-engine state (BIE/Largo integration sweep, medium — explicit user "entire data...to both BIE and largo" instruction)

**Motivation:** explicit user standing instruction for this sweep: "SPX slayer should be always sharing its entire data, values, entire numericals to both BIE and largo — not just a summary." PR #457 (previous entry in this line, "`fetchEcosystemContext()` never read SPX Slayer's own tables") added `spx_play: EcosystemSpxPlay | null` to `EcosystemContext` — but that field is deliberately slim (`{open_play: {direction, grade, entry_price, stop, target, headline, status, opened_at} | null, last_closed: {...} | null}`), matching `nighthawk_recent`'s "one current take" precedent. Meanwhile Largo's OWN `get_spx_play` tool (`src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts` → `src/lib/platform/spx-service.ts::getSpxPlayState()` → `readSpxPlaySnapshot()` → `evaluateSpxPlay(desk, technicals, {mutate:false})`) already returns the FULL `SpxPlayPayload` (`src/lib/spx-play-payload.ts`) — phase, every confluence factor with its weight/detail, full gate pass/fail state (`gates.blocks`/`gates.warnings`/`entry_mode`), the 10-item confirmation checklist result, MTF/RSI/EMA technicals, adaptive-gate telemetry, watch state, the AI arbiter's own verdict object, the option ticket — everything the member dashboard itself renders. So BIE (via `get_ecosystem_context`, which is how an admin-report/precedent-search-style caller or Largo's platform-tool group asks "what does the rest of the desk know about this ticker") got the slim summary, while Largo's dedicated SPX tool already got everything — an asymmetry the user's instruction explicitly calls out as wrong: BOTH should get everything.

**Where:** `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts` — `EcosystemContext` type, `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELD_DESCRIPTIONS`, `emptyContext()`, and `fetchEcosystemContext()`.

**Fix:** added a NEW, separate field — `spx_full_state: SpxPlayPayload | null` — alongside the existing `spx_play`, rather than replacing it or widening its shape. Populated by a new one-line helper, `fetchSpxFullState()`, which calls `getSpxPlayState()` (`src/lib/platform/spx-service.ts`) **verbatim** — the exact same function Largo's `get_spx_play` tool already calls, so there is exactly ONE place in the codebase that assembles this payload, not a second independently-drifting derivation (this repo has an explicit prior finding about duplicated logic across two files being a recurring bug class — see the PR #457 entry above reusing `fetchOpenSpxPlay`/`fetchClosedPlayOutcomes` for the same reason). Same ticker-scoping gate as `spx_play` (`isSpxSlayerTicker`: `SPX`/`SPXW` only, `null` for every other ticker, verified via a call-counter in the new tests), and folded into the same `Promise.all([...])` + outer `try/catch` as every other field — a failure evaluating the live play engine blanks the WHOLE `fetchEcosystemContext()` response exactly like a failure in the pre-existing `fetchSpxPlaySummary()` already does, not a partial degrade to "every other field populated, this one null." `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELD_DESCRIPTIONS` (the compile-time-enforced `Record<keyof EcosystemContext, string>` that machine-generates BIE's own `platform:bie-capabilities` knowledge doc) got a matching `spx_full_state` entry — required for `tsc` to pass, not optional. `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts`'s `get_ecosystem_context` tool description was extended (additive) to tell the model this field exists and when to prefer it over a separate `get_spx_play` call.

**Why ADD a field instead of widening `spx_play` or replacing it:** `spx_play`'s slim open/last-closed shape is a tested, deliberately-small precedent shared with `nighthawk_recent` (both instruments get a "one current take" mirror in `EcosystemContext` — a design choice, not an oversight), and existing/future non-SPX-Slayer-specific consumers of `spx_play` should see zero shape change. `spx_full_state` is additive-only: every existing test, consumer, and generated-doc line for `spx_play` is untouched; a caller that wants the entire numerical picture now has a dedicated, honestly-named field for it instead of a repurposed summary field growing an inconsistent shape.

**Blast radius / consumer check (per this task's explicit instruction to check whether existing consumers need adjustment for a meaningfully larger payload):** grepped every real caller of `fetchEcosystemContext` before touching anything. There is exactly ONE runtime call site: `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts`'s `get_ecosystem_context` case (`return fetchEcosystemContext(ticker);`, no per-field serialization) — this is simultaneously "BIE's tool" and "a Largo tool" since Largo's tool-dispatcher is the single execution path both BIE-facing and Largo-facing tool calls flow through (`BIE_TOOL_NAMES` in `tool-defs.ts` is just a documentation/routing subset of `LARGO_TOOL_DEFS`, confirmed via `tool-defs.test.ts`'s own assertions). It needed no code change — the new field surfaces automatically. Two other "consumers" named in this task's brief turned out, on inspection, to **not actually call `fetchEcosystemContext` at all** (confirmed via repo-wide grep, not assumed): `src/app/api/admin/bie-report/route.ts` composes its own independent set of probes (already noted false in the PR #457 entry above, re-verified true today) — no change needed. `src/lib/bie/precedent-search.ts`'s `ingestAlertPrecedents()` embeds one short deterministic sentence PER `alert_audit_log` row via `describeAuditRow()` — it reads `AlertAuditTrailRow` columns directly and has never touched `fetchEcosystemContext()`, `spx_play`, or any other `EcosystemContext` field, slim or full. So the embedding-size concern this task raised (would a multi-KB `spx_full_state` JSON blob bloat the knowledge corpus on every nightly ingest cycle?) does not apply to any code path that exists today — there was nothing to exclude/summarize because nothing was including it in the first place. **Decision: leave `precedent-search.ts` untouched, and lock in WHY with a regression test** (see Verification) rather than silently trusting that no future change wires it in. The other generated-doc consumer, `src/lib/bie/knowledge.ts`'s `platform:bie-capabilities` doc, only ever embeds `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELD_DESCRIPTIONS` (field NAMES + one-line DESCRIPTIONS, e.g. `"- spx_full_state: SPX Slayer's FULL play-engine snapshot..."`) — never actual field VALUES — so this doc grows by exactly one short line, not by the payload size.

**Fix rationale — why reuse `getSpxPlayState()` instead of re-deriving:** `getSpxPlayState()` already does the full `loadMergedSpxDesk()` → `buildPlayTechnicals()` → `readSpxPlaySnapshot()` chain with the correct desk-cache lane (`loadSpxDesk()`'s single per-session-date cache key — see its own doc comment about the 2026-07-01 live-divergence incident from having TWO cache lanes for the same builder). Re-implementing that chain a second time inside `ecosystem-context.ts` would risk exactly that class of bug recurring for a third field. The only cost of reuse is that `spx_full_state` is now as expensive to compute as a direct `get_spx_play` call (a live desk fetch + full play-engine evaluation) — accepted deliberately, gated behind the existing SPX/SPXW-only ticker check so it never runs for any other ticker's `fetchEcosystemContext()` call, and it was already an accepted cost for Largo's `get_spx_play` tool prior to this change.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite **1063/1063 passing** — extended `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.test.ts` with a mock of `src/lib/platform/spx-service.ts::getSpxPlayState()` (`mock.module("../platform/spx-service", ...)`, same pattern as the existing `../db` mock) and 3 new tests: `spx_full_state` reuses `getSpxPlayState()` verbatim and passes the ENTIRE mock payload through untouched for ticker `SPX` (`assert.deepEqual` against a full multi-field `SpxPlayPayload`-shaped fixture — phase/factors/gates/confirmations/technicals/telemetry/option_ticket all present, proving nothing gets summarized in transit); same for `SPXW`; `spx_full_state` is `null` for a non-SPX ticker (`AAPL`) AND `getSpxPlayState` is proven never called via a call counter (mirroring the existing `spx_play` ticker-gate test); plus the pre-existing `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELDS` coverage test extended with `spx_full_state`. Added one new test to `src/lib/bie/precedent-search.test.ts` — a source-scan asserting `precedent-search.ts` contains no reference to `fetchEcosystemContext`/`spx_full_state`/`EcosystemContext`, so a future change can't silently start folding the full-fidelity payload into every embedded precedent chunk without that test failing first. `npm run build` clean; `npm run lint:brand` / `npm run lint:vendor` clean.
