## 🟢 ADDED 2026-07-04 — Night's Watch narrates SPX Slayer's own live play alongside a user's SPX position (enhancement, not a bug fix)

**Motivating gap (new idea surfaced during the BIE/Largo integration sweep, not from the original audit's fix list):** Night's Watch (`src/lib/nights-watch/*`) already reads the SAME live desk cache SPX Slayer's own play engine uses (`loadMergedSpxDesk()` in `src/lib/spx-desk-loader.ts`) and independently recomputes the SAME pure `computeSpxConfluence()` to narrate structural context ("near the gamma flip", "approaching a GEX wall") for a user's saved SPX/SPXW option position. But none of that ever checked whether SPX Slayer's OWN play engine currently has an ACTUAL open play (`spx_open_play` table) — real, decision-relevant information the desk already reads elsewhere (`getSpxOpenPlay()` in `src/lib/platform/spx-service.ts`, used by the admin dashboard and Night Hawk edition builder) but never cross-referenced against a user's own position. A user holding an SPX call had no way to learn "SPX Slayer also has a live CALL play open right now, same direction" (a genuine confirmation signal) or "SPX Slayer just flipped to a PUT play against your position" (a genuine caution signal).

**Where:**
- `src/lib/nights-watch/position-context.ts` — `PositionContext` type (new optional `spxSlayerOpenPlay` field) + new exported cache reader `getNwSpxOpenPlay()` + `buildPositionContextMap()` (list/poll path, used by `enrichment.ts` for every saved position's verdict).
- `src/lib/nights-watch/position-detail.ts` — `PositionDetailSections` (new `spxSlayerPlay` section) + `buildPositionDetail()`'s parallel fetch + `buildVerdictContext()` (detail-view path, the "authoritative" verdict) + `buildDataSources()` ledger.
- `src/lib/nights-watch/verdict.ts` — new pure `spxSlayerAlignment()` helper + two new deterministic signals (`spx_slayer_aligned` / `spx_slayer_against`) wired into `computeVerdict()` alongside the existing `flowAlignment`/`trendAlignment` cross-tool signals.
- `src/lib/nights-watch/position-narrative.ts` — `buildContext()` gets a new "SPX SLAYER PLAY" prompt-context line (grade + entry price + direction), and the system prompt's list of reasoning inputs now names it explicitly.

**What changed:**
1. `getNwSpxOpenPlay()` wraps the EXISTING, already-correct `getSpxOpenPlay()` (which itself wraps `fetchOpenSpxPlay(todayEtYmd())` against `spx_open_play`) in `withServerCache` keyed by ET-date (60s TTL, mirroring the desk's own freshness window) — reused verbatim, **no new query** against `spx_open_play`. Exported so BOTH the list path (`buildPositionContextMap`) and the detail path (`buildPositionDetail`) share the SAME cache entry, exactly like the existing `getNwTickerGex()` sharing pattern.
2. `PositionContext.spxSlayerOpenPlay` is `{ direction: "long"|"short", grade, entry_price, opened_at } | null | undefined` — `null` means "the engine checked and has nothing open right now" (a real, meaningful state); `undefined` means "never populated" (every non-SPX underlying, since SPX Slayer's engine only ever trades SPX/SPXW). This mirrors the existing honesty-rule convention for `flows`/`trend`/`darkPoolBias` on the same type.
3. `computeVerdict()`'s new `spxSlayerAlignment()` compares the play engine's own `direction` (bullish "long" / bearish "short" — **not** call/put; a long CALL and a "long" play are the SAME direction) against the position's own bullish/bearish exposure (`wantsUp`, the same convention every other cross-tool signal in this file already uses). An aligned live play is a HOLD signal (`spx_slayer_aligned`); an opposing live play is a TRIM signal (`spx_slayer_against`) — both fire ONLY when a real play row exists (never on `null`/`undefined`), so a quiet day with no open play changes nothing.
4. `position-narrative.ts`'s `buildContext()` — already the single source of "known numbers" the grounding guard checks the AI narrative against — gets the new line folded into the SAME joined context string, so `entry_price`/`grade` numbers introduced here are grounded automatically via the file's existing `extractNumbersFromText(context)` call site; no separate registry to update.

**Blast radius:** purely additive. No existing structural-level narration (gamma/wall/max-pain/confluence) changed. Non-SPX positions are completely unaffected — the field is never even set on their `PositionContext`/`PositionDetailSections` object, so every pre-existing signal/test for AAPL-style tickers is untouched (verified: full regression suite `NEW_SIGNAL_IDS` list in `verdict.test.ts` extended, still 0 false-fires on a plain/undefined context). One-way only: SPX Slayer's own play engine (`src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts`) is never touched and never reads anything from Night's Watch — this is strictly a Night's Watch READ of SPX Slayer's existing state.

**Fix rationale:** reused the exact `getSpxOpenPlay()`/`fetchOpenSpxPlay()` read path rather than writing a second query against `spx_open_play`, and reused the existing shared-cache-reader + honesty-rule (`null` vs `undefined`) conventions already established for every other cross-tool signal in this file, so the new field composes with the existing verdict/narrative machinery instead of introducing a parallel pattern. Deliberately did NOT add a symmetric read the other way (SPX Slayer reading Night's Watch) — that would blur SPX Slayer's play engine into per-user state, which the standing architecture keeps strictly separate (SPX Slayer trades one desk-wide play; Night's Watch narrates N users' individual positions against it).

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. New tests: `src/lib/nights-watch/position-context.test.ts` (new file — proves `buildPositionContextMap` attaches the live play for SPX/SPXW, `null` when the engine has none open, and leaves the field completely unset for a non-SPX ticker in the SAME batch call, and that `getSpxOpenPlay` is never invoked for an all-non-SPX batch); `verdict.test.ts` (+7 tests: aligned/against/side-aware/undefined/null/grounded-reason, plus `spx_slayer_aligned`/`spx_slayer_against` added to the existing `NEW_SIGNAL_IDS` no-regression list); `position-narrative.test.ts` (+3 tests: the line appears and is grounded when present, is entirely absent when `null`, and a fabricated SPX Slayer entry price still fails the shared grounding guard). Full suite `npm test`: 1033/1033 passing. `npm run build`, `npm run lint:brand`, `npm run lint:vendor` all clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — `alert_audit_log.outcome` was NEVER written by anything — BIE precedent search (`get_similar_precedents`) has been a complete no-op, platform-wide, since it shipped (SPX Slayer/BIE-Largo sweep, high)
**Where:** `alert_audit_log` (`src/lib/db.ts:920-955`) has an `outcome`/`outcome_graded_at`/`later_correct` column set, added specifically so `src/lib/bie/precedent-search.ts::fetchResolvedAlertAuditRows()` (`src/lib/db.ts:3229-3242`) could find "resolved" rows to embed as searchable precedents for Largo's `get_similar_precedents` tool ("has a setup like this happened before, and what happened"). `fetchResolvedAlertAuditRows()` filters `WHERE outcome = ANY(TERMINAL_ALERT_OUTCOMES)` (`target|stop|ambiguous|unfilled`).

**Root cause:** nobody ever `UPDATE`s `alert_audit_log.outcome`. A repo-wide grep for `UPDATE alert_audit_log` returns zero matches anywhere before this PR. Every write path (`insertAlertAuditLog` in `zerodte/scan.ts`, `nighthawk/play-outcomes.ts`, `spx-play-claude.ts`) only ever `INSERT`s a row at fire-time — the `outcome` column was designed as "a materialized copy, source of truth stays the per-product grading columns" (`docs/bie/AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md`), but the copy step itself was never built. So every row for every product (0DTE, Night Hawk, and SPX Slayer's `spx_claude_play`) has sat at `outcome = NULL` forever, meaning `fetchResolvedAlertAuditRows()` has returned **0 rows** since Stage 4 shipped (2026-07-03) — `ingestAlertPrecedents()` has stored 0 precedents, and `findSimilarPrecedents()`/`get_similar_precedents` has had nothing to ever return, silently (both fail open to empty results, so there was no visible error — just an always-empty knowledge base).

**Evidence:** `grep -rn "UPDATE alert_audit_log" .` → zero matches pre-fix. Each product already computes its OWN outcome independently and correctly, just never propagated: `zerodte_setup_log.direction_hit` (set by `gradeZeroDteSetupRow`, `src/lib/db.ts:3352`, driven by `computeLedgerGrade` in `board.ts`), `nighthawk_play_outcomes.outcome` (set by `updateNighthawkPlayOutcome`, driven by `resolveOutcome()` in `play-outcomes.ts`), `spx_play_outcomes.outcome` (set by `classifyOutcome()` in `spx-play-outcomes.ts`).

**Fix — pure propagation, no new grading methodology:** new `src/lib/bie/alert-outcome-sync.ts` + a new low-frequency cron (`/api/cron/alert-outcome-sync`, registered in `cron-registry.ts`, `railway.alert-outcome-sync.toml`, every 6h). It selects ungraded `alert_audit_log` rows old enough to plausibly be settled (3h pre-filter — real gating is the origin row's own resolved state, not this threshold), looks up each row's origin via its existing `source_table`/`source_key`, and — if the origin is ALREADY resolved — copies/maps that already-computed value onto `alert_audit_log` via `UPDATE ... WHERE outcome IS NULL` (race-safe/idempotent). It never re-derives correctness from prices itself. Three new read-only DB functions added to `db.ts` (`fetchZeroDteGradeForAudit`, `fetchNighthawkOutcomeForAudit`, `fetchSpxClaudePlayOutcomeForAudit`) alongside the existing `fetchUngradedAlertAuditRows`/`gradeAlertAuditLogOutcome` pair — kept in `db.ts` to match this file's existing convention of owning all `alert_audit_log` SQL in one place.

**Outcome-vocabulary mapping (exact):**
- 0DTE: `direction_hit: true → "target"`, `false → "stop"`, `null` (graded but genuinely ungradeable — no flag/close price) → left alone, not forced into a vocabulary value.
- Night Hawk: `nighthawk_play_outcomes.outcome` already uses the identical vocabulary (`target|stop|open|ambiguous|pending|unfilled`) — a pass-through filter, not a translation; `open`/`pending` left alone.
- SPX Slayer (`spx_claude_play`): `win → "target"`, `loss → "stop"`, `breakeven → "ambiguous"` (not a clean win/loss, same "resolved but not directionally clear-cut" meaning `ambiguous` already carries); `open`/`superseded` (force-closed bookkeeping artifact, never a real trade thesis test) left alone.
- `later_correct` derived from the written outcome: `target → true`, `stop → false`, `ambiguous`/`unfilled → null` (genuinely indeterminate).

**The one genuinely hard join — `spx_claude_play`, documented as a known limitation, not silently glossed over:** unlike 0DTE/Night Hawk, this alert_type's `source_key` (`{price, direction, at}` — the Claude gate VERDICT snapshot, from `spx-play-claude.ts`'s `logPlayVerdict`) is not a real foreign key into `spx_play_outcomes` (whose actual PK is `open_play_id`, never available at verdict time — a verdict is logged before the engine decides whether to even open a play). Most `spx_claude_play` rows are VETOs and will correctly never match anything (a vetoed setup was never traded, so it has no trade outcome — this is the right behavior, not a gap). For APPROVED verdicts, `spx-play-engine.ts` opens the play from the exact same in-memory `desk`/`confluence` used for the verdict, moments later — so `fetchSpxClaudePlayOutcomeForAudit()` matches on exact direction + a 0.01-tolerance price match + a 30-minute `opened_at` window after the verdict's `fired_at`, `ORDER BY opened_at ASC LIMIT 1`, restricted to closed rows only. A miss just leaves the row ungraded for next run (safe); the tight constraints are chosen so this can find the right play or no play, never the wrong one.

**Blast radius:** this unlocks `get_similar_precedents` for real for the first time, platform-wide — 0DTE, Night Hawk, and SPX Slayer alerts will all start accumulating real, graded precedents once this cron runs in production. Wiring Largo's actual `get_similar_precedents` tool-calling behavior to *use* this newly-populated data (prompt design, retrieval tuning) is explicitly a separate, later task — this PR only fixes the pipeline that feeds it. No existing consumer of `alert_audit_log`, `zerodte_setup_log`, `nighthawk_play_outcomes`, or `spx_play_outcomes` is modified — this is a pure additive reader-then-writer on one previously-dead column.

**Fix rationale:** propagation (not a new price-checking/grading job) was the only safe choice — each product's existing settlement logic is already reviewed, already tested, and is the actual system of record per `AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md`'s own design ("source of truth stays the per-product grading columns"); re-deriving "was this correct" a second way here would risk a second, possibly-diverging answer for the same alert. A single shared low-frequency cron (not three separate ones) was chosen since all three lookups are cheap reads gated by the same `outcome IS NULL` pre-filter and the same "leave alone if unresolved" contract — splitting them into three crons would triple the boilerplate (auth/lock/logCronRun/Railway TOML) for no operational benefit, since none of the three is remotely live-critical.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite passing with 14 new tests in `src/lib/bie/alert-outcome-sync.test.ts` (pure mapping functions for all three products + `later_correct` derivation; `syncAlertAuditOutcomes()` end-to-end via `mock.module("../db", ...)` per the `largo-store.test.ts` convention — proves a resolved origin writes `outcome`/`outcome_graded_at`/`later_correct` correctly, an unresolved origin leaves the row untouched, a no-match (VETO) is counted separately from an error, and a concurrent-grade race (`UPDATE` affecting 0 rows) isn't double-counted); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🧠 ENHANCEMENT 2026-07-04 — SPX Slayer shadow signal: UW prediction-market consensus around macro hard-block windows (`feat/spx-shadow-predictions-macro`)

**Status:** SHIPPED, second of the 5 planned shadow factors riding the `feat/spx-shadow-signal-framework` framework (PR #464 — flow anomalies was the first; risk-reversal skew/realized vol, Benzinga catalysts, and ecosystem cross-instrument agreement are the remaining 3, expected concurrently from sibling branches).

**Motivation:** `src/lib/spx-play-gates.ts`'s `macroHardBlock()` is a binary, all-or-nothing gate — the moment `now` falls inside a CPI/FOMC/FED/NFP/PAYROLL/PPI/GDP window (computed from `desk.macro_events` via `parseMacroEventTime`/`macroBlockWindow` in `src/lib/spx-macro-window.ts`), EVERY new 0DTE entry is blocked, regardless of which way the release actually breaks. UW's prediction-market consensus (`fetchUwPredictionsConsensus` in `src/lib/providers/unusual-whales.ts` — insiders/smart-money/unusual/whales options-flow-derived directional reads per ticker, already used the same way by NightHawk in `src/lib/nighthawk/market-wide.ts`/`dossier.ts`, so this reuses the existing fetcher rather than inventing a new provider call) might carry pre-positioning information about which way a macro surprise breaks. Same evidence-first philosophy as the flow-anomaly shadow factor (`bie/calibration.ts`'s `MIN_EVIDENCE = 10` precedent): log what a "lean into consensus instead of blocking outright" refinement WOULD have read, with **zero** live effect, until a future separately-reviewed change ever promotes it into `macroHardBlock`'s actual gating logic.

**What was built:**
- `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-predictions.ts` (new file) — pure functions, no DB/fetch, no bare `Date.now()`/`new Date()` (caller passes `now`), same structural-isolation guarantee as `spx-signals-shadow.ts` (`git grep spx-signals-shadow-predictions src/lib/spx-signals.ts` returns nothing — confirmed).
  - `resolveMacroWindowState(desk, now)` — determines whether `now` is `active` (inside the SAME window `macroHardBlock` would block right now) or merely `near` (within a new `NEAR_WINDOW_LEAD_MINUTES = 30` lead BEFORE the window's start, so the factor can observe pre-positioning ahead of the real block, never after — once a window ends the surprise has already broken). Reuses the real gate's own exported, dependency-free time-window helpers (`parseMacroEventTime`/`macroBlockWindow`) since those are genuinely shared math, not a gating decision — but intentionally DUPLICATES `macroHardBlock`'s private `CPI|FOMC|FED|NFP|PAYROLL|PPI|GDP` keyword predicate (kept-in-sync-by-comment, same precedent as `SHADOW_ANOMALY_LOOKBACK_MINUTES` in `spx-signal-log.ts`) rather than importing/exporting it from `spx-play-gates.ts` — keeps this file's "never imports / never imported by the real gate" structural guarantee intact and avoids touching the real gating file at all.
  - `computeMacroPredictionsShadowFactor(desk, consensusSignals, consensusFresh, now)` — when `resolveMacroWindowState` says `near`, filters UW consensus to `MACRO_PREDICTION_TICKERS = ["SPY","QQQ"]` (broad-market proxies only — a macro surprise is a market-wide event, not a single-name one, unlike the flow-anomaly factor's mega-cap universe). A confidence_pct ≥ `CONSENSUS_CLEAR_MIN_PCT = 65` on a non-neutral direction counts as "clear"; SPY and QQQ must AGREE in direction (disagreement ⇒ mixed, weight 0) and the stronger of the two sets the provisional weight (tiers: 65%→±5, 70%→±9, 80%→±13, 90%→±18 — same ±3-to-±18 real-engine range as the flow-anomaly factor, documented inline as unproven). **3-way state discipline, stricter than a 2-way available/not split:** (1) outside any macro window → `available:true, weight:0` ("not applicable" — a CONFIRMED state, never conflated with a data problem); (2) inside/near a window but consensus not confirmed fresh (`consensusFresh:false` or `consensusSignals:null`) → `available:false` (mirrors `flowFeedFresh`'s exact discipline in the sibling factor); (3) inside/near a window, fresh data, but no SPY/QQQ signal or a mixed/sub-threshold read → `available:true, weight:0` (a real, confirmed "no clear lean" reading, distinct from both other states).
- Wiring: `logSpxMacroPredictionsShadowFactor(desk, confluence)` — new sibling function in `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts` (kept separate from `logSpxShadowFactors` so this factor's UW-fetch/cache concerns don't mix with the flow-anomaly factor's DB-read concerns). **Cost guard:** `fetchUwPredictionsConsensus` hits 4 UW endpoints per call — this function calls `resolveMacroWindowState` FIRST and skips the UW round trip entirely unless `near` is true, since macro windows are rare (~30 CPI/NFP + 8 FOMC + a handful of PPI/GDP releases a year) and `evaluateSpxPlay` (the call site) ticks continuously all session. When a fetch IS warranted, a module-scoped cache (`MACRO_PREDICTIONS_CACHE_TTL_MS = 90_000`, same idiom as `spx-desk.ts`'s `cachedPriorDay`) avoids repeat-fetching on every tick for the ~1-2 hours a window is active/near. Freshness (`consensusFresh`) is derived from `raw_counts` (the four sources' pre-filter row counts) rather than an empty `top_signals` array, because `fetchUwPredictionsConsensus` — via `uwGetSafe` — NEVER throws (it swallows failures and returns null/[]), so an empty result alone can't distinguish "UW is down" from "no consensus data right now"; all-four-sources-zero is treated as an outage. Called from `evaluateSpxPlay` in `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts`, immediately after the existing `logSpxShadowFactors` fire-and-forget call, same `firePlayTelemetry` non-blocking idiom, same pre-Night-Hawk-bonus score/grade snapshot. Persists via the EXISTING `insertShadowFactorObservation`/`spx_confluence_shadow_observations` table (no new table/migration — that table's own `db.ts` comment already anticipated "UW prediction-market consensus" as a future `factor_name` family sharing this same generic schema).

**PROOF THIS DOES NOT CHANGE LIVE SIGNALS:** zero lines changed in `src/lib/spx-signals.ts` (the pure confluence engine), `src/lib/spx-play-gates.ts` (`macroHardBlock` and its gating behavior), or `src/lib/providers/spx-desk.ts` (`SpxDeskPayload`'s shape) — `git status`/`git diff --stat` for this branch touches only `spx-signal-log.ts` (one new function) and `spx-play-engine.ts` (one new import + one new fire-and-forget call), plus 3 new files. The full pre-existing `computeSpxConfluence: byte-for-byte unchanged output` test in `src/lib/spx-signals.test.ts` was re-run unmodified and still passes (this PR doesn't touch anything it exercises). New tests: `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-predictions.test.ts` (16 cases — `resolveMacroWindowState`'s active/near/outside/non-hard-block-event classification across CPI's precise-time window and FOMC's afternoon-Fed window; `computeMacroPredictionsShadowFactor`'s outside-window "not applicable", stale/missing-data `available:false`, clear bullish/bearish signed weights at multiple confidence tiers, SPY/QQQ-disagreement and sub-threshold "mixed" cases, neutral-direction handling, and the SPY+QQQ-agree "strongest sets the weight" rule) and `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log-macro-predictions.test.ts` (7 cases — DB-not-configured short-circuit, the no-fetch-outside-window cost guard, UW-not-configured short-circuit, a real fetch producing the correct signed row, the 90s cache reusing one fetch across two calls, a simulated UW throw being caught rather than propagating, and the all-zero-raw_counts "treated as outage" rule). All 1082 tests in the suite pass (`npm test`).

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts` (one new exported function + one new module-scoped cache; `logSpxShadowFactors` and `maybeLogSpxPlay` untouched), `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` (one new import + one new fire-and-forget call in `evaluateSpxPlay`; nothing else in that file touched), and 3 new files. No other `computeSpxConfluence`/`macroHardBlock`/`SpxDeskPayload` consumer is affected — this branch never touches `spx-signals.ts`, `spx-play-gates.ts`, `spx-desk.ts`, or `db.ts` (the shadow table/insert helper already existed from PR #464, reused as-is).

**Fix rationale:** chose NOT to add a new UW fetch into `buildSpxDesk()` (`src/lib/providers/spx-desk.ts`) even though the task considered it — that function is on the hot ~1s desk-poll path, and baking a 4-endpoint UW call into every single poll for a signal that's only ever relevant during a handful of rare, short windows a year would be pure waste; instead the fetch lives at the shadow-logging call site, gated by `resolveMacroWindowState` so it's skipped >99% of the time and cached when it does fire. Chose to duplicate `macroHardBlock`'s keyword predicate rather than export it from `spx-play-gates.ts`, prioritizing the "structurally cannot touch/be touched by the real gate" guarantee (provable by `git grep`, per the framework PR's own stated design goal) over the small DRY cost of one duplicated boolean expression — the real window MATH (`parseMacroEventTime`/`macroBlockWindow`) is still reused as-is since that part is genuinely shared, dependency-free utility code, not a gating decision. Chose SPY+QQQ-must-agree (not "either one alone") for a "clear" reading, since a genuine market-wide macro consensus should show up in both broad-market proxies — if they disagree, that itself is informative (no clean read), not something to average away.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite `npm test` — 1082/1082 passing (23 new: 16 + 7). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🧠 SPX Slayer reads BACK from BIE's ecosystem-context SHIPPED 2026-07-04 — the other half of "closed ecosystem," SHADOW MODE, zero live behavior change (branch `feat/spx-shadow-ecosystem-context`)

**Status:** SHIPPED. Second of the 5 planned shadow factors named in the shadow-signal-framework entry below ("ecosystem cross-instrument agreement"), and the piece that makes SPX Slayer's data flow genuinely **bidirectional** with BIE for the first time — every other cross-instrument wire this sweep has built (`ecosystem-context.ts`'s `spx_play` field, the various `get_ecosystem_context`/Largo tool work) had SPX Slayer as a *source* other instruments could read; this is the first time SPX Slayer itself *consumes* what BIE already knows about the rest of the platform.

**Motivation:** `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts`'s `evaluateSpxPlay()` already has exactly ONE bespoke cross-instrument input wired live and un-shadowed — `getNhConfluenceBonus()` (lines 98-141), which reads Night Hawk's evening edition straight out of Postgres (`fetchLatestNighthawkEdition`) and injects a bounded ±3 "prior" directly into `confluence.score`. That's a real, hand-rolled, one-off integration for exactly one other instrument. Meanwhile `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts::fetchEcosystemContext(ticker)` already exists as BIE's general-purpose "what does the rest of the platform know about this ticker" query layer (already read by the admin BIE report and every Largo `get_ecosystem_context` tool call) — and SPX Slayer's own engine had never once called it. This PR is what happens when the engine reads from that general layer instead of requiring a new bespoke direct-DB read per instrument, generalizing the `getNhConfluenceBonus` pattern to 0DTE Command via a proper BIE-mediated read, entirely in shadow mode per the same `bie/calibration.ts` `MIN_EVIDENCE=10` "report first, prove it before it can move score" bar the sibling shadow-signal-framework PR established.

**What was built:**
- `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-ecosystem.ts` (new file) — two shadow factors, both fed by `fetchEcosystemContext("SPX")`:
  1. `ecosystem_zerodte_agreement` — compares 0DTE Command's same-day take (`zerodte_today.direction`, "long"/"short" per `src/lib/zerodte/board.ts`'s `ZeroDteSetup` type) against the engine's own `confluence.direction`. Provisional weight (±3/±5/±8, inside the real engine's ±3-to-±18 range) bucketed off 0DTE's own 0-100 dossier `score` (not its `conviction` label, which has drifted before — see `board.ts`'s "very strong" tier — while `score` is a stable numeric contract). `direction`/`implied_weight` sign follow 0DTE's own bullish/bearish call (mirroring how the live NH bonus is signed); the `detail` text explicitly states AGREES/DISAGREES per the task's framing.
  2. `ecosystem_spx_anomaly_*` — a pattern-detected flow anomaly attributed directly to ticker `"SPX"` (24h window, from `fetchEcosystemContext`'s own `recent_anomalies` query). **See the differentiation note below — this is deliberately NOT a duplicate of the sibling `flow_anomaly_*` factor.**
  - Two-tier shape: `deriveEcosystemShadowFactors(ctx, confluenceDirection)` is pure (no DB/fetch, exhaustively unit-testable with plain objects, matching `computeShadowFactors`'s own contract in the sibling file); `computeEcosystemShadowFactors(desk, confluenceDirection)` is the thin async wrapper that actually calls `fetchEcosystemContext("SPX")` and hands the result to the pure function.
- Wiring: `logSpxEcosystemShadowFactors(desk, confluence)` in `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts`, right next to the sibling's `logSpxShadowFactors`, writing into the SAME generic `spx_confluence_shadow_observations` table (`factor_name` is the discriminator column — no new migration needed; the sibling PR's table comment explicitly anticipated "ecosystem cross-instrument agreement" as a future tenant of this table). Called from `evaluateSpxPlay` in `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` immediately after the existing `logSpxShadowFactors` call (both fire via the file's existing `firePlayTelemetry` fire-and-forget helper), passing `confluence.direction` in addition to score/grade since the 0DTE-agreement factor's whole point is comparing directions.

**DIFFERENTIATION FROM THE SIBLING `flow_anomaly_*` FACTOR (read this before assuming duplication):** the sibling `computeShadowFactors` (`spx-signals-shadow.ts`) reads BIE's `flow_anomalies` table for the SPY/QQQ + 6-mega-cap proxy universe (`SHADOW_ANOMALY_TICKERS`), which deliberately EXCLUDES `"SPX"` itself. This PR's anomaly factor goes through `fetchEcosystemContext("SPX")`, whose `recent_anomalies` query is `WHERE ticker = 'SPX'` — rows the `market-regime-detector` cron writes for HELIX prints with NO per-stock ticker attribution at all (confirmed in `detectFlowAnomalies()`, `src/app/api/cron/market-regime-detector/route.ts`: `const t = r.ticker ?? "SPX"` — a null-ticker print, i.e. generic/unattributed SPX index 0DTE flow, groups under the literal string `"SPX"`). The two factors' ticker filters are mutually exclusive by construction (`"SPX"` vs. an 8-name list that never contains `"SPX"`) — they answer different questions ("is a proxy stock/ETF flashing an anomaly" vs. "is raw, unattributed SPX index flow itself flashing one") and can never fire on the same underlying row.

**Known, deliberately-accepted real-world gap (documented, not hidden):** neither `zerodte_setup_log` nor `flow_anomalies` currently write literal ticker `"SPX"` for 0DTE Command's own scanner rows in the way this PR's `zerodte_today` read is scoped — 0DTE Command's ticker universe is individual stocks/ETFs, not the index itself — so in production today `ecosystem_zerodte_agreement` will likely resolve to "no 0DTE data" (available:true, neutral) most of the time, exactly as designed for that state (never fabricated into a false agreement). The plumbing is built and fully exercised by mocked tests now so it activates automatically the moment 0DTE Command's coverage (or `flow_anomalies`' generic-SPX bucket) produces a real hit — no future code change needed on this side. This mirrors this repo's own precedent of shipping forward-compatible plumbing ahead of the data that will populate it (e.g. `spx_play`'s null-for-non-SPX-ticker contract in `ecosystem-context.ts`).

**STALENESS GUARD:** `flow_feed_fresh` (BIE's own `isFlowFrameFreshAnywhere()` cluster-wide check, already exposed on every `EcosystemContext`) gates BOTH factors in this PR as a blanket switch, not just the anomaly one — when false, both return `available:false, implied_weight:0`, never a fabricated neutral. This is a deliberately conservative choice: `fetchEcosystemContext()` itself already fails open to an all-empty, `flow_feed_fresh:false` context on ANY internal error, so treating that one flag as "can BIE vouch for anything it just returned" (rather than narrowly scoping it to literal flow-derived fields) means a BIE-side hiccup can never leak a stale `zerodte_today` read into a shadow observation either. A future, separately-reviewed change could split this into per-field freshness if evidence-gathering ever needs that granularity — not justified at today's shadow-only stakes.

**PROOF THIS DOES NOT CHANGE LIVE SIGNALS:** `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` for this PR is **empty** — untouched, same as the sibling shadow-signal-framework PR. `computeSpxConfluence()` is never imported by, and never imports, either shadow file (`git grep spx-signals-shadow src/lib/spx-signals.ts` returns nothing). The existing load-bearing test, `src/lib/spx-signals.test.ts::"computeSpxConfluence: byte-for-byte unchanged output for a rich fixture desk (shadow-framework PR proof)"`, was left in place unmodified and still passes byte-for-byte — this PR did not need to touch `spx-signals.ts` or that test at all to prove inertness, since `evaluateSpxPlay`'s new call sits in its own `firePlayTelemetry`-wrapped statement, reading `confluence.score`/`.grade`/`.direction` (never assigning back to them) after `computeSpxConfluence()` has already returned. `logSpxEcosystemShadowFactors` is itself only ever invoked via `firePlayTelemetry`'s `void work().catch(...)` fire-and-forget wrapper — the exact pattern already proven non-blocking for `logSpxShadowFactors` — so no `await` inside `computeEcosystemShadowFactors`'s `fetchEcosystemContext` call (itself already a `Promise.all` of several queries) can ever delay `evaluateSpxPlay`'s return to its caller.

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts` (one new exported function + one new import; `logSpxShadowFactors`/`maybeLogSpxPlay` untouched), `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` (one new import + one new fire-and-forget call in `evaluateSpxPlay`, immediately after the sibling's; nothing else in that file touched, `getNhConfluenceBonus()` itself untouched per the hard constraint), and two new files (`spx-signals-shadow-ecosystem.ts` + its test). No new migration, no new table, no change to `db.ts` — reuses `insertShadowFactorObservation` and `spx_confluence_shadow_observations` as-is. `fetchEcosystemContext` itself is unmodified (read-only consumer, one more caller alongside the admin BIE report and Largo's tools).

**Fix rationale:** kept the scoring logic in a brand-new file (not appended to the sibling `spx-signals-shadow.ts`) so the "structurally cannot touch the live score" guarantee stays visible by a single-file `git grep`, matching the sibling's own stated design goal. Chose the two-tier pure-deriver/async-wrapper split specifically so the scoring logic is unit-testable with zero mocking (fast, exhaustive) while the `fetchEcosystemContext` wiring gets its own focused test using this repo's established `mock.module()` convention (`ecosystem-context.test.ts`). Deliberately did NOT add a third factor reading `nighthawk_recent` from the same ecosystem-context payload — Night Hawk already has a live, un-shadowed, working integration via `getNhConfluenceBonus()`'s direct DB read, and `nighthawk_play_outcomes` is ticker-scoped the same way `zerodte_setup_log` is (so a `"SPX"`-scoped read would face the identical real-world sparsity gap noted above with no new signal to show for it); adding a second, redundant BIE-mediated echo of data already flowing into the live score would blur which of the two NH read-paths is authoritative. Left as an explicit candidate for a future, separately-scoped PR if evidence ever calls for retiring the direct read in favor of the BIE-mediated one.

**Tests added:** `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-ecosystem.test.ts` (12 cases: `flow_feed_fresh:false` → both factors unavailable; no 0DTE data → neutral/available; 0DTE agreement → positive weight signed by 0DTE's own bullish call; 0DTE disagreement → negative weight signed by 0DTE's own bearish call; no engine bias yet → neutral, not fabricated; unrecognized 0DTE direction string → neutral, never fabricated; no SPX-tagged anomaly → neutral/available with its own factor_name; a real SPX-tagged anomaly → signed weight; multiple SPX anomalies → highest-severity-wins collapse; plus 3 `mock.module()`-based wrapper tests proving `computeEcosystemShadowFactors` calls `fetchEcosystemContext` with exactly `"SPX"` and wires its fields straight through). `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log-shadow-ecosystem.test.ts` (4 cases mirroring `spx-signal-log-shadow.test.ts`'s structure: DB-not-configured short-circuit, `confluence.direction` passed through to the scorer, the persisted row shape for a real observation set, and an unavailable observation persisting as `available:false` rather than being silently dropped).

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite `1104/1104` passing after merging in the concurrent `feat/spx-shadow-catalysts` (#468) and `fix/retire-dead-signal-events-table` (#461) sibling PRs (16 new from this PR — 12 in the new shadow-ecosystem module test, 4 in the new wiring test; every pre-existing shadow/ecosystem-context/spx-signals test re-run alongside them to confirm zero regression). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand` / `lint:vendor` clean.

## 🧠 ENHANCEMENT 2026-07-04 — added `docs/bie/spx-slayer-mechanics.md` so BIE's knowledge corpus can ground SPX Slayer meta-questions (not a bug fix)
**The gap:** `ingestBieKnowledge()` (`src/lib/bie/knowledge.ts:161-277`) builds Largo/BIE's retrieval corpus from `docs/`, `docs/bie/`, `docs/audit/`, `AGENTS.md`/`CLAUDE.md`, a generated tool/cron map, a generated `platform:bie-capabilities` self-description, semantic precedent chunks, and the latest Night Hawk recap — but no document anywhere described **SPX Slayer's own play-engine mechanics** (confluence scoring, the sequential gate order, the AI arbiter's fail-closed behavior, the numeric-grounding guard). The closest existing doc, `src/lib/learn/guides/instruments/spx-slayer.ts`, is member-facing marketing/UX copy (panel layout, dos/don'ts, FAQ) — accurate about the desk's *UI*, not precise about the engine's *decision logic*, and it isn't markdown so `ingestBieKnowledge()` never reads it anyway. So a meta-question like "how does the play engine decide to fire a signal" or "why does SPX Slayer have a separate AI verdict step" had nothing accurate and specific for BIE's retrieval to ground an answer in — Largo would have had to infer from general training knowledge or scattered code comments, exactly the class of drift the 2026-07-04 `docs/bie/ARCHITECTURE.md` staleness incident (further up this file) already burned the platform on once.

**Fix:** wrote `docs/bie/spx-slayer-mechanics.md`, a precise reference doc (not marketing copy) covering, from the actual current source — `src/lib/spx-signals.ts`, `src/lib/spx-play-gates.ts`, `src/lib/spx-play-claude.ts`, `src/lib/spx-play-payload.ts`, `src/lib/spx-play-conflicts.ts`, `src/lib/spx-play-confirmations.ts`, `src/lib/grounding-guard.ts`, `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` — never the simplified learn-guide prose: the `buildSpxDesk()` data pipeline; Stage 1 confluence scoring (every weighted factor, the score clamp, the A+/A/B/C/D grade formula, conflicts vs. weighted_conflicts); Stage 2's sequential entry gates in their actual check order plus the independent 10-item confirmations checklist; Stage 3's AI arbiter — including the non-obvious fact that it's feature-flagged (`SPX_CLAUDE_GATE`, off by default) and substitutes a deterministic mechanical verdict when off, with **fail-closed** behavior (veto, not silent fallback) only once the flag/forced-call path is actually active; the numeric-grounding guard (`checkNumbersGrounded`/`knownPlayLevels`) that discards an ungrounded Claude verdict entirely; the open-play exit priority order; and where live state lives (`spx_signal_log`, `spx_open_play`, `spx_play_outcomes`, `platform_meta` cache/budget keys, `alert_audit_log`) plus the exact Largo tools (`get_spx_structure`, `get_spx_confluence`, `get_spx_play`, `get_open_plays`, `get_trade_history`, `get_setup_stats`, `get_signal_log`) that read that state.

**Ingestion — confirmed, no code change:** `ingestBieKnowledge()`'s `DOC_DIRS = ["docs", "docs/bie", "docs/audit"]` is a directory scan, not an explicit file list, and `docs/bie` is already one of the three scanned directories — so the new file is picked up automatically on the next `db-cleanup` cron ingest with zero wiring changes. Verified the file still lands inside the function's `files.slice(0, 40)` per-run cap: with the current corpus (24 files in `docs/`, 4 in `docs/bie` before this addition, 28 in `docs/audit`, 2 root docs — 59 candidates total), `docs`'s and `docs/bie`'s combined contribution is only ~29 files, so `docs/bie/spx-slayer-mechanics.md` sits at array index 28, comfortably inside the first-40 window regardless of `readdirSync`'s per-directory ordering (not fixed by the OS across all filesystems). **Noted but explicitly out of scope for this PR** (content-only addition per the standing instruction): the corpus already exceeds 40 candidate `.md` files today, meaning some `docs/audit/*.md` files at the tail of the scan order are silently dropped from ingestion every run — that's a pre-existing capacity/ordering issue in `ingestBieKnowledge()` itself, unrelated to adding one more doc to an under-capacity directory, and is left for a separate finding/fix rather than folded into a docs-only PR.

**Chunking-compatibility check:** `ingestBieKnowledge()` → `storeKnowledge()` → `chunkDocument()` (`src/lib/bie/embeddings.ts`) splits on blank-line paragraph boundaries into ≤1200-char chunks, hard-splitting (with a 150-char overlap) any single paragraph that itself exceeds the cap. Every paragraph in the new doc was deliberately kept ≤1200 chars (max 1076) so it chunks cleanly on natural section boundaries — verified by running the actual `chunkDocument()` against the file (17 chunks, all ≤1200 chars, none from a mid-sentence hard-split).

**Test:** per CLAUDE.md's issue-handling policy, a docs-only content addition with no ingestion-code change has no code path to unit-test for correctness — but the doc's *fitness for the pipeline that consumes it* is testable and now is: 3 new tests in `src/lib/bie/bie.test.ts` (nearest `*.test.ts` to `knowledge.ts`) assert the file exists under a `DOC_DIRS`-scanned path with real (not stub, not oversized) content, that every paragraph fits `chunkDocument()`'s cap so nothing hard-splits, and that the doc actually names the real functions/behaviors (`computeSpxConfluence`, `evaluatePlayGates`, `evaluateClaudePlayApproval`, `fail-closed`, `checkNumbersGrounded`, `get_spx_play`, `get_spx_confluence`) BIE is meant to ground answers in — so a future edit that guts the doc's substance or breaks its chunking would fail CI, even though the content's *accuracy* still rests on human review at write time, same as any doc.

**Blast radius:** additive knowledge-corpus content only. No change to `ingestBieKnowledge()`, `storeKnowledge()`, `searchKnowledge()`, `chunkDocument()`, embeddings, retrieval ranking, or any Largo tool definition/handler — the existing `get_spx_confluence`/`get_spx_play`/etc. tools already worked before this doc existed; this only gives BIE's *prose-explanation* retrieval a grounded source to cite for the "why"/"how" behind those tools' live numbers, not a new capability.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean, full `npm test` passing (3 new tests in `bie.test.ts`, all green), `npm run build` clean, `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## 🧠 SPX Slayer shadow signal framework, catalyst edition SHIPPED 2026-07-04 — Benzinga FDA/M&A/guidance catalysts scored in SHADOW MODE against the real Mega-caps factor, zero live behavior change

**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/spx-shadow-catalysts`), 2nd of 5 planned shadow factors extending `feat/spx-shadow-signal-framework` (the `flow_anomalies` factor immediately below this entry was the 1st; risk-reversal skew + realized vol and UW prediction-market consensus and ecosystem cross-instrument agreement are the remaining 3 follow-ups reusing this same framework/table).

**Motivation:** the real "Mega-caps" factor in `src/lib/spx-signals.ts` (`computeSpxConfluence()`, search `leader_stocks`) scores ONLY the raw average `change_pct` across the 6 mega-cap leaders (`src/lib/providers/polygon.ts`'s `LEADER_STOCKS`: AAPL/NVDA/MSFT/GOOG/TSLA/META) — it has zero awareness of WHY those stocks are moving. A 2% mega-cap move on an FDA approval, an active M&A deal, or a guidance revision is qualitatively different evidence than the same 2% move on no news (drift, sympathy, index-fund flow), but the real factor can't tell them apart today. Same shadow-mode philosophy as the framework PR (`bie/calibration.ts`'s `MIN_EVIDENCE = 10` "report-first, a human ships the change" precedent, not re-derived here) — this logs what a catalyst-aware overlay WOULD have contributed, with zero live effect, so it can be graded against outcomes before ever being proposed as a real `score +=` change.

**What was built:**
- `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-catalysts.ts` (new file) — `computeCatalystShadowFactors(desk, catalysts, catalystFetchOk, now?)`, a pure function scoring Benzinga catalysts already classified by the existing `fetchBenzingaCatalysts` (`src/lib/providers/polygon.ts`, the exact fetcher `largo/run-tool.ts`'s `get_catalysts` tool, `nights-watch/position-detail.ts`, and `nighthawk/dossier.ts` already use — no new provider call written) against the SAME `desk.leader_stocks` ticker/change_pct list the real Mega-caps factor already reads. In scope: only `binary` (FDA approval/rejection), `m&a`, and `guidance` catalyst types — insider/buyback/offering/short/ipo are real Benzinga types but a materially weaker directional read, explicitly out of scope rather than silently dropped. Recency window is 24h (not the flow-anomaly factor's 30min — a catalyst's price impact spans the trading day/pre-market, not a tape sweep's half-life). One `ShadowFactorObservation` per leader ticker with an in-window qualifying catalyst (highest-type-weight wins per ticker: binary(15) > m&a(12) > guidance(6), mirroring `computeShadowFactors`'s own per-ticker dedup), or a single `megacap_catalyst_watch` observation when nothing qualifies. Direction is a coarse keyword heuristic (`inferCatalystDirection`) — explicitly provisional/unproven, documented inline same as the weight scale. Each directional observation's magnitude is computed against the mega-cap **raw average** (recomputed independently from `desk.leader_stocks` with the identical formula — data reuse, not logic reuse, this file never imports `spx-signals.ts`): full magnitude when the catalyst's direction agrees with the raw-average sign, halved when it conflicts ("complicates" the raw average per the task's own framing), full magnitude when there's no aggregate lean to compare against. The `detail` string additionally notes whether the catalyst plausibly explains that specific ticker's own `change_pct` sign, for a human reader.
- **Availability/staleness guard** (mirrors `computeShadowFactors`'s exactly): `available:false` when `desk.leader_stocks` is empty (nothing to scope a catalyst check to) OR when `catalystFetchOk` is false — `fetchBenzingaCatalysts` swallows its own fetch errors internally and returns `[]` on failure, so it cannot itself distinguish "no catalysts" from "the fetch broke." The caller passes `polygonConfigured()` (Benzinga news is served through Polygon's `/benzinga/v2/news`, gated on `POLYGON_API_KEY`) as the best available proxy for "the fetch could even have succeeded" — an honest, documented limitation (a configured-but-transiently-failing fetch still reads as "no catalysts found," same as every other existing consumer of this fetcher), not a claim of a stronger guarantee than the underlying fetcher actually provides.
- Wiring: `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts::logMegaCapCatalystShadowFactors(desk, confluence)` — a NEW sibling function next to `logSpxShadowFactors` (not folded into it, so each shadow factor's wiring stays independently reviewable), fetching `fetchBenzingaCatalysts(ticker, 5)` concurrently per `desk.leader_stocks` ticker, computing observations, and persisting each via the existing `insertShadowFactorObservation` (same table, `spx_confluence_shadow_observations` — no schema change needed, `factor_name` was already the discriminator column by design). Called from `evaluateSpxPlay` in `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` immediately after the existing `logSpxShadowFactors` call, wrapped in the same `firePlayTelemetry()` fire-and-forget helper, passing the identical pre-Night-Hawk-bonus `confluence.score`/`.grade` snapshot.
- **Deliberately did NOT touch `buildSpxDesk()`/`SpxDeskPayload`** (`src/lib/providers/spx-desk.ts`): catalyst data is fetched directly in the wiring function, not threaded through the desk builder. That builder runs on every desk poll/render on the member-facing hot path; this shadow factor only needs to run once per `evaluateSpxPlay` tick. Same reasoning `logSpxShadowFactors` already established by querying `flow_anomalies` directly rather than attaching it to `desk`.

**PROOF THIS DOES NOT CHANGE LIVE SIGNALS:** `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` for this PR is **empty** — confirmed directly, the real Mega-caps factor's scoring block (`leader_stocks`/`change_pct`/`avg`/the `±6` weight) is byte-for-byte untouched, and nothing in `spx-signals.ts` imports `spx-signals-shadow-catalysts.ts` (`git grep spx-signals-shadow-catalysts src/lib/spx-signals.ts` returns nothing). The load-bearing test is the SAME `src/lib/spx-signals.test.ts::"computeSpxConfluence: byte-for-byte unchanged output for a rich fixture desk (shadow-framework PR proof)"` test the framework PR added (not duplicated here) — it already exercises a `leader_stocks` fixture and asserts the Mega-caps factor's own `{label:"Mega-caps", weight:6, detail:"Leadership avg +1.00%"}` line byte-for-byte, and re-ran clean (`ok 1`) after this PR's changes with zero modification needed. In `evaluateSpxPlay`, the new call sits after `confluence` is already computed and returned unconditionally above it, inside its own `firePlayTelemetry` fire-and-forget wrapper (an exception inside is caught/logged, never thrown into the caller) — identical structural guarantee to `logSpxShadowFactors`.

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts` (one new exported function + 3 new imports; `logSpxShadowFactors`/`maybeLogSpxPlay` untouched), `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` (one new import + one new fire-and-forget call in `evaluateSpxPlay`, same statement shape as the existing `logSpxShadowFactors` call, nothing else touched), and two new files (`spx-signals-shadow-catalysts.ts` + its test). No `db.ts` change — reuses the framework PR's existing `spx_confluence_shadow_observations` table/`insertShadowFactorObservation` as-is (proof the table's `factor_name`-discriminator design already works for a second, unrelated factor family). No `spx-desk.ts`/`SpxDeskPayload` change (see rationale above). Every other `computeSpxConfluence` call site is unaffected for the same reason the framework PR's blast-radius note applies unchanged here: none of them call `logMegaCapCatalystShadowFactors`, and `computeSpxConfluence` itself is unchanged.

**Fix rationale:** chose a NEW sibling function (`logMegaCapCatalystShadowFactors`) over extending `logSpxShadowFactors` in place so this PR's `spx-play-engine.ts` diff is a pure addition (one new call) rather than a change to the existing flow-anomaly call's body — matches this sweep's expectation that concurrent shadow-factor PRs each add their own call site and merge without semantic conflict. Chose to dampen (not zero out or drop) a catalyst that conflicts with the raw average rather than the alternative of suppressing it: a real, conflicting catalyst is itself useful evidence for later evidence-gathering (does the catalyst or the raw tape-average turn out to be the better predictor?), and dropping it would silently throw that comparison away. Chose `polygonConfigured()` over inventing a stronger freshness signal (e.g., a new Benzinga-specific health check) because `fetchBenzingaCatalysts` itself offers no better signal today without changing that shared fetcher (which every other Benzinga consumer in the repo also depends on) — flagged explicitly as a known limitation rather than silently claiming a guarantee the code doesn't have.

**Tests added:** `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-catalysts.test.ts` (12 cases — no-leader-stocks and fetch-not-ok availability guards and their `deepEqual` collapse proof, fresh-fetch-no-catalyst, bullish/agreeing and bearish/complicating and no-aggregate-lean weight math, 24h window filtering, off-universe ticker filtering, out-of-scope catalyst type filtering, multi-ticker sort + per-ticker highest-weight-wins dedup, neutral-direction handling, and the "does not clearly track its own move" detail branch); `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log-catalyst-shadow.test.ts` (6 cases covering `logMegaCapCatalystShadowFactors`'s DB-not-configured and Polygon-not-configured and no-leader-stocks short-circuits, the per-ticker fetch-call shape, and the persisted row shape for the no-catalyst/real-catalyst/out-of-scope-type states).

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite `1077/1077` passing (18 new). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand` / `lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — `signalAccuracy`/`regimeAccuracy` in `/api/platform/intel` + the Night Hawk platform-intel snapshot were computed from a bridge table that has never received a single write (SPX Slayer/BIE/Largo sweep, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/migrations/004_god_tier_features.sql:69-102` defines `signal_events`/`signal_outcomes`, a schema explicitly designed to unify SPX Slayer + Night Hawk signal accuracy under one ledger (`signal_source` documented as `SPX_SLAYER | NIGHT_HAWK | GEX_WALL`). It has never received a single row in production: `POST /api/signals/record` (`src/app/api/signals/record/route.ts`) is the only INSERT path, and grepping the entire `src/` tree turns up zero callers outside that route file itself — no cron, no engine write, nothing. Two live consumers still `JOIN` against it expecting real win-rate data and always got nothing: `src/app/api/platform/intel/route.ts` (`signalAccuracy` via `GROUP BY se.signal_source`, `regimeAccuracy` via `JOIN signal_outcomes so ON so.signal_event_id = se.id`, both gated on `se.fired_at > NOW() - INTERVAL '30 days'`) and `src/lib/nighthawk/platform-intel-snapshot.ts::fetchPlatformIntelSnapshot()` (an independent, duplicated copy of the same dead join, feeding `formatPlatformIntelForPrompt()` into the Night Hawk edition-build Claude prompt and the Largo `get_platform_intel` tool). `scripts/railway-layer-audit.mjs` already had a named check (`P1-TR-SPLIT`) that had been silently monitoring for exactly this gap.

**Evidence:** `grep -rn "signal_events\|signal_outcomes\|signals/record\|signals/open\|signals/outcome" src/` returns exactly 6 non-test source files: the 3 `src/app/api/signals/*` route files themselves, the migration, and the 2 dead-data consumers above — no writer anywhere. Because the `JOIN` always returns 0 rows, `route.ts`'s `intelligence.signalRecommendation` was hard-pinned to the `"INSUFFICIENT DATA — not enough signals to assess regime accuracy yet."` branch forever, and `platform-intel-snapshot.ts`'s `signal_recommendation` was permanently `null` unless a critical anomaly happened to be active — a silently-broken feature dead since day one, never a data-availability lull.

**Fix:** new shared module `src/lib/signal-accuracy.ts` — `fetchSignalAccuracyBySource()` reads the two REAL, live outcome ledgers instead: SPX Slayer's via the already-existing `fetchPlayOutcomeStats()` (`src/lib/spx-play-outcomes.ts`, backed by `spx_play_outcomes`), Night Hawk's via the already-existing `fetchNighthawkOutcomeAnalytics()` (`src/lib/db.ts`, backed by `nighthawk_play_outcomes`) filtered through the same `isNighthawkOutcomeScoreable()` the public track-record page already uses (`src/lib/track-record-page.ts`) — so this reports the identical Night Hawk win rate members see there, not a third, independently-drifting definition of "win." `blendedAccuracy()` combines both into one real win rate, gated by a `MIN_SAMPLE_FOR_RECOMMENDATION = 10` floor so a thin sample still reports "insufficient data" honestly instead of a misleadingly precise percentage. Both `route.ts` and `platform-intel-snapshot.ts` now call this ONE shared module instead of running two independent copies of the dead join (the exact duplicated-logic-in-a-second-file shape this repo's audits have flagged before) — `signalAccuracy` (`route.ts`) now returns real `{SPX_SLAYER, NIGHT_HAWK}` `{total, wins, winRate}` numbers (`winRate` is `null`, never a fabricated `0%`, until that source has a closed sample), and `currentRegimeProfitable`/`signalRecommendation` (`route.ts`) and `signal_recommendation` (`platform-intel-snapshot.ts`) are now driven by the real blended win rate.

**`regimeAccuracy` — resolved as "honestly empty," not faked:** the original per-regime breakdown depended on `se.metadata->>'regime'`, a field nothing ever wrote even hypothetically (no caller of the dead `POST /api/signals/record` ever passed it). Neither real ledger (`spx_play_outcomes`, `nighthawk_play_outcomes`) tags an outcome with the market regime (`market_regime.composite`) active at entry, and joining either against `market_regime` by nearest timestamp would be new, unverifiable-from-this-sandbox raw SQL (direct Postgres access is blocked here per this repo's environment notes) for a breakdown this task's scope didn't require. `route.ts`'s `regimeAccuracy` field stays an array (shape-compatible for any future consumer) but is now intentionally `[]` with a comment explaining why, and `bestPerformingRegime`/`worstPerformingRegime` stay `null` — both were ALSO always null before this fix (the dead join never returned rows either), so this is not a behavior regression, just an honest one instead of an accidental one.

**Dead-schema disposition — documented, not removed:** did not drop `signal_events`/`signal_outcomes` or the `/api/signals/{record,open,outcome}` routes. `/api/signals/open` is still exercised by `scripts/gha-http-smoke.mjs` and `scripts/validate-deploy.mjs` as an auth-gate smoke check (expect 401 unauthenticated) — removing the table/routes would require also editing those two scripts for zero functional gain, since nothing depends on the DATA in this table anymore. Instead: added explicit `ORPHANED` comments to the table definitions (`004_god_tier_features.sql`) and all 3 route files explaining nothing writes to them and pointing at the real ledgers, and downgraded `scripts/railway-layer-audit.mjs`'s `P1-TR-SPLIT` check from a `fail()` (which would now permanently false-positive on an intentionally-orphaned table) to an informational log line noting it's expected-empty-by-design.

**Blast radius:** `src/app/api/platform/intel/route.ts` and `src/lib/nighthawk/platform-intel-snapshot.ts` (both consumers, now sharing one fetch instead of two independent dead-join copies), new `src/lib/signal-accuracy.ts`, `src/lib/migrations/004_god_tier_features.sql` (comments only, no schema change), all 3 `src/app/api/signals/*/route.ts` files (comments only, no behavior change), `scripts/railway-layer-audit.mjs` (check downgraded from fail to informational log). No other call site references `signal_events`/`signal_outcomes`/`/api/signals/*` (verified by grep) and no consumer anywhere reads `regimeAccuracy`'s contents (`nighthawk-morning-confirm/route.ts`, the only other HTTP consumer of `/api/platform/intel`, only reads `regime.composite`/`anomalies`/`lastBrief`) or `platform-intel-snapshot.ts`'s internal regime-accuracy rows (the exported `PlatformIntelSnapshot` type never had a `regimeAccuracy` field — only the derived `signal_recommendation` string), so no other consumer's shape changes.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite passing locally on Node 22. `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean. **CI (Node 20) caught a real, environment-specific bug this local run missed:** `verify` failed 6/1046 with `ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND '.../src/lib/@/lib/db'` — under Node 20 + `--experimental-test-module-mocks`, `spx-play-outcomes.ts`'s dynamic `await import("@/lib/db")` (tsconfig-path alias) mis-resolves once any module in the process has been mocked (Node 22 doesn't hit this); confirmed via a direct repro (downloaded a standalone Node v20.19.0 binary and ran the exact `ci.yml` command locally). Fixed by switching all of that file's dynamic `@/lib/db` imports to the relative `./db` specifier (same directory, so alias resolution is bypassed entirely, no other behavior change) — re-verified clean on both Node 20.19.0 and Node 22: `1046/1046` passing (10 new: 5 in `src/lib/signal-accuracy.test.ts` for the pure `nightHawkAccuracyFromRows()`/`blendedAccuracy()` aggregation, 3 new in `src/app/api/platform/intel/route.test.ts` and 3 new in `src/lib/nighthawk/platform-intel-snapshot.test.ts` proving a real favorable win rate, a real unfavorable win rate, and the honest below-sample-size case using fixture rows standing in for `spx_play_outcomes`/`nighthawk_play_outcomes`). **Merge note:** a concurrent sibling PR (`298eed2`, below the shadow-framework entry) independently hit the exact same root cause for `fetchClosedPlayOutcomes` specifically and fixed it with a static top-level import instead — reconciled by adopting their static import for that one call site (the more idiomatic fix) and keeping the relative-import fix for this file's other, still-dynamic `@/lib/db` imports (`getMeta`/`setMeta`, `insertPlayOutcomeEntry`, `closePlayOutcomeRow`, `fetchRecentPlayOutcomeRows`), which their narrower fix didn't touch.
