## 🧠 SPX Slayer shadow signal framework SHIPPED 2026-07-04 — `flow_anomalies` scored in SHADOW MODE, zero live behavior change

**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/spx-shadow-signal-framework`), first of 5 planned shadow factors (risk-reversal skew + realized vol, UW prediction-market consensus, Benzinga catalysts, and ecosystem cross-instrument agreement are the 4 follow-ups reusing this same framework).

**Motivation:** `src/lib/spx-signals.ts::computeSpxConfluence()` is the pure scoring function that gates a real BUY_CALL/BUY_PUT recommendation shown to paying members trading real-money same-day 0DTE options. BIE's `flow_anomalies` table (SPY/QQQ/mega-cap sweep/skew/premium-spike patterns, written every 30min by the `market-regime-detector` cron — already read by `ecosystem-context.ts`'s `recent_anomalies` and the member-facing `/api/market/anomalies` feed) has never been read by the confluence engine at all. Guessing a live weight for a brand-new, never-backtested input on a real-money signal engine is genuinely risky — this repo's own BIE calibration harness (`src/lib/bie/calibration.ts`, `MIN_EVIDENCE = 10`) already refuses to turn a measured pattern into an acted-on recommendation until a bucket clears 10 graded plays, "report-first, a human ships the change." A brand-new input deserves at least that same bar before it can move score/action/grade by one point. So this PR builds **shadow mode**: log what the factor WOULD have scored, next to what the engine actually did, with **zero** live effect — promoting it into the real `score +=` chain is explicitly deferred to a future, separately-reviewed change once there's evidence.

**What was built:**
- `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow.ts` (new file) — `computeShadowFactors(desk, anomalies, flowFeedFresh, now?)`, a pure function scoring BIE's `flow_anomalies` table for the same SPY/QQQ + 6-mega-cap universe `src/lib/providers/polygon.ts`'s `LEADER_STOCKS` already tracks, within the same 30-minute window `scoreHelixFlowAlignment` uses for HELIX 0DTE sweeps. One `ShadowFactorObservation` per watched ticker with an in-window anomaly (highest severity wins per ticker, mirroring `scoreFlowStrikeConcentration`'s "dominant stack only" rule), or a single `flow_anomaly_watch` observation when nothing fired. Provisional weight scale (±3 to ±10, inside the real engine's ±3-to-±18 range) keyed off the regime detector's own CRITICAL/HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW severity taxonomy — explicitly unproven, documented inline, never to be trusted until a `factor_name` bucket clears the same `MIN_EVIDENCE = 10` bar. **Staleness guard:** `flowFeedFresh` (the caller's `isFlowFrameFreshAnywhere()` read, same cluster-wide check `ecosystem-context.ts` exposes as `flow_feed_fresh`) gates everything — when false, returns `available:false, implied_weight:0` regardless of what `anomalies` contains, so a dead ingestion pipeline can never be silently recorded as a confirmed "no anomaly" data point.
- `spx_confluence_shadow_observations` table, added to `db.ts::runMigrations()` (the live boot-time migration path — **not** the separate admin-triggered `src/lib/migrations/` folder, which a prior audit finding already established is effectively dead for anything actually reaching production). Deliberately generic (not `spx_flow_anomaly_observations`): `factor_name` is the discriminator column so all 5 planned shadow factors write into this one table. Columns: `id, observed_at, session_date, factor_name, available, implied_weight, direction, detail, price_at_observation, actual_score, actual_grade` (the last two are the REAL `computeSpxConfluence()` output at the same moment, for later correlation against outcomes — never fed back into shadow scoring). `insertShadowFactorObservation(...)` added to `db.ts` next to `insertSpxSignalLog`, same idiom (no `ON CONFLICT`, since unlike the signal log this wants one row per factor per evaluation tick, not de-duped).
- Wiring: `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts::logSpxShadowFactors(desk, confluence)` — queries `flow_anomalies` scoped to the watched tickers via `ticker = ANY($1::text[])` (same query shape as `ecosystem-context.ts`'s `recent_anomalies`, same ticker-list-batching pattern `fetchNighthawkEchoForTickers` uses, not a third divergent query style), reads `isFlowFrameFreshAnywhere()`, calls `computeShadowFactors`, and persists each observation. Called from `evaluateSpxPlay` in `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts`, **immediately after** its existing `computeSpxConfluence(desk)` call (the live cron path: `/api/cron/spx-evaluate` → `runSpxEvaluator` → `evaluateSpxPlay`), wrapped in the file's existing `firePlayTelemetry()` fire-and-forget helper — the exact same non-blocking, try/catch-via-`.catch()` idiom already used for `maybeLogSpxPlay`. The call passes `confluence.score`/`.grade` captured **before** the Night Hawk morning-prior bonus a few lines below mutates `confluence.score` in place, so the persisted `actual_score` pairs with the pure engine output, not a later ad hoc adjustment.

**PROOF THIS DOES NOT CHANGE LIVE SIGNALS:** `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` for this PR is **empty** — the confluence engine's own file was never touched, and nothing in it imports `spx-signals-shadow.ts` (the reverse is also true: `spx-signals-shadow.ts`'s own module doc notes `git grep spx-signals-shadow src/lib/spx-signals.ts` returns nothing). The load-bearing test is `src/lib/spx-signals.test.ts::"computeSpxConfluence: byte-for-byte unchanged output for a rich fixture desk (shadow-framework PR proof)"` — it feeds `computeSpxConfluence()` a fixture desk exercising ~21 of its factors (VWAP, γ regime, GEX support/anchor, max pain, 0DTE flow, dark pool, tide, NOPE, IV rank, TICK/TRIN/ADD, mega-caps, live tape, EMA20, net premium, VIX curve, HELIX sweeps, news risk, strike stack) with the wall clock frozen via `node:test`'s `MockTimers` (session-window scoring reads `new Date()` directly), and asserts the **entire** returned object — score (100, clamped), grade (A+), action (BUY_CALL), confidence (96), the full ordered `factors` array with every label/weight/detail, and `levels` — is byte-for-byte identical to a value captured from this exact code path. In `evaluateSpxPlay` itself, the new call sits in its own statement after `confluence` is already computed and returned unconditionally on the line above; it cannot execute before `computeSpxConfluence` returns, and its `firePlayTelemetry` wrapper means an exception inside it is caught and logged, never thrown into the caller.

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/db.ts` (new table + one new `insert*` function, additive only — no existing table/query touched), `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts` (one new exported function, `maybeLogSpxPlay` untouched), `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` (one new import + one new fire-and-forget call in `evaluateSpxPlay`, nothing else in that ~1100-line file touched), and two new files. `SpxPlayPayload`'s shape, the dashboard, and every other `computeSpxConfluence` call site (`spx-power-hour-engine.ts`, `spx-lotto-engine.ts`, `nights-watch/position-detail.ts`, `admin-spx-dashboard.ts`, `largo/run-tool.ts`, `largo-live-feed.ts`, `spx-commentary.ts`, `spx-signal-observe` cron) are all unaffected — none of them call `logSpxShadowFactors`, and `computeSpxConfluence` itself is unchanged.

**Fix rationale:** kept `computeShadowFactors` in a brand-new file rather than a same-file-but-unused function in `spx-signals.ts`, per the explicit design goal that the "cannot touch the live score" guarantee should be visible by inspection (a `git grep`), not just by a passing test — a reviewer (or Cursor) should be able to trust this PR without re-deriving the proof. Chose one observation per ticker (not one aggregate observation across the whole watched universe) so each `factor_name` accumulates its own independent evidence bucket, matching `bie/calibration.ts`'s per-bucket evidence-gate philosophy — a future promotion decision can be made per-ticker/anomaly-type if the evidence supports it, rather than an all-or-nothing call. Deliberately did NOT attempt to mock the `pg` package directly to unit-test `insertShadowFactorObservation`'s SQL in isolation — confirmed empirically that `node:test`'s `mock.module()` does not intercept the "pg" CJS package under this project's `tsx`-loader-based `npm test` setup (the mock silently fails to apply and the real `Pool` attempts a live TCP connect, timing out); no existing test in this codebase mocks `pg` either. Instead followed this repo's actual working DB-mocking convention (`whop-revocation.test.ts`, `platform-intel-snapshot.test.ts`: mock `@/lib/db` from the consumer under test) to test `logSpxShadowFactors`'s exact call contract into `insertShadowFactorObservation`.

**Tests added:** `src/lib/spx-signals.test.ts` (2 cases — the byte-for-byte proof above, plus a same-input-twice determinism check); `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow.test.ts` (10 cases covering: stale/missing feed → `available:false` regardless of anomaly content; fresh feed + no anomalies → `available:true, implied_weight:0`, explicitly distinct from the stale case; fresh + bullish/bearish real anomalies → signed `implied_weight`; window/ticker-universe filtering; same-ticker dedup by severity; unrecognized-severity fallback; null-direction handling); `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log-shadow.test.ts` (5 cases covering `logSpxShadowFactors`'s DB-not-configured short-circuit, the `ANY($1)` query shape, and the persisted row shape for the no-anomaly/stale/real-anomaly states).

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite `1044/1044` passing (17 new). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand` / `lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🧠 SPX Slayer shadow signal framework, factor #2 SHIPPED 2026-07-04 — risk-reversal skew + realized-vs-implied vol in SHADOW MODE, zero live behavior change

**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/spx-shadow-skew-vol`), second of the 5 planned shadow factors from the framework PR above (`feat/spx-shadow-signal-framework`, #464). Follows that PR's pattern exactly — same `ShadowFactorObservation` type, same `spx_confluence_shadow_observations` table (no schema change needed, `factor_name` is already the discriminator), same fire-and-forget wiring shape.

**What was built:**
- `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-skew.ts` (new file) — `computeSkewShadowFactor(desk, reading, now?)` and `computeVolDivergenceShadowFactor(desk, reading, now?)`, two pure functions mirroring `computeShadowFactors`'s exact shape (pure, `now` injectable, `void desk` accepted-but-unused for the same forward-compat reason). Both reuse `ShadowFactorObservation` from `spx-signals-shadow.ts` unchanged.
- **Provider reuse (no new provider calls):** `src/lib/providers/unusual-whales.ts`'s already-existing `fetchUwRiskReversalSkew`/`fetchUwRealizedVol` (previously only called from `largo/run-tool.ts`'s `get_risk_reversal_skew`/`get_realized_vol` tool cases and `nighthawk/dossier.ts`) and `src/lib/providers/polygon-options-gex.ts`'s `fetchPolygonRealizedVol`/`fetchPolygonIvTermStructure`. New parsing reuse: `src/lib/nighthawk/vol-metrics.ts`'s existing `parseLatestRiskReversalSkew`/`parseLatestRealizedVol` plus two small additive exports — `latestRow` (exposes the raw latest-by-date row so a caller can read its `date` for a staleness check, something the single-field parsers discard) and `parseLatestImpliedVol` (a live pull against `/api/stock/SPX/volatility/realized` on 2026-07-04 showed UW's realized-vol rows ALSO carry `implied_volatility` on the same row, e.g. `{"date":"2025-07-03","implied_volatility":"0.131000","realized_volatility":"0.087404"}` — previously unread; this lets the UW fallback recover BOTH legs of the divergence from one call).
- **Architecture decision — NOT wired through `SpxDeskPayload`/`buildSpxDesk()`:** the task brief's default assumption was to add a field to the desk if new data was needed. Investigated and deliberately deviated: `buildSpxDesk()` is the single hot path shared by the member dashboard's ~every-few-seconds poll, the play route, AND the evaluator cron, all through one cached `loadSpxDesk()` lane — the exact same "scarce 2-RPS cluster UW budget" `spx-desk.ts`'s own comments and `runUwPooled` usage already treat as a constrained resource. Adding 2 more forced UW/Polygon calls there would tax every desk consumer for a pair of factors that only need to run once per `evaluateSpxPlay` tick and are explicitly unproven. Instead both factors fetch directly inside the new `logSpxSkewShadowFactors` wiring function — exactly how the framework PR's OWN `logSpxShadowFactors` already fetches `flow_anomalies` directly rather than threading it through the desk payload. `SpxDeskPayload`/`buildSpxDesk()` are untouched by this PR (verify: `git diff main -- src/lib/providers/spx-desk.ts` is empty).
- **Risk-reversal skew factor** (`factor_name: "risk_reversal_skew"`): UW's `historical-risk-reversal-skew` endpoint returns empty for ticker `SPX` (confirmed live, `{"data":[]}`) but real data for `SPY` — the same "SPX sometimes empties, use SPY as the liquid proxy" situation `spx-desk.ts` already handles for NOPE (`fetchUwNope("SPX").catch(...).then(r => r ?? fetchUwNope("SPY")...)`); mirrored here as a sequential SPX-then-SPY try. **Sign convention, verified against live data, not just a docstring:** a live pull of `SPY`'s 25-delta risk reversal (29 daily rows, 2026-05-21..2026-07-02) was positive on EVERY row (+0.0067 to +0.0663). A "call IV minus put IV" definition would be predominantly negative for an equity index (the persistent put-side "volatility smirk" is one of the most robust stylized facts in index options) — a multi-week run of positive values under that definition would be the anomaly, not the norm. This confirms UW's `risk_reversal` here is effectively (put IV − call IV): positive = puts bid over calls = fear, matching `vol-metrics.ts`'s existing docstring. Provisional weight tiers (flat band <0.01, moderate ±4, extreme ±8 at >=0.05) are anchored to the observed live sample range and to two real named factors already in `spx-signals.ts` ("IV rank" ±4, "VIX curve" backwardation ±8).
- **Realized-vs-implied vol factor** (`factor_name: "realized_vs_implied_vol"`): Polygon primary (`fetchPolygonRealizedVol` + `fetchPolygonIvTermStructure`, nearest-30-DTE point — matching the exact primary source `get_realized_vol`/`get_iv_term_structure` already use in `largo/run-tool.ts`), UW's combined endpoint as an all-or-nothing fallback (never mixes a Polygon leg with a UW leg — keeps each observation one coherent snapshot). Mirrors `spx-signals.ts`'s real "VIX curve" factor's regime framing: implied running rich vs realized (spread > +0.02) scores bearish (elevated fear premium, same regime VIX backwardation scores), implied running cheap (spread < −0.02) scores bullish (calm/complacent, same regime VIX contango scores) — deliberately did NOT copy VIX curve's real ±8/+4 asymmetry (calibrated to VIX9D-vs-VIX3M specifically, an arbitrary transplant here), kept symmetric ±4/±8 instead.
- **Staleness guard, both factors:** UW's series here are once-daily historical rows (unlike `flow_anomalies`' 30-min-window WS-fed table), so freshness is checked by the latest row's own `date` against a 5-calendar-day window (covers a 3-day holiday weekend + processing lag) rather than a cluster-wide liveness flag — `reading === null` OR a stale `date` both collapse to `available:false`, never a fabricated flat/neutral zero. A Polygon-sourced vol-divergence reading has no `as_of_date` (computed live on every call) and is therefore never subject to this staleness check.
- Wiring: `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts::logSpxSkewShadowFactors(desk, confluence)`, added alongside the existing `logSpxShadowFactors` (both exported from the same file — no behavior of the first function touched). Called from `evaluateSpxPlay` in `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` immediately after the existing `logSpxShadowFactors` fire-and-forget call, wrapped in the same `firePlayTelemetry` helper, reading `confluence.score`/`.grade` from the same pre-Night-Hawk-bonus snapshot.

**PROOF THIS DOES NOT CHANGE LIVE SIGNALS:** `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` and `git diff main -- src/lib/providers/spx-desk.ts` are both **empty** for this PR — neither the confluence engine nor the desk builder was touched. `git grep spx-signals-shadow-skew src/lib/spx-signals.ts` returns nothing. The existing load-bearing test `src/lib/spx-signals.test.ts::"computeSpxConfluence: byte-for-byte unchanged output..."` still passes unmodified (same fixture, same frozen clock, same full-object assertion) — this PR adds nothing to that test because it adds nothing to `computeSpxConfluence`'s inputs or body. In `evaluateSpxPlay`, `logSpxSkewShadowFactors` is called from its own `firePlayTelemetry("logSpxSkewShadowFactors", ...)` statement, strictly after `confluence` is already computed and returned unconditionally above it — it cannot execute before `computeSpxConfluence` returns, and any exception inside it is caught/logged, never thrown into the caller.

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/nighthawk/vol-metrics.ts` (two new exported functions, additive only — `parseLatestRealizedVol`/`parseLatestRiskReversalSkew` and every existing caller, `nighthawk/dossier.ts` and `nighthawk/scorer.ts`, untouched); `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log.ts` (one new exported function + 3 new private helpers, `logSpxShadowFactors`/`maybeLogSpxPlay` untouched); `src/lib/spx-play-engine.ts` (one new import + one new fire-and-forget call, nothing else touched); two new files (`spx-signals-shadow-skew.ts` + its test). `SpxDeskPayload`, `buildSpxDesk()`, `db.ts` (schema/migrations), and every `computeSpxConfluence` call site are all unaffected.

**Separate finding surfaced during this investigation (NOT fixed here, logged for a follow-up PR):** `src/lib/nighthawk/scorer.ts::scoreSkewConfirmation`'s doc comment/logic ("positive RR skew = calls bid over puts = bullish") appears to have the sign backwards relative to the live UW data above and relative to `vol-metrics.ts`'s own docstring on the same field. That function feeds NightHawk's ticker-candidate scoring (`scoreCandidate`, a different subsystem from SPX Slayer's confluence engine) — out of scope to change in this PR (this PR touches SPX Slayer only, per the standing "one issue per branch/PR" policy), but worth a dedicated `fix/nighthawk-skew-sign` investigation+fix given it could be flipping a real scoring signal in production.

**Fix rationale:** kept the two factors in one new file (not folded into `spx-signals-shadow.ts`) because they share a fetch-and-parse concern (UW/Polygon HTTP, not a local Postgres read) genuinely different from the flow_anomalies factor's, mirroring the existing 1-file-per-provider split (`unusual-whales.ts` vs `polygon.ts` vs `polygon-options-gex.ts`) rather than merging unrelated data sources into one shadow file. Chose to fetch directly in the wiring function rather than extend `SpxDeskPayload` — see the Architecture decision above.

**Tests added:** `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-skew.test.ts` (15 cases — null/stale/fresh for both factors, flat-band/moderate/extreme tiers each direction, Polygon-sourced readings never staleness-gated); `src/lib/nighthawk/vol-metrics.test.ts` (8 cases covering the two new exports plus the live-shaped UW row fixtures); `src/lib/providers/spx-signal-log-skew.test.ts` (7 cases covering DB-not-configured short-circuit, the SPX-then-SPY skew fallback, Polygon-primary short-circuiting the UW fallback call, the UW fallback path, both-sources-unavailable, and the persisted row shape/count for a happy path). 30 new tests total.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite `1089/1089` passing (30 new). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand` / `lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — `spx-issues-sync` cron shipped without a `CRON_SERVICE_NAMES` entry — merged with a failing manifest check (BIE/Largo integration sweep, low, CI/ops)

**Where:** PR #463 (immediately below this entry) added the `spx-issues-sync` cron to `src/lib/cron-registry.ts` and its `railway.spx-issues-sync.toml` trigger, but never added a matching entry to `scripts/railway-cron-services.mjs`'s `CRON_SERVICE_NAMES` map — the table `railway-apply-cron-config.mjs`/`railway-audit-apply.mjs` use to reconcile the registry against Railway's actual provisioned services. `scripts/validate-railway-cron-manifest.mjs` (the CI `check` job) caught this correctly (`[FAIL] registry key "spx-issues-sync" missing from CRON_SERVICE_NAMES`) — but that check isn't a required branch-protection gate, so the PR's other required checks (`verify`, CodeQL) passed and auto-merge landed it on `main` anyway with a known, CI-flagged manifest drift.

**Fix:** added `"spx-issues-sync": "SPX-Issues-Sync"` to `CRON_SERVICE_NAMES`, matching the existing `SPX-`-prefixed Title-Case convention used by the other `spx-*` cron keys (`SPX-Engine-Evaluation`, `SPX-Signal-Observe`, `SPX-Signal-Weight-Optimize`). Re-ran `node scripts/validate-railway-cron-manifest.mjs` directly: `registry=24 toml=24 services=24` — GREEN.

**Blast radius:** one line in one config-mapping file. No runtime code changed — the cron itself (`/api/cron/spx-issues-sync`) was already correct and already firing on its Railway schedule; this only fixes the ops-tooling map used by scripts that reconcile against Railway's API, so a future `railway-audit-apply.mjs` run doesn't flag/mis-provision this service.

**Process note:** flagging for awareness, not blame — the `check` job firing correctly and still not blocking merge is itself worth a follow-up: either make `validate-railway-cron-manifest.mjs`'s `check` job a required status check, or have the per-PR sweep agents treat any CI failure (not just the ones GitHub currently gates on) as blocking before calling `enable_pr_auto_merge`.

**Verification:** `node scripts/validate-railway-cron-manifest.mjs` — GREEN. `npx tsc --noEmit` clean (no `.ts` changed). No test added — this is a static config-table fix already covered by the manifest validator script itself, which is what caught the gap in the first place.

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — SPX play/engine issue sync only ran when a human loaded the admin dashboard (BIE/Largo integration sweep, high — ops blind spot)
**Where:** `src/lib/admin-spx-issues.ts`'s `buildSpxAdminIssues()` computes real SPX play-engine health issues from live `SpxPlayPayload` state — `category:"play"` (Claude arbiter vetoes, gate blocks, gate warnings) and `category:"engine"` (play-engine heartbeat silent/stale). `src/lib/admin-spx-dashboard.ts:220-229`'s `fetchSpxAdminDashboard()` calls `buildSpxAdminIssues()` then `syncAdminIncidents(issues.issues, {resolveScope: (cat) => !cat.startsWith("data-integrity")})` to persist them into the shared `admin_incidents` table that BIE's discovery layer (`fetchDiscoveryIncidents()` in `src/lib/bie/discovery.ts`) reads to populate the member/admin "Open issues" panel.

**Root cause:** that sync sequence had exactly one caller — `GET`/`POST /api/admin/spx/dashboard` (`src/app/api/admin/spx/dashboard/route.ts`) — and nothing else. Confirmed via `grep` across `src/lib/cron-registry.ts` (the single source of truth for every scheduled job in this app, per its own header comment) that no cron entry referenced `admin-spx-dashboard`, `admin-spx-issues`, or `syncAdminIncidents`. So this sync was entirely gated on a human (or an external hit) happening to load that one admin page. If nobody viewed `/api/admin/spx/dashboard` for a stretch, BIE's "Open issues" feed silently went stale on SPX engine health — no error, no alert, just quietly out of date — a real blind spot for a live trading-signal engine's own health surface. This wasn't caught earlier because the admin page IS loaded routinely during manual audit/ops work, which masked the gap in every session where someone happened to be watching.

**Fix:** extracted the shared glue into a new importable function, `runSpxIssuesSync()` in new file `src/lib/spx-issues-sync.ts`: loads the merged SPX desk (`loadMergedSpxDesk`, same single cached desk lane every other consumer uses — no extra upstream Polygon/UW calls), builds a **read-only** play snapshot via `readSpxPlaySnapshot` (`mutate:false` — the exact same dry-run path the admin dashboard's `?live=1` view uses; it never writes play state, never fires Discord, and never advances `recordPlayEngineTick`, so it's safe to run unattended), feeds that into the existing `buildSpxAdminIssues()`, and syncs via the existing `syncAdminIncidents()`. Added a new cron route `src/app/api/cron/spx-issues-sync/route.ts` (auth via `isCronAuthorized`/`CRON_SECRET`, `requireDatabaseInProduction` guard, `isSpxEngineCronWindow` RTH gate with `?force=1` override, `logCronRun` — the exact idiom of `src/app/api/cron/provider-health-reconcile/route.ts`), registered it in `cron-registry.ts` as `spx-issues-sync` (`~Every 5 min (7AM–4PM ET)`, `stale_after_min: 20`, `weekdays_only`/`market_hours_only`, no `produces_member_alert` — it's a validator that opens admin incidents, like `data-integrity`/`provider-health-reconcile`, not a member-alert producer), and added the matching Railway cron-trigger config `railway.spx-issues-sync.toml` (`*/5 11-21 * * 1-5`, mirroring `railway.data-integrity.toml`/`railway.spx-evaluate.toml` — **every** existing registry entry has a 1:1 `railway.<key>.toml` trigger service, confirmed by diffing the two file lists; without this file the registry entry alone would never actually fire in production, which would have quietly reproduced the exact bug this PR fixes one layer down).

**Blast radius:** `admin-spx-dashboard.ts`'s inline `resolveScope: (cat) => !cat.startsWith("data-integrity")` predicate is the SAME namespace split the new cron needs, so it was pulled out to an exported `SPX_ISSUES_RESOLVE_SCOPE` constant in `spx-issues-sync.ts` and both call sites (the dashboard and the new cron) now import the one literal instead of maintaining two copies that could silently drift apart. No other call site computes or syncs this issue set.

**Fix rationale:** `buildSpxAdminIssues` and `syncAdminIncidents` were already plain exported functions — the only missing piece was the glue (load desk → read-only play snapshot → build issues → sync), so the new function is a thin composition rather than a refactor of either. Deliberately used the dry-run/read-only play snapshot (matching the admin dashboard's own `?live=1` default) instead of the mutating `runSpxEvaluator` path — the mutating tick is already owned by the `spx-evaluate` cron on the same 5-min cadence; duplicating it here would double-fire Discord/state writes for no benefit, since this cron only needs to READ current play state to classify issues. Chose a new dedicated cron route over an HTTP self-call to `/api/admin/spx/dashboard` (avoids an internal network hop, admin-auth plumbing, and the dashboard's unrelated analytics/lotto/terminal-feed work) and over piggy-backing on the existing `spx-evaluate` or `provider-health-reconcile` crons (each has a distinct, unrelated purpose/namespace — bolting this on would blur what each cron owns). Cadence matches `spx-evaluate`/`data-integrity` (every 5 min, 7AM–4PM ET) rather than a slower interval, since this reconciler surfaces the SAME heartbeat those crons drive and needs to catch a stale/silent engine on their cadence, not lag behind it; the route self-skips outside the RTH window so off-hours ticks are cheap no-ops.

**Verification:** new route test `src/app/api/cron/spx-issues-sync/route.test.ts` (4 cases: 401 when unauthorized touches nothing; RTH-window skip never calls sync; success path proves `syncAdminIncidents` is called exactly once with the exact issues array `buildSpxAdminIssues` returned, and that the resolveScope predicate matches `SPX_ISSUES_RESOLVE_SCOPE`'s data-integrity exclusion; a thrown sync error logs a failed cron run and returns 500) — run standalone via `npx tsx --test` and passing. `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full `npm test` suite green; `npm run build` clean; `npm run lint:brand` / `npm run lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — `fetchEcosystemContext()` never read SPX Slayer's own tables — the play engine was invisible to itself (BIE/Largo integration sweep, medium)
**Where:** `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts::fetchEcosystemContext(ticker)` is BIE's per-ticker cross-instrument snapshot — the single query layer that the admin BIE report, Largo's `get_ecosystem_context` tool, and precedent-search ingestion all flow through to answer "what does the rest of the platform know about this ticker." Its `EcosystemContext` type (lines 76-94 pre-fix) read `zerodte_setup_log` (`zerodte_today`), `nighthawk_play_outcomes` (`nighthawk_recent`), `alert_audit_log` (`recent_audit_entries`), and `flow_alerts`/`flow_anomalies` (`recent_flow`/`recent_anomalies`) — every cross-instrument write path EXCEPT SPX Slayer's own `spx_open_play`/`spx_play_outcomes`/`spx_signal_log`. Confirmed by grep: zero references to any `spx_*` table anywhere in `ecosystem-context.ts` before this fix. So a member or Largo asking this function "what's going on with SPX" got 0DTE + Night Hawk + flow, but never SPX Slayer's own live/recent play state — the one instrument this sweep is strengthening BIE/Largo integration for.

**Fix:** added `spx_play: EcosystemSpxPlay | null` to `EcosystemContext`, shaped `{ open_play: {...} | null, last_closed: {...} | null }` — deliberately a single most-recent open + single most-recent closed play, matching `nighthawk_recent`'s "one current take, not a history array" precedent rather than `recent_audit_entries`'s list shape. Populated ONLY when `ticker` is `"SPX"` or `"SPXW"`; `null` for every other ticker. Sourced via the exact fetchers `src/lib/platform/spx-service.ts` already calls for the same tables (`getSpxOpenPlay` → `fetchOpenSpxPlay(todayEtYmd())`; `getSpxTradeHistory` → `fetchClosedPlayOutcomes(limit)`, here called with `limit=1` since only the most recent closed play is needed) — no new SQL, no new write path, both imported straight from `src/lib/db.ts`.

**Ticker-scoping note (why a conditional fetch, not a `WHERE ticker = $1`):** `zerodte_today`/`nighthawk_recent` scope to the requested ticker via a SQL `WHERE` clause because their source tables carry a `ticker` column. `spx_open_play`/`spx_play_outcomes` carry **no ticker column at all** (confirmed against their `CREATE TABLE` in `db.ts`) — SPX Slayer is a single-instrument engine, so there's nothing to filter on. `spx_play` is scoped instead by only calling `fetchOpenSpxPlay`/`fetchClosedPlayOutcomes` when `ticker.toUpperCase()` is `SPX`/`SPXW`, so a non-SPX ticker gets `null` without a query ever running (verified in the new test via a call counter).

**Blast radius:** additive-only. `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELD_DESCRIPTIONS` (the `Record<keyof EcosystemContext, string>` that machine-generates BIE's own `platform:bie-capabilities` knowledge doc in `knowledge.ts`) required a matching `spx_play` entry — a compile-time-enforced mapping, so this was a `tsc` error, not an optional nicety, until added. `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts`'s `get_ecosystem_context` case returns `fetchEcosystemContext(ticker)` directly with no per-field serialization, so the new field surfaces to Largo automatically with no code change there. `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts`'s `get_ecosystem_context` tool description was updated (small, additive) to mention `spx_play` so Largo's own system-prompt-level tool description doesn't undersell what the tool now returns. `src/app/api/admin/bie-report/route.ts` does NOT call `fetchEcosystemContext` at all (checked directly — it composes its own independent set of probes), so no change was needed there. No write path, no schema change, no existing field's shape changed.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean (confirms the `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELD_DESCRIPTIONS` compile-time contract stayed satisfied). Full suite `1023/1023` passing — 4 new/updated tests in `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.test.ts` using the `mock.module("../db", ...)` pattern from `nighthawk/platform-intel-snapshot.test.ts`: `spx_play.open_play` populates correctly for ticker `SPX` when an open play exists; `spx_play.last_closed` reflects the most recent closed play for ticker `SPXW`; `spx_play` is `null` for a non-SPX ticker (`AAPL`) AND the SPX-only fetchers are proven never called via a call counter; plus the pre-existing `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELDS` coverage test extended with `spx_play`. `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## 🧠 BIE calibration gains SPX Slayer awareness SHIPPED 2026-07-04 — two self-improving loops, one report (branch `fix/bie-calibration-spx-slayer`)
**Gap:** `src/lib/bie/calibration.ts`'s `runBieCalibration()` — BIE's Layer-5 gate-calibration harness — read ONLY `zerodte_setup_log` (0DTE Command's ledger), bucketed by score band / time-of-day / spike, and produced evidence-gated (n≥10) recommendations. It had zero awareness that SPX Slayer runs its OWN separate, already-live adaptive-gate calibration loop: `src/lib/spx-play-telemetry.ts`'s `loadAdaptivePlayGates()` reads `fetchPlayOutcomeStats()` (`src/lib/spx-play-outcomes.ts`, backed by `fetchClosedPlayOutcomes` over `spx_play_outcomes`) and feeds real `global_min_score_boost`/`promote_min_score_boost` adjustments into `spx-play-engine.ts`. Two self-improving loops on the same platform had never been introduced to each other — BIE's own calibration report was blind to a whole product's outcome data, even though the fetcher it needed already existed.

**Fix — read-only analytics addition, does NOT touch the live engine:** `calibration.ts` now runs a second, parallel bucketing pass over `spx_play_outcomes` (via the SAME `fetchClosedPlayOutcomes` fetcher `spx-play-telemetry.ts` already uses — no new SQL) alongside the existing 0DTE pass. New pure functions `computeSpxCalibration`/`formatSpxCalibration` bucket SPX Slayer's own closed plays by **grade band** (`A/A+` / `B` / `C/D`, via the existing `gradeRank` from `spx-play-config.ts` so the band edges can't drift from the live grade-floor gate) and by the **same 4 time-of-day windows** 0DTE already uses (deliberately identical boundaries so the two sections read side by side), applying the identical n≥10 evidence gate before emitting any recommendation. Win/loss classification uses the play's own graded `outcome` field (`spx-play-outcomes.ts`'s `classifyOutcome`, which already handles STOP/TARGET/TRAIL/THESIS/THETA/SESSION exit nuance) rather than a raw pnl-sign check, so breakevens are counted as neither a win nor a loss. `CalibrationReport` gains one additive, nullable field — `spx_slayer: SpxCalibrationReport | null` — set by the new `runBieCalibration()` orchestration step (`computeSpxSlayerCalibration`, isolated in its own try/catch so an SPX-side DB hiccup can never take down the 0DTE half of the report); `computeCalibration()` itself is untouched and always seeds `spx_slayer: null`, so no existing caller's shape or test changes. `formatCalibration()` now labels its own section "0DTE Command calibration" (was bare "BIE calibration") and appends a clearly separated `---`-delimited "SPX Slayer calibration" section when `spx_slayer` is attached — both sections keep fully separate bucket sets and recommendation lists, never merged.

**Explicitly NOT touched (blast radius):** `spx-play-telemetry.ts` and `spx-play-engine.ts` — SPX Slayer's live adaptive-gate loop (`loadAdaptivePlayGates`, `computeAdaptiveGates`, `effectiveFullMinScore`/`effectivePromoteMinScore`) reads `fetchPlayOutcomeStats()` exactly as before; this PR adds a second, independent read of the same underlying table for reporting only, never feeding anything back into what score-floor/promote adjustments actually apply. `/api/admin/bie-report/route.ts` needed NO code change — it already forwards the whole `CalibrationReport` object as `calibration.data` and `formatCalibration(calibration)` as `calibration.text`, so the new field and section flow through automatically; `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` only ever rendered `calibration.text` in a `<pre>` block, so the richer text renders with zero frontend changes.

**Verification:** 5 new tests in `src/lib/bie/bie.test.ts` (nearest existing test file for `calibration.ts` — no dedicated `calibration.test.ts` exists; 0DTE's own calibration tests already live there) — SPX buckets by grade band and cites evidence; refuses to recommend below n=10 (mirrors the existing 0DTE thin-evidence test); excludes `outcome: "open"` rows from every bucket; combined report shows both "0DTE Command calibration" and "SPX Slayer calibration" headers; without an attached SPX pass the report stays 0DTE-only text (no restructuring). Full suite `1025/1025` passing, `npx tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm run build` clean, `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — SPX Claude play-gate's fabrication guard checked the thesis but not the headline (SPX Slayer/BIE sweep finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/spx-play-claude.ts`'s `evaluateClaudePlayApproval()` builds a `ClaudePlayVerdict` with both a `headline` (max 12 words) and a `thesis` (2 sentences) — the prompt (line ~362) explicitly instructs Claude to put "a specific level or catalyst" in the headline, so it is just as likely to cite a price level as the thesis is. Both fields ship verbatim onto the real-money 0DTE play card the same way. But the post-generation FABRICATION GUARD added by the earlier "SPX Claude play-gate thesis had no fabrication guard" fix (this doc, below) only ever called `checkNumbersGrounded(result.thesis, known)` — `result.headline` was never passed to the guard at all. A hallucinated number confined to the headline (e.g. Claude inventing "Breakout toward next major level 6120" when nothing in `knownPlayLevels()` is anywhere near 6120) would sail straight past the guard, get cached, get audit-logged, and ship to paying members — while an identical fabrication in the thesis one field over was already being caught. This was found while auditing the SPX Slayer engine's BIE/Largo integration surface for exactly this class of gap (a check applied to one sibling field but not another).

**Why it wasn't caught earlier:** the original fabrication-guard fix (and its test) treated "the thesis" as a stand-in for "Claude's free text," matching the pattern of `gex-heatmap/explain`'s `narrativeLevelsAreGrounded` (which only ever had one narrative string to check). `spx-play-claude.ts` is the only one of the six `checkNumbersGrounded` call sites with two independently-hallucinate-able free-text fields shipping to the same card — `spx-commentary.ts` was built (or later fixed) to already join `` `${headline}\n${body}` `` before checking, but `spx-play-claude.ts`'s two-field shape was never cross-checked against that sibling.

**Fix:** `checkNumbersGrounded` now runs against `` `${result.headline} ${result.thesis}` `` (joined, mirroring `spx-commentary.ts`'s existing `headline+body` join) instead of `result.thesis` alone — so a fabricated number in either field trips the same guard. On failure, the fallback path is unchanged in shape: discard the whole Claude verdict (not just the offending field) and fall back to `mechanicalVerdict()`, still audit-logged via `logPlayVerdict()`. Renamed the `trigger_reason` string passed to `logPlayVerdict()` from `"ungrounded_claude_thesis"` to `"ungrounded_claude_verdict"` since it can now fire for a headline-only fabrication too and the old name would be actively misleading in the audit trail; confirmed (via repo-wide grep) this string has exactly one producer (`spx-play-claude.ts`) and no consumer pattern-matches its literal value — `trigger_reason` is read everywhere else (`AdminBieDashboard.tsx`, `ecosystem-context.ts`, `precedent-search.ts`) as an opaque display/context string, so the rename is safe.

**Blast radius:** scoped to the one grounding check and its log label in `spx-play-claude.ts`. Did not touch the five other `checkNumbersGrounded` call sites (`gex-heatmap/explain`, `flow-brief`, `spx-commentary.ts`, `nights-watch/position-narrative.ts`, `nighthawk/play-critic.ts`, `nighthawk/play-explainer.ts`) — each already checks its own single narrative string (or, for `spx-commentary.ts`, an already-joined `headline+body`), so none share this two-separately-checked-fields gap.

**Fix rationale:** joining the two fields into one `checkNumbersGrounded` call (rather than two independent calls) was chosen to match the existing `spx-commentary.ts` precedent exactly and because the guard's contract is "does this text cite any number outside the known set" — a single joined call and two independent calls are behaviorally equivalent here (either failure is treated identically: discard the whole verdict), so the simpler one-call form was preferred.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite `1024/1024` passing — extended `src/lib/spx-play-claude.test.ts` with: (1) two new unit-level cases proving a headline-only hallucinated level fails the joined `` `${headline} ${thesis}` `` check even though the thesis alone is fully grounded (and passes when both are grounded), directly mirroring the file's existing thesis-only unit tests; (2) two new full-integration cases that actually call `evaluateClaudePlayApproval()` end-to-end with `node:test`'s `mock.module` swapping in a fake `providers/anthropic` (mirroring `nighthawk/play-critic.test.ts`'s pattern for the same bug class) and `DATABASE_URL`/`DATABASE_PUBLIC_URL` blanked before import (mirroring `nighthawk/discovery-quality.test.ts`, since this sandbox's ambient `DATABASE_URL` points at a Railway-internal host this environment cannot reach) — proving a Claude response with a grounded headline+thesis is approved as-is, and one with a fabricated headline number falls back to `source: "mechanical"` with the mechanical (not the fabricated Claude) headline, even though its thesis is independently fully grounded. This closes the gap the original fix's own verification note flagged ("Full async pipeline — Claude calls, DB caching — not mocked/tested; no existing test harness for that in this file's sibling `spx-play-*.test.ts` files.") — `spx-play-claude.test.ts` now has one. `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — Live Desk AI grounding-failure discard had no durable audit trail (SPX Slayer/BIE integration sweep, medium)
**Where:** `src/lib/providers/spx-commentary.ts`'s `generateSpxCommentary()` runs `checkNumbersGrounded()` against the generated headline+body (the fabrication guard added earlier this session — see the "Flagship SPX Live Desk AI commentary had no fabrication guard" entry below) and, on failure, just `return null` (line ~597-602 pre-fix) — the caller (`src/app/api/market/spx/commentary/route.ts`) 502s to the client with the rejected text discarded and nothing durable recorded, only an ephemeral `console.warn`. This is the flagship "Live Desk AI" rail on the SPX Slayer dashboard, one shared Claude Haiku call every ~5 minutes cached cluster-wide, so a hallucinated read there is a real, repeatable event worth a trace.

**Contrast that exposed the gap:** the sibling AI-narration surface, `src/lib/spx-play-claude.ts`'s `logPlayVerdict()` (added the same day this same fabrication-guard work landed on that file), writes a real row to the shared `alert_audit_log` table via `insertAlertAuditLog` on EVERY verdict — pass or fail — with `alert_type: "spx_claude_play"`. `spx-commentary.ts` got the identical grounding guard in the same audit pass but never got the matching audit-log write, so there was (and until this fix, remained) zero historical trace of how often the dashboard's headline AI rail silently throws away a hallucinated read — an observability gap on the platform's single most-viewed AI surface.

**Fix:** added `logUngroundedCommentary(desk, ctx, parsed, grounding)`, called synchronously (never awaited, matching `logPlayVerdict`'s call shape exactly) from the existing `if (!grounding.grounded)` branch, immediately before its unchanged `return null`. It fire-and-forgets a `alert_type: "spx_commentary_ungrounded"` row via `insertAlertAuditLog` (guarded by the same `dbConfigured()` early-return `logPlayVerdict` uses, and a `.catch(err => console.error(...))` so a DB hiccup can never throw into `generateSpxCommentary`'s control flow): `source_table: "spx_commentary"`, `source_key: {price, as_of}`, `ticker: "SPX"`, `direction` set to the model's (untrusted) `bias` so a reviewer can see what stance it was hallucinating in, `confidence_score`/`confidence_label` pulled from the same deterministic `ctx.confluence.score`/`.grade` the prompt itself was built from (never a model self-grade, matching the table's own column-comment contract), `trigger_reason` naming the specific ungrounded value, `decision_trace: [{check: "numbers_grounded", passed: false, value: <the value>}]`, and — the part that actually lets someone reconstruct what was rejected — `final_output: {headline, body, bias}` holding the raw generated text verbatim (otherwise unrecoverable once discarded) plus an `input_snapshot` of the handful of desk levels (price/vwap/gamma_flip/gex_king/max_pain) the model was looking at, without dumping the whole deeply-nested `ctx` object into every rejected row.

**Blast radius:** purely additive — the success path (`return parsed`) and the existing failure path's `console.warn` + `return null` contract to the caller are byte-for-byte unchanged; the caller's 502 behavior on a `null` return is untouched. No other call site references `generateSpxCommentary`'s grounding branch.

**Fix rationale:** mirrored `logPlayVerdict`'s exact shape (module-level `function ...(): void` that internally fire-and-forgets, called synchronously with no `await`/`void` at the call site) rather than inventing a new pattern, since this task is explicitly about closing the asymmetry between the two sibling AI-narration surfaces. Considered logging on the SUCCESS path too (for parity with `logPlayVerdict` logging both outcomes) but deliberately did not — the success path already has zero observability gap (the commentary itself gets served and cached, which is its own record), and the standing instruction here scoped this purely to the discard branch.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; new `src/lib/providers/spx-commentary.test.ts` (mocks `./anthropic`, `../grounding-guard`, and `../db` per this repo's `mock.module()` idiom — bare specifiers resolve relative to the test file, not the `@/` alias `spx-commentary.ts` itself uses) with 3 cases: a forced-ungrounded generation returns `null` AND fires exactly one `alert_type: "spx_commentary_ungrounded"` audit row with the expected shape; a grounded generation passes through untouched and never touches the audit log; and the write is skipped (while the `null` return stays unchanged) when `dbConfigured()` is false. Full suite passing; `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — Largo had no way to compare SPX Slayer vs Night Hawk without synthesizing the arithmetic itself — a "true numbers, false derived conclusion" grounding blind spot (SPX Slayer ↔ BIE/Largo integration sweep, medium)

**Where:** `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts` — Largo's two performance tools, `get_setup_stats`/`get_trade_history` (SPX Slayer, reads `spx_play_outcomes` via `src/lib/platform/spx-service.ts`, around line 877-885) and `get_nighthawk_outcomes` (Night Hawk, reads `nighthawk_play_outcomes`, around line 1253-1268), return structurally DIFFERENT schemas: SPX exposes win-rate/pnl_pts by grade; Night Hawk returns raw target/stop/open rows and leaves hit-rate interpretation to the caller. Neither accepts a shared, consistent time window either — SPX's `days` and Night Hawk's `window_days` are independent rolling-day-count params, not a real calendar week. A question like "how's SPX Slayer doing vs Night Hawk this week" forced Largo to call both tools and then synthesize the comparison — a subtraction, a "X points hotter than Y" — itself, in free text.

**Why this is a real correctness risk, not just an inconvenience:** the numeric-grounding verifier (`src/lib/bie/verifier.ts`, consumed by `largo-verifier.ts`) checks that every individual number an answer cites traces back to a real tool result (`extractNumericClaims` + `collectContextNumbers` + trace-back) — it has no concept of a *derived* claim. It cannot distinguish a correct subtraction of two real numbers from a confidently wrong one. Every raw number in a bad synthesized comparison ("SPX Slayer is running 12 points hotter than Night Hawk this week") could be genuine and independently traceable, and the verifier would still mark the whole answer grounded. This is the "true numbers, false derived conclusion" class of bug — the numbers check out, the conclusion drawn from them doesn't, and today's tooling has no way to catch that.

**Fix:** new Largo tool, `get_spx_vs_nighthawk_comparison` (`src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts`, registered in `TOOL_GROUPS.platform` alongside `get_nighthawk_outcomes`/`get_nighthawk_dossier` so it's offered whenever `NIGHTHAWK_RE` matches the question), that computes the comparison server-side, once:
1. **SPX side** — new `fetchPlayOutcomeStatsForWindow(days)` in `src/lib/spx-play-outcomes.ts`, a windowed sibling of the existing `fetchPlayOutcomeStats()`. It reuses the same SQL fetcher (`fetchClosedPlayOutcomes`) and the same pure aggregator (`computePlayOutcomeStats`) rather than re-deriving either, applying the identical closed_at-falls-back-to-opened_at day-cutoff pattern `getSpxTradeHistory` already uses in `spx-service.ts`. `fetchPlayOutcomeStats()` itself is deliberately left untouched — it backs the public track-record page, the shadow-recompute cross-check, and admin analytics, all of which want the all-time number, not a rolling window; repurposing it would have risked regressing three unrelated consumers.
2. **Night Hawk side** — calls the existing `fetchNighthawkOutcomeAnalytics(days)` directly (same fetcher `get_nighthawk_outcomes` already uses) and derives win/loss the same way `src/lib/nighthawk/analytics.ts`'s `winRate()` does (`outcome === "target"` = win, `"stop"` = loss, everything else excluded from the rate denominator as not-yet-decided).
3. Both sides share one clamped `days` param (1-180, default 7, mirroring `get_nighthawk_outcomes`' existing `window_days` clamp) applied identically to both products, and the tool description explicitly documents `days` as a rolling window, not a calendar week — matching this codebase's established honest-approximation convention rather than pretending to a precision the data doesn't have.
4. The response returns each product's `*_win_rate`/`*_signal_count` plus a pre-computed `win_rate_delta` (`spx_win_rate - nighthawk_win_rate`) and `signal_count_delta` — computed once, in code, so Largo only ever repeats a number the platform already produced instead of subtracting two tool results itself. In-code comments in the new `run-tool.ts` dispatch case spell out why this tool exists (the grounding blind spot above) for future readers.

**Blast radius:** one new tool + its dispatcher case + one new sibling fetcher — `get_setup_stats`, `get_trade_history`, and `get_nighthawk_outcomes` are all unchanged, still callable independently exactly as before. No schema change to any existing tool or table.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1030/1030` passing (3 new in `src/lib/largo/run-tool.test.ts` — a mixed win/loss fixture across both products proving the correct win rate, signal count, and pre-computed delta, including that a 10-day-old SPX row is excluded from a 7-day window; the all-omitted-input default-to-7-days case; and the days-param clamp for both an oversized and a non-numeric input). New test mocks `@/lib/db` via `mock.module()` (spreading the real module's exports before overriding `fetchClosedPlayOutcomes`/`fetchNighthawkOutcomeAnalytics`, since `namedExports` fully replaces rather than merges with the real module) and stubs the `server-only` marker package (run-tool.ts transitively imports `gex-positioning.ts`, which throws outside Next's own webpack "react-server" condition — same class of issue already documented further down in this file's `largo-verifier.ts` entry). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — `portfolioGreeks` aggregation in `/api/account/positions` skipped `roundFloats()` (follow-up audit finding, low — last of the 9)
**Where:** `src/app/api/account/positions/route.ts`'s `GET` handler builds `portfolioGreeks` (delta/gamma/theta/vega/totalPremiumAtRisk/totalDeltaDollars) via a `reduce` over open legs' raw valuation greeks, then returned it straight in the JSON response with no rounding — unlike the sibling per-position fields in `enrichPosition` (`current_value`, `unrealized_pnl`, `pnl_pct`, etc.), which are all rounded via inline `.toFixed(2)` before being serialized.

**Currently inert, confirmed by tracing the one consumer:** `src/components/nights-watch/NightsWatchPanel.tsx` destructures `data.portfolioGreeks` (line ~1369) but never actually reads it — it calls its own local `computePortfolioGreeks(positions)` (defined in the same file) instead, both where the aggregate is displayed and where `liveLegs` is read. So today this bug produces no visible float noise; it's a live landmine for the moment anything (a future UI change, a Largo/BIE tool, an external API consumer) starts reading the field the route already documents itself as providing.

**Fix:** wrapped the field in `roundFloats()` before the response: `portfolioGreeks: roundFloats(portfolioGreeks)`. Left `positions` (the `enriched` array) alone — its numeric fields are already rounded via `enrichPosition`'s own inline `.toFixed()` calls, so wrapping the whole response would be redundant.

**Noted but NOT fixed here (out of scope for this fix):** whether `NightsWatchPanel.tsx` should be changed to consume the server-computed `portfolioGreeks` instead of its own client-side `computePortfolioGreeks` recomputation is a design question, not a correctness bug — the client computation isn't wrong, just duplicated. Left for a separate decision rather than folded into this fix.

**Blast radius:** one field, one route. No consumer currently reads it, so no behavior change is observable today — this fix only prevents a future consumer from inheriting unrounded floats.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1013/1013` passing (no new test — `roundFloats()` already has its own direct unit coverage in `round-floats.test.ts`, and this route has no existing test file to extend, matching the precedent set by the earlier `positions/[id]/detail/route.ts` `roundFloats` fix, which also didn't add a route-level test). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — `uw-socket.ts`/`stocks-socket.ts` reconnect backoff had no jitter (follow-up audit finding, low-medium)
**Where:** `polygon-socket.ts` and `options-socket.ts` both add `Math.floor(Math.random() * 400)` jitter to their reconnect backoff delay; `uw-socket.ts`'s `scheduleReconnect()` and `stocks-socket.ts`'s `scheduleStocksReconnect()` didn't — the delay was a plain exponential backoff with no randomization.

**Why it matters, especially now:** masked in normal single-leader operation (only one replica ever holds each socket, so there's no peer to collide with). But it compounds the split-brain fencing fix immediately above: two replicas that BOTH briefly believed they were leader (during a stall-then-fence-detection window) and got disconnected by the same upstream blip would, without jitter, reconnect at the exact same moment instead of staggered — the opposite of what jitter exists to prevent.

**Fix:** added the identical `Math.floor(Math.random() * 400)` jitter term to both files' reconnect delay computation, matching `polygon-socket.ts`/`options-socket.ts` exactly. `uw-socket.ts`'s auth-failure cooldown branch (a fixed "wait until this deadline" cooldown, not an exponential backoff) was deliberately left unjittered — jitter doesn't apply to a fixed-deadline wait the way it does to a churn-avoidance backoff.

**Blast radius:** the two reconnect-delay computations only — no change to backoff caps, auth-failure cooldown logic, or any other reconnect behavior.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1013/1013` passing (no new tests — `scheduleReconnect`/`scheduleStocksReconnect` aren't exported for direct testing, matching the precedent that `polygon-socket.ts`'s and `options-socket.ts`'s own jitter isn't unit-tested either). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — WS/cron leader locks split-brain under a stalled leader — no fencing token (follow-up audit finding, high)
**Where:** all 5 Redis SETNX cluster-leader locks in the codebase — `src/lib/ws/uw-socket.ts`, `polygon-socket.ts`, `options-socket.ts`, `stocks-socket.ts`, and `src/lib/rth-warm-leader.ts` (the 5th manager fixed immediately above). Each acquires with `SET key "1" EX ttl NX` — a **constant** value, never a per-replica identity — then renews on a timer via an **unconditional** `EXPIRE(key, ttl)` and releases via an unconditional `DEL(key)`, neither of which ever checks that the key still belongs to the replica calling them.

**The split-brain sequence:** replica A acquires the lock. A stalls past the lock's TTL (GC pause, a slow synchronous call, event-loop backlog under load — all normal Node.js realities, not exotic failures). The key expires in Redis. Replica B's next acquire attempt wins (`SETNX` succeeds against no key). A resumes. A's own renewal timer fires next, sees its local `isLeader` flag is still (stale) `true`, and calls `EXPIRE(key, ttl)` — blindly re-arming the TTL on a key that now belongs to B, with no check that A still owns it. Both A and B now believe they hold leadership indefinitely (the key never naturally expires again, since both keep renewing it), with **no alert or log signal** that anything is wrong. Each of the 4 WS sockets opens its own live connection to an upstream that permits only ONE connection per API key — both get bounced/throttled by the vendor, and `rth-warm-leader.ts` dispatches every cron-warm target from two replicas at once.

**Fix:** new `src/lib/ws/leader-lock-fencing.ts` — each acquirer now writes a random per-process `crypto.randomUUID()` token instead of the constant `"1"`. Renew and release are now atomic Lua check-and-act scripts (`redis.eval`): `renewFencedLock` only extends the TTL if `GET(key) === myToken`, returning `false` (not just silently no-op'ing) when it isn't — the caller then explicitly sets `isLeader = false` and logs a "lost cluster lead… standing down" warning instead of continuing to believe it's leader. `releaseFencedLock` only deletes the key if it's still mine, so a stalled-then-resumed replica's shutdown path can never delete a lock a different replica has since legitimately acquired. All 5 files call the same two shared functions rather than re-deriving the check-and-act logic 5 times. Each of the 4 WS sockets already had its own leadership-gated reconcile tick (running every 10-15s, well inside every lock's 25-45s TTL) that re-checks leadership and calls the socket's `standDown()`/close — so once the renewal detects the loss and flips the flag, the existing reconcile loop closes the now-illegitimate connection within one tick, no new teardown path needed. `rth-warm-leader.ts`'s next 60s `tick()` does the same via its own existing `!isLeader` re-acquire check.

**Blast radius:** exactly these 5 files' leader-lock acquire/renew/release call sites — no other logic in any of them (message handling, subscription management, reconcile cadence, watchdogs) was touched. `leader-lock-fencing.ts` is a new, standalone module (only imports `node:crypto`) — it doesn't touch `leader-lock-shared.ts`'s existing `REPLICA_COUNT` fail-open/closed policy, which is unrelated (fencing protects against a stalled-but-alive leader; the fail-open policy protects against Redis itself being unavailable — both bugs could occur independently or together).

**Fix rationale:** a random-token-plus-Lua-check-and-act is the standard, minimal-correct fencing pattern for this exact class of lock (the well-known "Redlock safe release" shape) — it was chosen over a full distributed-lock library (e.g. Redlock across multiple Redis instances) because this codebase already trusts a single Redis instance for these locks (see `leader-lock-shared.ts`'s own reasoning for why single-Redis SETNX is an accepted tradeoff here), so only the ownership-check gap needed closing, not the underlying single-point-of-failure model.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1009/1009` passing (5 new in `leader-lock-fencing.test.ts` — renew succeeds/fails correctly on token match/mismatch, release deletes only on match and is a safe no-op otherwise, and token uniqueness). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — `/api/market/quote` REST fallback had no negative-result cache — sustained outage = unbounded retries + log spam (follow-up audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/app/api/market/quote/route.ts`'s `getRestQuote()` only cached SUCCESSFUL snapshots (`quoteMem`/Redis, 5s TTL). A failed upstream call (vendor 404, timeout, empty snapshot) returned `null` with nothing cached, so the very next poll — this route is deliberately polled every ~1.5s per open tab for the live GEX-header tape — re-attempted the exact same upstream call. During a sustained vendor-side outage (the trigger: a benign-but-real `[market/quote] REST quote failed for SPY: ... → 404` observed in production logs over the extended July 4th holiday weekend, traced and confirmed to be vendor snapshot-cache flakiness, not a broken endpoint/URL), every poll from every open tab on every one of 5 replicas re-hit the upstream with zero backoff — wasted vendor-call budget for the full duration of the outage. Separately, `console.warn` fired on every single failed attempt with no rate-limiting, so a multi-hour or multi-day outage produced a wall of identical, alarming-looking log lines that gave no signal of whether this was a fresh problem or the same ongoing one.

**Fix:** added a short negative-result cache (`quoteFailureMem`, 3s TTL — shorter than the 5s positive-cache window since a real recovery should be picked up quickly) that `getRestQuote()` checks before even attempting L1/L2/upstream, so a ticker mid-outage returns `{available:false}` immediately without touching the upstream. Paired with `quoteFailureWarned`, a per-ticker "already logged this outage" set: the first failure after a success logs one `console.warn`; every subsequent failure while still in the outage window is silent; the warning re-arms only once a success clears both maps. Net effect: one log line per outage (not one per poll), and upstream call volume during a sustained outage drops to roughly 1 per ticker per 3s cluster-wide instead of 1 per ticker per ~1.5s per open tab per replica.

**Blast radius:** `getRestQuote()` only — the WS path (`indexStore` direct read) and the positive-cache path are both unchanged. `{available:false}` was already the exact response shape on any failure before this fix; callers see no contract change, just fewer redundant upstream calls and quieter logs during a real outage.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1007/1007` passing (3 new in a new `route.test.ts` for this route, using `mock.module()` to stub the upstream/auth/cache dependencies per the pattern established in `platform/intel/route.test.ts`: a failed snapshot returns `available:false` and logs exactly once; a second poll for the same ticker within the negative-cache window neither re-hits the upstream nor re-warns; a different ticker's success is unaffected by another ticker's failure cache). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — 9 more hand-rolled ET-date duplicates found consolidating the 4 the audit flagged (follow-up audit finding, medium)
**Where:** the follow-up audit flagged 4 files (`spx-play-engine.ts:851`, `spx-signals.ts:80`, `nighthawk/agents/day-trade-filters.ts:90`, `nighthawk/hunt-builder.ts:87`) still hand-rolling `Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", {timeZone:"America/New_York"})` instead of importing `todayEt()` from `et-date.ts`. Before fixing just those 4, grepped the whole codebase for the exact same literal pattern to get real blast-radius coverage (per this repo's PR-writeup policy: fix and note every call site touched by the same root cause, not just the one flagged) — found **5 more** in `greek-exposure-summary.ts:33`, `providers/polygon.ts:226`, `providers/macro-events.ts` (3 separate call sites: `:237`, `:259`, `:396`), `api/cron/nighthawk-edition/route.ts:57`, `api/cron/nighthawk-morning-confirm/route.ts:142`, and `components/desk/GexHeatmap.tsx:2665` (a client component — safe to consolidate since `et-date.ts`'s header explicitly documents it as "importable from server engines/stores AND from client modules").

**Fix:** all 9 sites now call `todayEt()` (aliased where a file already had its own local `todayEt` variable name or a colliding same-named import from `nighthawk/session.ts` — see Fix rationale). Two files (`providers/polygon.ts`, `providers/macro-events.ts`) already imported `todayEtYmd`/`todayEt` from the earlier consolidation for OTHER call sites in the same file but had these specific lines missed — a reminder that "the file already imports the helper" doesn't guarantee every call site in it uses it.

**Fix rationale — naming collisions handled per-file:**
- `nighthawk/agents/day-trade-filters.ts` and `nighthawk/hunt-builder.ts` each had a local `const todayEt = ...` variable — imported the shared function under an alias (`import { todayEt as todayEtStr }`) so the local variable name (and every downstream reference to it in the same function) stayed unchanged.
- `api/cron/nighthawk-morning-confirm/route.ts` already imports a **different, zero-argument** `todayEt` from `@/lib/nighthawk/session` (itself a thin wrapper delegating to the same canonical `et-date.ts` implementation) — but this call site needed the parameterized form (`todayEt(new Date(ms))`, converting an arbitrary bar timestamp, not "today"). Importing the real `todayEt` under a second identifier (`import { todayEt as etYmdOf }`) avoided a duplicate-import compile error while preserving the existing zero-arg call sites elsewhere in the same file untouched.
- `api/cron/nighthawk-edition/route.ts` already imports the *same* correctly-delegating `todayEt` from `nighthawk/session.ts` with a compatible zero-arg call shape — no new import needed, the raw inline computation was simply replaced with a call to what was already in scope.

**Noted but deliberately NOT fixed in this pass:** `nighthawk/session.ts` also defines its own `formatEtDate(d: Date)`, which independently reimplements the identical `Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", {timeZone: ET})` computation as a named (not raw inline) helper — functionally redundant with `todayEt(d)` from `et-date.ts` now that `todayEt` accepts an optional `Date` argument. This wasn't included here because it's an established, multi-consumer named export (not a raw inline duplicate), and removing/aliasing it is a slightly bigger refactor (auditing every `formatEtDate` call site) that deserves its own focused pass rather than scope-creeping into this fix.

**Blast radius:** exactly the 9 call sites listed above, across 8 files — no function signature or return type changed anywhere, so no downstream consumer needed updating.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean (confirms no naming collisions slipped through); full suite `1004/1004` passing (no new tests — every substitution is a byte-identical drop-in, matching the same class of change already covered by `et-date.ts`'s own test suite from the original consolidation). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — 9th `fmtPremium` reimplementation found, in the file that IS the grounding-guard reference implementation (follow-up audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/app/api/market/gex-heatmap/explain/route.ts:44` — a local `fmtMoney(n: number)` reimplementing the "compact signed dollar magnitude" formatter that task #75 (earlier today) already consolidated 8 other copies of into `src/lib/fmt-money.ts`'s `fmtPremium()`. This is the route that builds the Largo "desk read" narrative prompt context and then grounds the model's response against it via `checkNumbersGrounded` — i.e. the numbers this formatter renders are exactly what the model is told is true AND what its output gets checked against. A silently-diverging formatter here doesn't just risk a wrong number on screen; it risks the grounding check itself passing or failing against the wrong reference string.

**A real behavioral divergence, not just a style copy:** the local version always used `.toFixed(1)` in its thousands branch (e.g. `$15.0K`); the canonical `fmtPremium` uses `k < 10 ? k.toFixed(1) : k.toFixed(0)` (whole-K at $10K+, e.g. `$15K`) — confirmed by reading `fmt-money.ts`'s own comments, which explain this exact branch was itself a deliberate fix for an earlier bug (`GexDealerPanel.tsx:39` printing `$5000.0M` instead of `$5.0B` before the billions-first branch ordering was added). The local copy also had no null/NaN guard (`fmtPremium` returns `"—"` for `null`/non-finite input; the local one had no `null` case in its signature at all and would have silently rendered `"$0"` for a NaN via `Math.abs(NaN)` → `0` had one ever reached it).

**Fix:** deleted the local `fmtMoney`; both call sites (top flow strikes by net premium, dark-pool levels by notional) now call `fmtPremium` imported from `@/lib/fmt-money`.

**Blast radius:** 2 call sites, both within this route's own prompt-context builder — no other file imports this route's (now-deleted) local `fmtMoney`.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1004/1004` passing (no new tests — `fmtPremium` already has direct coverage in `fmt-money.test.ts` from task #75, and this route has no existing test file to extend). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — WS-fed `change_pct` served unrounded via `/api/market/quote` (follow-up audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/lib/ws/polygon-socket.ts` — both places `indexStore[sym].change_pct` is computed from a live WS message (the `A`/`AM` aggregate-bar handler, and the `V` tick-value handler) did raw floating-point division with no rounding: `((current - sessionOpen) / sessionOpen) * 100`. Every REST sibling in `src/lib/providers/polygon.ts` rounds the same computation via `Number((...).toFixed(2))` — this WS-fed path was the one place that didn't. `src/app/api/market/quote/route.ts` reads `indexStore` straight through into its JSON response with no `roundFloats()` pass, so the raw unrounded float reached the wire. This is the SPX/VIX header tape `GexHeatmap.tsx` polls every ~1.5s — previously masked only by the frontend's own `fmtPct()` display formatting, i.e. correct on screen but wrong in the actual API payload (the same "systemic: several endpoints serve unrounded floats" pattern this doc's CLAUDE.md note calls out).

**Fix:** extracted the shared computation into a new exported `computeSessionChangePct(current, sessionOpen)` in `polygon-socket.ts`, rounding via the same `Number((...).toFixed(2))` pattern as the REST sibling, and pointed both the `A`/`AM` and `V` handlers at it instead of each inlining (and, in the `V` handler's case, never rounding) the arithmetic separately.

**Blast radius:** both `indexStore` write sites in `polygon-socket.ts` — no consumer of `indexStore` or `/api/market/quote` needed a change, since the field's type/shape is unchanged (still a `number`), only its precision.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1008/1008` passing (4 new in `polygon-socket-change-pct.test.ts` — rounds a representative raw float to 2dp, returns 0 with no anchor, rounds a negative change correctly, and a general "never more than 2 decimal digits" property check). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — `unusual-whales.ts` had its own unenumerated ET-date duplicate, largest blast radius of any date-dup found (follow-up audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/providers/unusual-whales.ts:346` — a local `todayIso()` reimplementing the exact `Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", {timeZone:"America/New_York"})` logic that task #74 (earlier today, and originally on 2026-07-01/02) consolidated 6 other copies of into `src/lib/et-date.ts`'s `todayEt()` — but this copy was never found or enumerated, because it lives in the core UW provider file rather than in any of the play-engine/dashboard files the original sweep scanned. It has 6 call sites (`:373`, `:463`, `:821`, `:881`, `:924`, `:1495`) gating 0DTE expiry-date filtering and "today's" max-pain contract selection — the largest blast radius of any date-duplication instance found across either audit pass, since `unusual-whales.ts` is the shared REST client every 0DTE/GEX-by-strike/max-pain consumer platform-wide ultimately calls through.

**Why it's a real risk, not just style:** `et-date.ts`'s own header comment states the exact failure mode this class of duplication causes — a future one-off DST or timezone-boundary fix applied to only one copy silently shifts that copy's day-boundary out of sync with every other copy, corrupting cross-file date comparisons (e.g. "is this contract's expiry today" agreeing in one file but not another) without any error being thrown.

**Fix:** deleted the local `todayIso()` and its 6 call sites now call `todayEt()` imported from `@/lib/et-date`. Confirmed byte-identical output before changing anything: `new Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", {timeZone:"America/New_York", year:"numeric", month:"2-digit", day:"2-digit"})` (the local version's explicit options) and `new Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", {timeZone:"America/New_York"})` (`todayEt()`'s, no explicit y/m/d fields) both format to the same `YYYY-MM-DD` string — verified directly in a Node REPL against the current date rather than assumed from reading the two implementations.

**Blast radius:** single file, 6 call sites, all within `unusual-whales.ts` itself — no caller of any of these functions passes or receives a date string differently than before (the return shape/format is identical), so no downstream consumer needed a change.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1004/1004` passing (no new tests needed — the substitution is a proven byte-identical drop-in, and `todayEt()` itself already has direct coverage from task #74's consolidation). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## 🟢 FIXED 2026-07-04 — 5th WS-adjacent leader-lock manager (`rth-warm-leader.ts`) missed by the REPLICA_COUNT fail-open sweep (follow-up audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/rth-warm-leader.ts:47-56` (`tryAcquireLead`) — `if (!redis) return true; // single-replica / no Redis — run locally`. This is the exact fail-open-on-Redis-loss bug already fixed today in all four WS socket managers (`uw-socket.ts`/`polygon-socket.ts`/`options-socket.ts`/`stocks-socket.ts`, see the "Gate WS leader-lock fail-open" entry below), but `rth-warm-leader.ts` wasn't in that sweep's file list — it lives outside `src/lib/ws/` and isn't itself a WebSocket, so a `grep`-by-directory or by-name pass over "the WS sockets" walks right past it. It's booted from the same `ensureDataSockets()` entry point as the four already-fixed files (`src/lib/ws/init-data-sockets.ts`) and races the same Redis `SET NX EX` leader-election pattern.

**Impact:** on a Redis outage across the 5-replica production topology, every replica would simultaneously believe it holds the cluster lead and independently poll `cron_job_runs` + dispatch `nights-watch-warm`/`uw-cache-refresh`/`heatmap-warm` warmers every 60s. Bounded (the dispatch targets are curated idempotent-only per `cron-dispatch.ts`) so this isn't data-corrupting, but it's 5x redundant vendor-facing warm calls landing exactly when the WS layer is *also* degrading — the worst possible moment to add uncoordinated load, and the fix for the sibling bug specifically exists to prevent that compounding effect.

**Fix:** identical pattern to the four already-fixed sockets — reused `wsLeaderShouldFailOpenWithoutRedis()`/`alertWsLeaderFailClosedOnce()`/`clearWsLeaderFailClosedAlert()` from the shared `src/lib/ws/leader-lock-shared.ts` module added earlier today, rather than duplicating the REPLICA_COUNT-threshold logic a 5th time. `tryAcquireLead()` now fails open only when `REPLICA_COUNT<=1`; otherwise fails closed (with a one-time ops alert) on both the "no Redis client" and the "Redis errored" branches — the errored-branch behavior is slightly stricter than before (previously always failed closed on error regardless of replica count; now correctly fails open too at `REPLICA_COUNT<=1`, matching the sibling sockets).

**Blast radius:** searched the rest of the codebase for the same `SET ... NX` leader-election shape (`cf-purge-on-deploy.ts`, `membership-sync-limit.ts`, `webhook/whop/route.ts` also matched) — all three are deliberately-scoped, already-correct fail-open designs for a *different* problem class (idempotent one-shot cache purge, per-user rate-limit cooldown, webhook dedup) where fail-open means "occasionally redundant/duplicate work," not "N-way contention for a single exclusive upstream resource." None needed the same fix; `rth-warm-leader.ts` was the only other genuine cluster-leader-election lock in the codebase.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; existing `rth-warm-leader.test.ts` (covers `rthWriterOverdue`) and `leader-lock-shared.test.ts` (covers the fail-open/closed threshold itself) both pass unchanged — `tryAcquireLead` isn't exported for direct unit testing, matching the precedent set by the four sibling socket files fixed earlier today (none of them export their `tryAcquire*Lead` either; the shared threshold logic they all now call is what's actually under test). `npm run build` clean.
