## Night Hawk "tomorrow's plays" deep audit (2026-07-02)
Four parallel deep-dives (discovery, scoring, AI/edition assembly, lifecycle/grading) + live production checks. System is 4 editions old (Jun 29→Jul 2); the Jul-2 edition published recap-only (0 plays); analytics: 10 resolved, 60% target-hit / 50% profitable, A-conviction n=4 shows 75% wins but −0.55% avg return (small sample + target-hit≠profitable divergence).

**FIXED same-day (PR: fix/nighthawk-holiday-guard):**
- Morning-confirm had NO holiday guard — would fire Fri 2026-07-03 (July 4th observed), fall back via `fetchLatestNighthawkEdition()` to MONDAY's edition (published Thu evening), compute an "overnight gap" from a closed market, spuriously INVALIDATE Monday's plays + false-page ops, and leave the bogus verdicts in Redis all weekend. Now gated on `isTradingDayEt(todayEt())` + a session-match guard (only confirm an edition whose `edition_for` === today; the fetchLatest fallback can legitimately return a future edition). 3 holiday tests added to `session.test.ts` (2026-07-03 not a trading day; Thu→Mon skip).
- Recap-only CLOBBER — `publishRecapOnlyEdition` upserted `plays:[]` unconditionally, and the exception rescue runs on ANY post-context throw, including AFTER the full edition row was written (post-publish `syncNighthawkPlayOutcomes`/job-flip were un-caught inside the same try). A transient DB error seconds after publishing a 5-play edition — or a force rebuild collapsing on a one-off Claude timeout — overwrote the good playbook with an empty recap, unrecoverable without manual force. Now: clobber guard (recap never overwrites an existing plays>0 edition) + post-publish steps isolated with their own catch/ops-alert (job-flip failure → next fire resumes idempotently, strictly better than the rescue).

**Key open findings (severity-ordered; full detail in the audit conversation):**
- HIGH scoring: published conviction/score were Claude's SELF-GRADE — **FIXED 2026-07-02 (PR: fix/nh-publish-gates)**, see grounding entry: score pinned to the deterministic dossier score; conviction can only be downgraded from the deterministic mapping (by the model or the critic), never upgraded.
- HIGH scoring: several factors not direction-mirrored — **FIXED 2026-07-02 (PR: fix/nh-scorer-direction-correctness)**: news sentiment now computed on a bullish axis and signed by direction (insider buys included); buyback removed from the news regex (triple-count dedupe — catalyst + fundamentals keep their direction-aware scoring); institutional net-buying mirrored (+3 aligned / −2 contradicting); congress rows weighted by disclosed side (buys back longs, sells back shorts, unknown side ×0.5); dark-pool magnitude now full only when bias CONFIRMS, half when unknown, zero when contradicting (was inverted at both ends); strike stacks and OI-change only score when their option side aligns; presence-as-signal points (net_vex/max_pain/oi-count) removed; SHORT tech branch fixed (gap-UP tag keyword collision removed, bearish-MA-stack +4 added, fresh-highs −6 penalty added). Also wired the DEAD earnings-proximity −6 and analyst-PT nudge into the edition path (session-aware rescore before ranking) and the PT input into the hunt path. 16 regression tests (`scorer-direction.test.ts`).
- HIGH discovery: HELIX Postgres bonus — **FIXED 2026-07-02 (PR: fix/nh-discovery-quality)**: now a CONFIRMATION signal, not a second full read of the same tape — direction-gated (a contradicting live tape applies a small penalty instead of a bonus), capped at +8 (score/4), and scaled by the candidate's own regime multiplier instead of bypassing it.
- HIGH discovery: no data-completeness gate — 12-call hunt budget exhaustion silently strips dark-pool/OI/skew/congress enrichment; plays publish at full conviction with no "data incomplete" flag; starvation biases against the unusual-flow names the product exists to surface.
- HIGH grounding: entry/target/stop levels unverified — **FIXED 2026-07-02 (PR: fix/nh-publish-gates)**: new deterministic `validatePlayGeometry()` gate at publish (uses the SAME `parsePlayLevels` parser the outcome grader uses): unparseable target/stop → DROP; corrupt entry band (non-positive bound or width >20% of mid — the exact #207 class) → DROP at publish, not just nulled retrospectively; LONG/SHORT target+stop must sit on the correct sides of the entry mid → DROP otherwise; prose-only entries kept but flagged. Same PR: member-visible `score` PINNED to the deterministic dossier score (model self-grade no longer overrides), `conviction` capped at the deterministic score→letter mapping (model may only grade DOWN), model-vs-flow direction divergence logged, and a sector-concentration cap (max 2 per sector, unknown sector exempt, applied before the overshoot slice so other sectors backfill). 12 regression tests (`play-geometry.test.ts`).
- HIGH confirm: missing-data-→-CONFIRMED and index-only gap check — **FIXED 2026-07-02 (PR: fix/nh-morning-confirm-robustness)**: verdict engine extracted to `morning-confirm-verdict.ts` (testable); per-play evaluated-check counting → zero evaluable data now returns a new neutral **UNVERIFIED** state (grey badge, "verdict withheld", counted separately in the summary — never a green CONFIRMED built on nothing); a GLOBAL abstain skips the whole run (no Redis write) when every source is unreachable; each play's OWN pre-market price (one batched Polygon snapshot call) is now checked against its published levels — gapped through stop → INVALIDATED, at/through target → DEGRADED (reward consumed), gapped past the entry band → DEGRADED do-not-chase. Also fixed the pre-open prior-close off-by-one (`at(-2)` assumed a today-bar exists before the open — the "overnight gap" absorbed an extra full session and could false-trip the 20-pt INVALIDATE); now selects the last bar dated strictly before today in ET. 9 regression tests.
- MEDIUM grading: entry-range reachability — **FIXED 2026-07-02 (PR: fix/nh-grading-observability)**: new `unfilled` outcome (with CHECK-constraint migration) when the session never traded back into the entry band (long: low stayed above the band top; short mirrored) — no phantom wins/losses from unfillable entries; excluded from all win-rate denominators like `stop_data_unavailable` (analytics `unfilled_count`, track-record `isNighthawkOutcomeScoreable`, PlayHistoryTable "UNF" badge); morning-confirm prior-close off-by-one FIXED (see confirm entry above); scorer's earnings-proximity −6 and analyst-PT nudge were dead code in the edition path (FIXED, see scoring entry above); buyback triple-count (FIXED, same PR); mono-source discovery PARTIALLY FIXED (top-net-impact now seeds candidates at 0.75 weight, fix/nh-discovery-quality; OI-change still unused); sector-concentration cap ADDED (fix/nh-publish-gates); flow "streak" now requires consecutive TRADING days (holiday/weekend-aware, fix/nh-discovery-quality); sub-$2/warrant/unit/leveraged-ETP filter ADDED (same PR); play-critic fails open at every step (advisory, not binding); Hawk-Intel explainer prose has zero post-generation grounding; no as-of timestamps in Claude prompts; zero-candidate recap-only vs UW outage — FIXED (same PR): market-wide records `flow_fetch_failed` when the flow-alerts pull errors; zero candidates + failed fetch now alerts ops as ANOMALOUS instead of passing as a quiet tape. Also fixed: the member play-status "not yet run" lie on no-play editions (morning-confirm now writes an honest empty blob), and chain tables in Claude prompts carry an as-of timestamp + "after-hours last prints" label.
- SOLID: holiday-aware session targeting; DST-safe cron schedules (all 3); checkpointed/idempotent build state machine; correct long/short grading signs incl. whipsaw disambiguation; hard strike/premium/OI grounding with live-mark overwrite; PT reconciliation; honest failure degradation (no path fabricates plays); the LLM critic's actual output quality (live notes caught a bad analyst PT, an S/R mix-up, and cut a play on contradicting flow).

Every page/subpage/panel/button/layout/font; every number/level/matrix/flow value validated vs ground truth; SPX Slayer levels+logic; heatmaps for **multiple stocks** (not just SPX/SPY); Night Hawk play-logic strength; Night's Watch UI; **all** REST **and** WebSocket endpoints on **UW, Polygon, Benzinga**; site-wide UX improvements.

## NightHawk skew sign-flip bug FIXED 2026-07-04 (task #125) — LIVE scoring path, not shadow mode

**Status:** FIXED (`fix/nighthawk-skew-sign-flip`). Direct follow-up to the finding surfaced during `feat/spx-shadow-skew-vol` (SPX Slayer shadow-mode risk-reversal-skew factor, see the entry above this one) — that PR's own module doc (`src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-skew.ts`) flagged this exact NightHawk sign flip as out-of-scope for a shadow-only PR ("out of scope to change in this PR ... worth a dedicated `fix/nighthawk-skew-sign` investigation+fix") and this FINDINGS.md's own prior entry logged it for follow-up. This is that fix.

**Severity:** HIGH. Unlike the SPX Slayer shadow-mode skew factor immediately above (provably inert — `git diff main -- src/lib/spx-signals.ts` is empty, the shadow factor writes to a separate observations table that is never read back into a real score), this bug lives in `src/lib/nighthawk/scorer.ts`, on `scoreCandidate`'s LIVE ticker-candidate scoring path — the one that runs today and feeds published NightHawk plays. This fix therefore CHANGES live scoring output going forward; see "Risk carried by this fix" below.

**Root cause:** `scorer.ts` had TWO independent sites hardcoding the wrong sign for UW's `risk_reversal` field (surfaced as `dossierExtras.risk_reversal_skew` via `vol-metrics.ts::parseLatestRiskReversalSkew`, sourced from `fetchUwRiskReversalSkew` in `dossier.ts`):
1. `scoreSkewConfirmation` (pre-fix, was scorer.ts:700-708): doc comment read "Positive RR skew (calls bid over puts) = bullish; negative = bearish" and the body computed `const skewDir = skew > 0 ? "long" : "short"`.
2. `scoreFlowQuality`'s direction-flip branch (pre-fix, was scorer.ts:397-410 — the logic that overrides the flow-implied LONG/SHORT direction when call/put premium is nearly tied and skew magnitude is large): the identical `const skewDir = skew > 0 ? "long" : "short"`, which can flip a candidate's overall direction outright, not just nudge its score.

**Evidence (live UW data, re-verified from the shadow-mode PR's investigation):** `GET /api/stock/SPY/historical-risk-reversal-skew` on 2026-07-04 returned 29 daily 25-delta rows spanning 2026-05-21..2026-07-02, EVERY ONE positive (+0.0067 to +0.0663), e.g. `{"date":"2026-07-02","ticker":"SPY","delta":25,"risk_reversal":"0.0663361729210146"}`. A "call IV minus put IV" definition would be predominantly NEGATIVE for an equity index — the persistent put-side "volatility smirk" is one of the most robust stylized facts in index options, so a multi-week run of all-positive values under that definition would be the anomaly, not the norm. This confirms UW's `risk_reversal` here is effectively (put IV − call IV): positive = puts bid over calls = fear/bearish; negative = calls bid over puts = bullish. This matches `src/lib/nighthawk/vol-metrics.ts`'s OWN docstring on the same field (line 31: "positive puts bid over calls (fear)") and `src/lib/spx-signals-shadow-skew.ts::computeSkewShadowFactor` (the shadow-mode factor, which already had this sign right, `skew > 0 ? "bearish" : "bullish"`) — `scorer.ts` was the one outlier with the sign backwards.

**Why it wasn't caught earlier:** `risk_reversal_skew` is a relatively recent dossier field with no dedicated sign test — the 2026-07-02 "Night Hawk direction-correctness regression suite" (`scorer-direction.test.ts`, see the "Night Hawk 'tomorrow's plays' deep audit" entry above) covered news sentiment, smart money, options positioning, and technicals, but the skew scorer functions predate and were outside that sweep's scope. No live-data cross-check against UW existed until the SPX Slayer shadow-skew investigation pulled real rows and noticed the all-positive pattern was inconsistent with a "calls minus puts" reading.

**Blast radius — every call site checked, both bugs fixed:**
- `src/lib/nighthawk/scorer.ts::scoreSkewConfirmation` (called from `scoreCandidate`, feeds the `skewAdj` term added to every candidate's score) — sign corrected; docstring rewritten with the live evidence above plus a pre-fix-history note so the reasoning survives a skim.
- `src/lib/nighthawk/scorer.ts::scoreFlowQuality`'s direction-flip branch (called from `scoreCandidate` via the `riskReversalSkew` option; also called independently and skew-less from `hunt-builder.ts`'s HELIX-tape reconciliation, `scoreFlowQuality(mapped)` — that second call site never passes `riskReversalSkew`, so it was never hitting this branch, but shares the same function body, so the fix covers it too if that call site is ever extended) — sign corrected.
- Reviewed and confirmed NOT affected (no hardcoded sign assumption to flip): `src/lib/nighthawk/format.ts::formatTickerDossierText` (line 364-365) prints the raw signed `risk_reversal_skew` value with no bullish/bearish label attached — neutral text, nothing to invert. `src/lib/nighthawk/play-critic.ts` (line 17) only instructs the Claude critic model, in its system prompt, to check "no contradiction with risk reversal skew" — the sign interpretation is left to the model reading that same neutral `format.ts` line, not hardcoded in this codebase's logic. `src/lib/nighthawk/dossier.ts` and `hunt-builder.ts` only parse/pass the value through, no sign comparison. Confirmed exhaustively via `grep -rn "risk_reversal\|riskReversal\|skewDir" src` — no other hardcoded sign comparison exists outside the two sites fixed here.

**Fix:** flipped the ternary at both sites from `skew > 0 ? "long" : "short"` to `skew > 0 ? "short" : "long"`, matching `vol-metrics.ts`'s docstring and the shadow-mode factor's already-correct convention. Deliberately did NOT touch either function's magnitude/threshold constants (`scoreSkewConfirmation`'s +3/−2 asymmetry; `scoreFlowQuality`'s 0.12/0.25 flow-margin and 0.3/1.0 skew-magnitude flip thresholds) — recalibrating those is a separate, evidence-driven question (this codebase's own precedent: `bie/calibration.ts`'s `MIN_EVIDENCE = 10` gate) orthogonal to a pure sign-correctness fix, and left untouched.

**Risk carried by this fix (called out explicitly, per the task instruction):** unlike the SPX Slayer shadow-mode skew factor above — provably inert, written only to an observations table, never read back into a real score — this fix changes NightHawk's LIVE scoring output starting with the next hunt/scoring cycle after merge. Any ticker candidate where the previously-inverted skew sign was the deciding factor in its score or its LONG/SHORT direction will score differently going forward. This is the intended correction (the old behavior was actively mis-scoring against what the options market was pricing), but it ships with no shadow/observation period first — recommend a human spot-check of the next few NightHawk editions' skew-influenced candidates (specifically ones where `directionFlippedBySkew: true`, or where `risk_reversal_skew` was large) for sanity after this merges.

**Fix location:** `src/lib/nighthawk/scorer.ts` — `scoreFlowQuality`'s skew branch (line 406) and `scoreSkewConfirmation` (line 736, after the docstring rewrite).

**Tests added:** `src/lib/nighthawk/scorer-direction.test.ts` (5 new cases appended to the existing 2026-07-02 direction-correctness suite): `scoreSkewConfirmation` with the live +0.0663 SPY value (short=+3/long=−2, was the reverse pre-fix) and a bullish −0.04 value (long=+3/short=−2), plus null/undefined/0/NaN neutrality; `scoreFlowQuality`'s direction-flip with a tied call/put flow + strong positive skew (now flips LONG→SHORT) and a put-leaning flow + strong negative skew (now flips SHORT→LONG). Verified all 4 non-neutral cases FAIL against the pre-fix code (ran the new tests with only `scorer.ts` stashed back to its pre-fix state — 4/5 failed as expected) before confirming all 5 pass post-fix.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite 1192/1192 passing (5 new). `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand` / `lint:vendor` clean.

---

## SPX Slayer <-> BIE/Largo data-sharing correctness validator (task #124, 2026-07-04)

**Status:** DONE — validator built and passing (`feat/spx-bie-correctness-validator`). Two structural observations LOGGED below (both WARN-severity, not FAIL) as a direct byproduct of tracing the data-sharing chain end-to-end; neither is fixed in this PR — this PR's charter (per its own task brief) is read-only/additive validation, not remediation, so both are left for a dedicated `fix/<slug>` follow-up per the standing issue-handling policy.

**Connects to:** the user's standing instruction — "SPX slayer should be always sharing its entire data, values, entire numericals to both BIE and largo and there should be a validation also to check if all the data is 100% correct." PR #471 (`feat/ecosystem-context-spx-full-fidelity`, merged to `main` as of this task) added `EcosystemContext.spx_full_state` and claimed, in its own module doc, that it and Largo's `get_spx_play` tool share "one derivation, not two." This task builds the validation half of that instruction: prove the claim is actually true, keep proving it on every future change, and catch any real drift between what a member sees, what BIE sees, and what Largo sees.

**Chain traced and CONFIRMED TRUE:** `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts:289-291` (`fetchSpxFullState()`) returns `src/lib/platform/spx-service.ts:74-84`'s `getSpxPlayState()` **verbatim** (`return getSpxPlayState();` — no field reconstruction). `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts:873-875` (`case "get_spx_play"`) calls `marketPlatform.spx.getSpxPlayState()`, and `src/lib/platform/index.ts:6,13` (`marketPlatform.spx = import * as spx from "./spx-service"`) proves that resolves to the literal same module ecosystem-context.ts imports from — not a re-export or wrapper. `getSpxPlayState()` itself is `loadMergedSpxDesk() -> buildPlayTechnicals() -> readSpxPlaySnapshot()`, and `readSpxPlaySnapshot()` (`src/lib/spx-evaluator.ts:55-60`) hardcodes `evaluateSpxPlay(desk, technicals, { mutate: false })` with no caller-overridable option — BIE and Largo reads can never accidentally trigger a live write/Discord side effect. So: BIE's `spx_full_state` and Largo's `get_spx_play` genuinely call the exact same function object at runtime. All 4 of these claims are now mechanically re-verified on every run by `scripts/audit/spx-bie-consistency-validator.mjs`'s Layer A (static source-invariant checks), not just asserted once by reading the code.

**Two structural observations found while tracing the chain (both WARN, logged not fixed):**
1. **The member dashboard's own endpoint doesn't call `getSpxPlayState()` at all.** `src/app/api/market/spx/play/route.ts:20-28` independently calls the exact same 3-function chain (`loadMergedSpxDesk -> buildPlayTechnicals -> readSpxPlaySnapshot`) inline, rather than delegating to `getSpxPlayState()`. So there are really **three** call sites of one chain (route.ts inline, `spx-service.ts`'s wrapper used by both BIE and Largo), not the "one derivation" PR #471's doc describes — that claim is true for BIE-vs-Largo specifically, but not for member-vs-(BIE/Largo). Harmless *today*: `loadMergedSpxDesk()` is a single shared cache lane (`src/lib/spx-desk-loader.ts`'s own doc explicitly warns against ever introducing a second cache key for this exact reason — a prior incident, 2026-07-01, had the member dashboard and the trade-alert panel disagree on trade direction from a duplicated cache key), so both copies of the chain see identical inputs within the cache TTL and therefore produce identical output. But nothing *guarantees* the two copies of the chain stay byte-for-byte identical if either is edited alone in the future — no existing test compares route.ts's output to `getSpxPlayState()`'s output. **Recommended fix (not applied here):** have route.ts call `getSpxPlayState()` (plus its own `roundFloats()`, see #2) instead of re-implementing the chain, eliminating the duplication and the drift risk entirely. Left to a follow-up `fix/<slug>` PR since this task's charter is validation-only.
2. **`roundFloats()` asymmetry.** route.ts rounds its response to 2 decimal places (`roundFloats(play)`, `src/lib/round-floats.ts`) before replying to the member dashboard; `getSpxPlayState()` — BIE's `spx_full_state`, Largo's `get_spx_play` — does not. So a member can see e.g. `7499.36` for a number where BIE/Largo see `7499.360000000001` for the *same underlying value* — not a wrong answer, but not byte-for-byte identical either, which is the standard the task's own brief set ("assert... MATCH exactly, or within a documented tolerance ONLY if truly unavoidable float rounding is involved — flag any such tolerance explicitly, don't hide it"). This is the same systemic float-noise pattern already logged elsewhere in this doc ("Systemic: several endpoints serve unrounded floats... round at the data layer," CLAUDE.md), newly confirmed to also apply to the BIE/Largo internal-consumer boundary, not just member-facing HTTP endpoints. **Tolerance applied, not hidden:** the live validator's Layer B diff uses `ROUND_TOLERANCE = 0.5 * 10^-2 = 0.005` (half a rounding step at `roundFloats`'s default 2dp) — any numeric divergence *larger* than that is flagged as a real FAIL, not absorbed silently. **Recommended fix (not applied here):** same as #1 — once route.ts calls `getSpxPlayState()` + its own `roundFloats()`, BIE/Largo would need `roundFloats()` applied at their own boundary too (in `fetchSpxFullState()` or inside `getSpxPlayState()` itself) to close this gap for real; left to the same follow-up.

**What the validator checks:**
- **Layer 1 (unit, `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.test.ts` + new `src/lib/bie/spx-full-state-fixture.ts`):** tightened the existing PR #471 pass-through tests from `assert.ok(fullStateCalls > 0)` to `assert.equal(fullStateCalls, 1)` (and the pre-existing `openPlayCalls` check likewise) — proves `getSpxPlayState()` runs *exactly* once per `fetchEcosystemContext()` call, not merely "at least once." More importantly: **the test's fixture is now typed as the real `SpxPlayPayload`** (`src/lib/spx-play-payload.ts`), moved into its own plain `.ts` file rather than living inside the `.test.ts` file. This matters because of a real gap found while implementing this: **`tsconfig.json` excludes `**/*.test.ts` from `npx tsc --noEmit`** — a `SpxPlayPayload`-typed fixture declared directly inside `ecosystem-context.test.ts` would compile-check *nothing*, since `tsx` (esbuild) strips types without validating them and the project's type-check command never looks at test files at all. Verified this empirically: an invalid literal (`verdict: "CONFIRM"`, not a member of `ClaudePlayVerdict`'s `"APPROVE_BUY" | "VETO"` union) inside the old in-test fixture passed `tsc --noEmit` silently; the same literal inside the new `spx-full-state-fixture.ts` correctly fails compilation (`TS2322: Type '"CONFIRM"' is not assignable to type '"APPROVE_BUY" | "VETO"'`). This is a **general, previously-undocumented gap in this repo's CI posture** worth flagging on its own: any `.test.ts` file's type annotations — however earnest-looking — provide zero real protection under this project's current `tsc --noEmit`/`npm test` setup. Filed here rather than as its own entry since it was discovered as a direct byproduct of this task, not a separate audit pass.
- **Layer 2 (`scripts/audit/spx-bie-consistency-validator.mjs`, new sibling to `data-validator.mjs`):**
  - Layer A (static, always runs, zero network/cost): the 4 source-invariant checks described above, using a proper brace-depth block extractor (a first draft used a naive `[^}]*` regex that silently mis-extracted every function body containing a nested `{...}` literal — e.g. `{ mutate: false }` — caught and fixed during this task's own manual verification before it shipped a false FAIL).
  - Layer B (live): fetches the member endpoint `GET /api/market/spx/play` (via `CRON_SECRET` bearer — `authorizeCronOrTierApi`'s cron branch — no temp Clerk user needed for this one), and in the SAME process calls the REAL `getSpxPlayState()` directly (dynamic `tsx` import of `spx-service.ts`, with the same `mock.module("server-only", ...)` stub the test suite already uses — verified this works outside `node --test` too, not just under it). Diffs every leaf field: non-numeric leaves exactly, numeric leaves within `ROUND_TOLERANCE`.
  - Layer C (opt-in, off by default via `AUDIT_INCLUDE_LARGO_LIVE_CHECK=1`): a Largo liveness smoke check (`tools_used` includes `get_spx_play`/`get_ecosystem_context`) — NOT a byte-for-byte diff, see below.
- New `scripts/audit/lib/prod-clerk-session.mjs`: a `fetch`-based port of `data-validator.mjs`'s Clerk temp-user sign-in flow, factored out so Layer C (and any future script) can reuse it without modifying `data-validator.mjs` itself (purely additive — that file is untouched by this PR).

**What the validator CANNOT verify live in this sandbox (documented plainly, not swept under the rug):**
- **No HTTP endpoint anywhere returns BIE's raw `fetchEcosystemContext()`/`spx_full_state` or Largo's raw `get_spx_play` tool result.** Both are internal server functions. The only HTTP path to Largo's tool output is the full AI conversation loop (`/api/market/largo/query`), which (confirmed by reading `runLargoQuery`'s return type in `src/lib/largo-terminal.ts`) returns only `{answer, tools_used, verification, ...}` — **never the captured raw tool-call JSON** — plus it costs real Anthropic spend and is non-deterministic about whether/how it surfaces exact numbers in prose. Layer B works around this by calling `getSpxPlayState()` directly in-process instead of over HTTP (arguably a *stronger* ground truth than a hypothetical debug endpoint would be, since it's the literal function object, not a re-implementation) — but this means Layer B needs live DB/Redis/Polygon/UW network egress, which this sandbox does not have (confirmed: direct Postgres TCP blocked per this doc's existing sandbox-limitations notes; `POLYGON_API_BASE` also resolves to a literal unresolved placeholder string here, not a real URL, per CLAUDE.md's documented `${{shared.*}}` gotcha). Ran it live in this sandbox anyway to prove the mechanism: Layer A's 6 checks all reported correctly (4 PASS + 2 WARN, matching the two logged findings above); Layer B's **member-endpoint half succeeded against real production** (`GET /api/market/spx/play` → `phase=SCANNING action=SCANNING grade=D`, live, via `CRON_SECRET`); Layer B's **direct in-process `getSpxPlayState()` half SKIPPED with the exact reason** (`POLYGON_API_BASE` env placeholder), not a hang or a silent pass — confirming both that the mechanism works end-to-end up to the network boundary, and that it fails loudly/informatively rather than quietly when that boundary isn't available. Exit code 0 (no FAIL) for this sandbox run, as expected with nothing but SKIPs/WARNs.
- **Layer C (Largo liveness) was not run live in this session** — deliberately, to avoid spending Anthropic budget and Clerk FAPI sign-in cycles on a smoke check whose logic was already verified by code review; it is off by default (`AUDIT_INCLUDE_LARGO_LIVE_CHECK=1` required) for the same reason in normal operation.

**Tests added/changed:** `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.test.ts` (fixture moved to typed `spx-full-state-fixture.ts`; call-count assertions tightened to exact-once) — all 11 tests pass (`node --import tsx --experimental-test-module-mocks --test src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.test.ts`). New `src/lib/bie/spx-full-state-fixture.ts` (not a test file — the actual regression net, see Layer 1 above).

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean (including the new fixture file — confirmed it actually fails when sabotaged, see Layer 1 above). Full `npm test` clean. `npm run build` clean. `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.
